Passing a decimal-scale return like 0.0865 would land in the "<2" band giving score 5, completely misrepresenting performance. Auth-11 runner multiplies per-regime cumulative return by 100 before populating RegimeTestInput fields. Lesson: when invoking a gate from a runner, check whether the gate's input fields are documented as percent or decimal. The two gates in this codebase have DIFFERENT conventions — anti_overfit uses decimal, regime_score uses percent. Don't assume consistency; check.

- 2026-05-14/15 Auth-11 lesson — gates are read-only when invoked by runners — Both Auth-10 and Auth-11 invoked production gate functions (evaluate_anti_overfit, evaluate_regime_score) directly via imports, but with strict NO-MODIFICATION rules. The pattern that worked: (1) runner imports the gate's public API (`from strategy_lab.X import evaluate_Y`); (2) runner constructs the input dataclass with honestly-derived values; (3) runner calls the gate function; (4) gate writes its standard artifact JSON; (5) runner verifies the artifact and records the verdict; (6) runner does NOT modify the gate module source. Lesson: this is the right pattern for any "invoke a production gate from a research runner" need — use the gate's public API, never the internals. The gate's source byte-identity is verifiable post-run (sha sanity check). The gate's thresholds remain authoritative.

- 2026-05-14/15 Auth-11 lesson — Auth-10 verdicts are frozen historical records — When Auth-10 ran, it wrote anti_overfit verdicts with regime_count_tested = 0 (honest default — Auth-11 hadn't yet generated regime evidence). Auth-11 generates regime_score evidence showing regime_count_tested = 6 for all 5 strategies. Question: should Auth-10's anti_overfit verdicts be RE-RUN to update regime_count_tested from 0 to 6? Decision: NO. Auth-10 verdicts are FROZEN as historical records. They reflect the evidence state AT THE TIME they were written. The audit at Auth-12 will compute FRESH verdicts from raw inputs (Auth-9 v2 records + Auth-10 anti_overfit + Auth-11 regime_score) without depending on Auth-10's historical verdicts. Lesson: anti_overfit/regime_score verdicts in this codebase are time-of-write snapshots, NOT live computations. The audit is responsible for fresh aggregation. Document this clearly so future readers don't expect retroactive updates.

- 2026-05-14/15 Auth-11 lesson — regime-uniform vs walk-forward-stable are different properties — rsi_mean_reversion shows that a strategy can have regime-uniform profitability (all 6 regimes positive) AND poor walk-forward stability (WF rate 0.44, MaxDD 42.28%). These are not the same thing. Regime-uniform = "averages out positive in every regime bucket"; walk-forward-stable = "consistently profitable in sequential time slices". A strategy can be one without being the other. RSI captures small profits at local lows everywhere (regime-uniform) but holds during bear moves that hit deep drawdown in 2022 (walk-forward unstable). Lesson: when designing strategies (future Batch #004 work), aim for BOTH properties: regime-uniform AND walk-forward-stable. Achieving one without the other is partial. Volatility-targeting achieves walk-forward partial (best WF rate at 0.58, lowest MaxDD); RSI achieves regime-uniform fully. A combination — vol-scaled RSI mean-reversion — might achieve both. This is a hypothesis worth testing in any future strategy iteration.

- 2026-05-14/15 Auth-10 lesson — strategy-level aggregate is the breadth-correct shape — Re-confirmed from Auth-6: anti_overfit_gate's `symbol_count_tested ≥ 3` is a STRATEGY-level threshold, not a per-experiment threshold. Per-experiment shape (45 verdicts, each with `symbol_count_tested=1`) misuses the gate; strategy-level aggregate shape (5 verdicts, each aggregating across 9 cells with `symbol_count_tested=3`) is correct. Lesson re-validated: when a downstream gate has "breadth" thresholds, encode the aggregation at the breadth-appropriate level + use a `<name>_aggregate_v1` candidate_id pattern to distinguish from per-experiment records. The aggregation formulas matter too: max (worst-case) for max_drawdown, mean for out_of_sample_return, sum for trades_count, count-over-total for walk_forward_pass_rate. Document them explicitly in the manifest so the audit can re-derive.

- 2026-05-14/15 Auth-10 lesson — anti_overfit scoring is a useful continuous signal even when all candidates fail — All 5 batch #003 strategies got `passed=False, risk_level=HIGH`. The verdicts look identical at first glance. BUT the score field (0-100) gives a continuous diagnostic: 0/9/9/33/59 — those are NOT the same. volatility_targeting's 59 vs atr_compression_expansion's 0 is a 59-point spread reflecting real strategy-quality differences. The 59 sits at the LOW/MEDIUM band boundary; if WF cleared (1 more positive quarter), the score jumps ~25+ to clear the 80-100 LOW band. Lesson: when surfacing anti_overfit verdicts in dashboards or reports, ALWAYS show the score alongside passed/risk_level. Score reveals near-pass candidates that the binary passed flag hides. This is especially important when multi-strategy comparison is the goal.

- 2026-05-14/15 Auth-10 lesson — inverse-vol position sizing is what protects against bear-year tail risk — Batch #003 cross-sectional pattern is unmistakable: the 4 binary-position strategies (atr_compression_expansion, regime_filter_overlay, momentum_breakout, rsi_mean_reversion) ALL hit max_drawdown > 35% somewhere in their 9-cell sample (ranging 42-71%). volatility_targeting's worst MaxDD is 21.16% — the ONLY strategy clearing the threshold. The mechanism is its inverse-vol position-sizing-with-1.5x-leverage-cap: when daily volatility spikes (which happens during bear-year drawdowns), the strategy automatically reduces position size, capping the loss. Lesson: for any future strategy added to this codebase, position sizing is the dominant risk-control lever. Binary positions (long 100% or flat) cannot meet a 35% MaxDD bar across diverse OOS regimes. Future strategies that aim to pass anti_overfit MUST either (a) include vol-scaled sizing, (b) include a stop-loss / time-stop overlay, or (c) include a max-loss-per-trade cap. This is now a design principle for the codebase, not just an observation.

- 2026-05-14/15 Auth-10 lesson — the gate-staging chain is doing its job — Looking at Auth-6 vs Auth-10 outcomes side-by-side: Auth-6 had 19 evidence-coverage failures + 0 quality failures (verdict: "evidence is too narrow"). Auth-10 has 5 coverage failures (all Auth-11-fixable) + 14 quality failures (verdict: "the strategies as built don't meet the quality bar at broad scope"). This is exactly what the multi-stage gate chain was designed to produce: evidence first, judgment second. We could now sign Checkpoint A with a verdict that means something — and that verdict would be HONEST FAIL on quality grounds, not misleading FAIL on coverage grounds. Lesson: the chain pattern (Auth-1 sourcing → Auth-2 strategies → Auth-3 data → Auth-4 tests → Auth-5 narrow execution → Auth-6 narrow anti_overfit → pause/plan → Auth-7 broader data → Auth-8 broader windows → Auth-9 broader execution → Auth-10 strategy-level aggregate → Auth-11 regime → audit code → Auth-12 audit → Checkpoint A) takes 12+ gates to get to a verdict but the verdict at the end MEANS something. This is the right trade-off for high-stakes research. Apply this pattern to any future audit-style evaluation.

- 2026-05-14/15 Auth-9 lesson — CSV float-precision compounding can break tight tolerances — backtest_wrapper.write_bar_returns_csv uses `:.10f` formatting, so each bar's return has per-bar truncation up to 5e-11. Over N bars of cumulative product, the accumulated relative error can reach N×5e-11 (~2e-8 for 364 bars). The runner's P8 cumulative-matching check at rel_tol=1e-9 was tighter than this physical precision floor — Batch #003 hit it at cell 14 even though Batch #002 (5 cells × 365 bars) passed by luck. Lesson: when comparing CSV-roundtrip values, use rel_tol ≥ 1e-7 (or compute the theoretical precision floor from format spec × bar count). Better: also write a separate per-bar-difference check that's tight (rel_tol=1e-10 per bar) — catches single-bar corruption without false-positives from compounded rounding. Codified in v2_batch_003_runner.py with rel_tol=1e-6 + abs_tol=1e-9 (matching v2_batch_002_runner.py).

- 2026-05-14/15 Auth-9 lesson — abort-policy rehearsals are valuable as incidental tests — The false-start at cell 14 was an unintended dress rehearsal of the abort/rollback machinery: (1) per-cell rollback correctly deleted the failed cell's envelope + CSV + restored candidates.json + packs.json; (2) batch abort correctly halted further cells; (3) manual full-batch rollback (using auth9_pre.json's base64-encoded bytes) cleanly restored to pre-batch state, verified by sha-compare. None of this was "tested" before — it just worked. Lesson: every multi-stage gate chain should have a forced-failure test path before any real execution, OR (as here) accept that the first real execution will be the integration test of the rollback machinery — but ONLY if pre-snapshots include byte-content (not just shas) so manual restoration is possible. base64-encoded bytes in the pre-snapshot were what saved the day.

- 2026-05-14/15 Auth-9 lesson — multi-year multi-symbol surfaces what single-year hides — Batch #002 (BTC 2024 only) showed 5/5 strategies positive (+7% to +79%). Batch #003 (3 symbols × 3 years) shows 4/5 strategies have LOWER mean return, atr_compression_expansion flips from +8.65% to -9.69%, 4/5 strategies exceed 35% MaxDD somewhere, and 5/5 fail the 60% walk-forward threshold. The 2024 results were not edge — they were long-bias plus bull year. Without 2022 (bear) in the OOS set, this would be invisible. Lesson: for any future strategy evaluation in this codebase, multi-year OOS spanning at least one bear regime is non-negotiable. Any "audit window lock" for crypto strategies must include at least one bear year + one bull year + one sideways year, OR be marked CONDITIONAL by construction. Codified now: this is the standard going forward.

- 2026-05-14/15 Auth-9 lesson — walk-forward pass rate is the better stability signal than mean return — momentum_breakout has the 2nd-highest mean return (+40.82%) but a 47% walk-forward pass rate (mediocre). regime_filter_overlay has the highest mean (+50.87%) but a 36% WF pass rate (worst in batch). volatility_targeting has a modest mean (+8.79%) but a 58% WF pass rate (best). The high-mean strategies are dominated by outliers (e.g., momentum_breakout SOL 2023 +324.81%, regime_filter_overlay SOL 2023 +220.74%); pull those out and the mean drops dramatically. Walk-forward pass rate counts QUARTERS not RETURN MAGNITUDE — it's a stability test, not a profitability test. Lesson: when ranking strategies in this codebase, prioritize WF pass rate + MaxDD discipline over mean return. They tell you whether the strategy is BROADLY good or just had a few good quarters. The Checkpoint A audit's metric set already reflects this (8 metrics with WF + MaxDD weighted alongside return), which is the right design.

- 2026-05-14/15 Auth-9 lesson — same-input determinism produces cross-batch sha collisions (correctly) — batch_003_atr_compression_expansion_BTCUSD_2024_v1 has the EXACT same oos_bar_returns_sha256 as batch_002_atr_compression_expansion_v1, because the same strategy ran on the same OHLC slice (BTC 2024-01-01 to 2024-12-30) with the same config. The G16 (45 distinct shas WITHIN Batch #003) check still passes — the cross-batch collision is desirable (it's how the audit confirms reproducibility). Lesson: when designing distinctness checks for a new batch, scope them to the new batch's cells; cross-batch collisions on identical inputs are a reproducibility WIN, not a failure. Document this convention explicitly so a future review doesn't misread the collision as a bug.

- 2026-05-14 Auth-8 lesson — verify warmup against the MOST DEMANDING strategy, not the average — When locking OOS windows for a batch that runs multiple strategies, the warmup-feasibility check must use the most demanding strategy's warmup_required, NOT the average or the median. In Batch #003: regime_filter_overlay's sma_period=200 dominates; the other 4 strategies have warmups of 74, 20, 15, 31 bars. If you checked only the average (~68 bars), Window 1 (365 prior bars) would look like it has 5× headroom — but regime_filter_overlay would actually have only 1.8× headroom (165 bars of margin). Lesson: in any pre-flight feasibility check involving multiple consumers, find the strictest constraint and verify against it explicitly. Document the per-consumer warmup table alongside the aggregate result so reviewers can confirm. Don't hide the strictest constraint behind aggregation.

- 2026-05-14 Auth-8 lesson — cross-symbol consistent OOS bar counts are an invariant, not a coincidence — Window 1's OOS bar count is 364 across BTC, ETH, and SOL — and that's because all 3 CSVs share bit-for-bit identical date sequences (verified at Auth-7). If a future batch adds a symbol whose CSV has a different date sequence (e.g., a symbol that didn't trade on a specific holiday), the per-symbol OOS bar counts would diverge — and that would BREAK stitched-Sharpe and ranking-stability metrics (which assume bar-for-bar comparability across symbols at each timestamp). Lesson: when adding new symbols to a batch, enforce a cross-symbol calendar-alignment check (BTC dates == ETH dates == SOL dates == new_symbol dates) at the data-approval gate (here, Auth-7). If it fails, either reject the symbol OR require an explicit gap-handling policy (drop bars / forward-fill / re-align) BEFORE the window-lock gate. Don't discover bar-count divergence at runtime.

- 2026-05-14 Auth-8 lesson — 2022 is a leap-adjacent year, 2024 is leap, 2023 is non-leap — bar counts depend on these — W1 OOS 2022-01-01 → 2022-12-30 inclusive = 364 bars. W2 OOS 2023-01-01 → 2023-12-30 inclusive = 364 bars. W3 OOS 2024-01-01 → 2024-12-30 inclusive = 365 bars (leap year). Total per (strategy, symbol) = 1093 OOS bars across 3 years. The Auth-9 runner MUST assert each per-cell bar count exactly (`len(bar_returns) == 364` or 365 depending on window) — a 1-bar drift would fail the audit's stitched-Sharpe consistency check. Lesson: when locking multi-year windows, ALWAYS list the per-window expected bar count explicitly in the closure doc + enforce it at runtime + verify per-cell at audit consumption. Year-boundary edge cases (Dec 30 vs Dec 31, leap vs non-leap) are common 1-bar drift sources. Lock the count, then test the count.

- 2026-05-14 Auth-8 lesson — holdout-gap headroom matters as a structural buffer — W1 ends 1046 days before the regime v2 holdout starts; W2 ends 681 days before; W3 ends 315 days before. All three are well-buffered. Lesson: when locking OOS windows that approach a protected holdout, the gap-in-days metric is what you want to track — not just "before the holdout starts". A 30-day gap is technically safe but invites mistakes (e.g., off-by-one in window definition or accidental warmup-window expansion). A 300+ day gap eliminates the class of risk. For Batch #003, the smallest gap (W3: 315 days) is comfortable. Codify "≥ 30 days holdout gap" as a hard pre-flight rule going forward, and report the actual gap in days alongside the binary pass/fail check.

- 2026-05-14 Auth-7 lesson — 11-check integrity pattern is reusable across data sources — Auth-3 ran the 11-check integrity pattern on BTCUSD; Auth-7 reused the EXACT same 11-check pattern on ETHUSD + SOLUSD. The checks (file exists, sha matches, required columns, dates parse, no NaN/Inf, no duplicates, no missing days, OHLC consistency, non-negative volume, date span matches, OOS feasibility) are domain-general — they apply to any daily-OHLC time-series CSV. Lesson: when validating a new data source in this codebase, reuse the 11-check pattern verbatim — don't invent ad-hoc checks. The pattern is so reusable I should consider extracting it into a shared validation utility (e.g., `tools/data_validators/ohlc_csv_validator.py`) so future batches (regime v3, futures, FX, etc.) just call the validator instead of re-implementing. Caveat: not done at Auth-7 (don't add infrastructure beyond what's needed) — but flag for a future round.

- 2026-05-14 Auth-7 lesson — cross-symbol calendar alignment is a load-bearing invariant — When validating 3 CSVs intended for cross-symbol metrics (stitched Sharpe, ranking stability, correlation matrix), the per-symbol date sequences MUST be bit-for-bit identical. Auth-7 confirmed BTC dates == ETH dates == SOL dates exactly — but this is NOT guaranteed in general (e.g., different exchanges have different listing dates, different holiday calendars, etc.). Lesson: any future multi-symbol data inventory must include a cross-symbol calendar-alignment check as a separate 12th step beyond per-symbol checks. If alignment fails, the audit's cross-symbol metrics become semantically broken (comparing apples to oranges). Codify this in the 11-check pattern's extension.

- 2026-05-14 Auth-7 lesson — lab-side validator scripts don't trip Phase 9 — auth7_validate.py was authored at C:\SPARTA_RESEARCH_LAB\robustness_audit_exp\ (NOT under C:\SPARTA_BRAIN\). This is intentional and important: the Phase 9 safety scanner (test_phase9_regime_modeling.py::test_lab_python_does_not_import_research_os_or_strategy_lab) scans the LAB ROOT and the LAB ROOT only. SPARTA_BRAIN code that needs to interact with strategy_lab lives at C:\SPARTA_BRAIN\tools\pilot_runners\. Lab-side validators that interact with lab-owned data live in the lab. Lesson: for any future "I need a one-shot script to inspect/validate something" need, ask first: does this script touch SPARTA_BRAIN modules or only lab data? If only lab data, put the script at the lab. If it touches SPARTA_BRAIN, put it under tools/pilot_runners/ or tools/ and use the sys.path bootstrap pattern. This keeps the import-safety invariants clean and Phase 9 happy.

- 2026-05-14 Auth-7 lesson — read-only validation should write only its results — auth7_validate.py reads 3 CSVs + writes ONE JSON output file (batch_003_three_symbol_validation_results.json). It does NOT modify the 3 CSVs, does NOT write to strategy_lab/data/, does NOT touch candidates.json or packs.json. Lesson: a "validation gate" should output a single machine-readable artifact (JSON or similar) that downstream gates can consume, but NEVER mutate the data being validated. The validation result becomes its own audit trail; if the validator is rerun and produces a different result, that itself is a tamper signal.

- 2026-05-14 Post-Auth-6 pause lesson — distinguish "audit FAIL" from "evidence narrow" before signing — When all 5 candidates fail anti_overfit on evidence-coverage thresholds (walk_forward / symbol / regime / trades_count) but pass all quality thresholds (OOS positive / MaxDD ≤ 35% / parameter sensitivity ≤ 70%), running the Checkpoint A audit will produce a verdict whose negative result is dominated by evidence-coverage failure, not strategy-quality failure. Signing that verdict places a misleading FAIL stamp on the project's permanent record — readers will see "the strategies failed the audit" instead of "we tested too narrowly to claim anything". Lesson: BEFORE signing Checkpoint A (or any audit-style verdict), categorize each failed threshold as either (a) evidence-coverage failure (we didn't test broadly enough) or (b) quality failure (the strategy was tested and failed the quality bar). If ALL failures are (a), the verdict means "evidence too narrow" not "strategies bad" — and the right move is to collect broader evidence first. This split is non-obvious; document it in the gap-analysis closure doc so future readers don't misinterpret.

- 2026-05-14 Post-Auth-6 pause lesson — don't lower thresholds to fix narrow evidence — When anti_overfit_gate's thresholds (symbol_count ≥ 3, regime_count ≥ 3, walk_forward ≥ 0.60, trades_count ≥ 30) reject narrow evidence, the WRONG move is to lower those thresholds to make narrow evidence pass. The thresholds ARE the gate's contract; lowering them silently corrupts the meaning of "passed". The RIGHT move is to keep the gate untouched and collect the evidence the gate requires. Batch #003's plan is built around this principle: 3 symbols (the threshold), 36 walk-forward windows per strategy (gives the gate statistical power), 3 OOS years (≥30 trades clears comfortably), 6 regimes classified. Lesson: the gate is the arbiter. Don't change the arbiter to fit the evidence; collect the evidence the arbiter requires.

- 2026-05-14 Post-Auth-6 pause lesson — multi-asset CSVs at the same provenance root enable cheap broader testing — The regime v2 lab's data/raw/ directory already has BTC + ETH + SOL CSVs from the same exchange historical → regime v1 → regime v2 provenance chain, all with identical date range (2021-01-01 → 2026-05-12) and identical bar count (1958). At Auth-3 only BTC was approved; the other two were "reference-only". That choice was the right move at Auth-3 (smaller decision surface) but it surfaces now: adding ETH + SOL is a one-Auth ask (Auth-7) with no new fetches, no new APIs, just elevating reference-only to approved. Lesson: when curating data sources at a lab, even if you only authorize ONE source initially, curate the SIBLING sources at the same provenance root so future authorizations are integrity-pre-validated. This pattern saves a full Auth round in the future. Apply to: regime v3 (if it happens), futures/stocks/FX CSVs (when needed), etc.

- 2026-05-14 Post-Auth-6 pause lesson — single-year bull-year OOS can mask strategy weakness — Batch #002 OOS was 2024 BTCUSD, which was +125% spot. ALL 5 strategies showed positive OOS returns (+7% to +79%) — looking great. But this can be entirely explained by "long-bias + bull year" rather than "the strategy has edge". Batch #003 deliberately samples 3 OOS years: 2022 (BTC crashed ~75%), 2023 (mostly sideways), 2024 (bull). A strategy with REAL edge should still average positive across all three. A strategy that was just long-biased in a bull year will get exposed in 2022's downturn. Lesson: never sign a robustness verdict from a single bull-year sample. Multi-year OOS — especially including down years — is the structural antidote to confirmation bias. Codified now: any future "audit OOS window" lock for crypto strategies must include at least one bull year + one bear year + one sideways year, or be marked CONDITIONAL by construction.

- 2026-05-14 Post-Auth-6 pause lesson — strategy-level aggregate vs per-experiment candidate_id — anti_overfit_gate consumes ONE candidate at a time with one set of input fields. For Batch #003 with 45 per-experiment v2 records (5 strategies × 3 symbols × 3 years), the design choice is: do we run anti_overfit per-experiment (45 verdicts) or per-strategy aggregate (5 verdicts)? Per-experiment makes each verdict's symbol_count_tested = 1 (which always fails the threshold ≥ 3). Per-strategy aggregate gives the strategy a symbol_count_tested = 3 (matching the threshold). The aggregate is the CORRECT shape because anti_overfit measures whether a STRATEGY has been tested broadly, not whether a single experiment has. Lesson: when a downstream gate has "breadth" thresholds, aggregate the inputs at the breadth-appropriate level. A per-experiment shape misuses the gate. Encode the aggregate explicitly with a `<name>_aggregate_v1` candidate_id pattern so per-experiment and strategy-level records don't get confused in the registry.

- 2026-05-14 Auth-6 lesson — honest defaults beat synthetic fill — anti_overfit_gate's AntiOverfitInput has 7 fields; batch #002 measured 3 of them (out_of_sample_return, trades_count, max_drawdown). For the OTHER 4 (in_sample_return, walk_forward_pass_rate, symbol_count_tested, regime_count_tested, parameter_sensitivity_score) batch #002 had no data. Two choices: (a) fill with optimistic synthetic values to make the verdict pass, or (b) fill with honest zeros (or 1 for "BTCUSD only") which CORRECTLY causes thresholds to fail. Chose (b) for Auth-6. Lesson: when a downstream gate has thresholds that require evidence you don't have, filling honest zeros surfaces the evidence-coverage gap AS the verdict failure. Filling synthetic values would create the illusion of evidence and corrupt the verdict's meaning. The HIGH-risk reject_or_rework verdicts that result are the TRUTHFUL signal that evidence is narrow — they are NOT a strategy indictment. This is the right pattern for any future "I have partial evidence and need a verdict" situation.

- 2026-05-14 Auth-6 lesson — verdict ≠ deployment recommendation — anti_overfit_gate's recommendation field returns "reject_or_rework" when thresholds fail. In SPARTA terminology this might sound like "the strategy is bad, reject it". In the gate's actual semantics it means "the EVIDENCE is insufficient, gather more evidence before any deployment decision". The distinction matters because "reject_or_rework" gets surfaced in dashboards, reports, and brain memory — readers who don't know the convention might conflate evidence-coverage rejection with strategy-quality rejection. Lesson: when re-reading anti_overfit verdicts, always check WHICH thresholds failed: evidence-coverage thresholds (symbol_count, regime_count, walk_forward, trades_count) vs performance-quality thresholds (OOS positive, MaxDD ≤ 0.35, parameter sensitivity ≤ 0.70). Batch #002 verdicts failed 100% on evidence-coverage and 0% on quality. Document this distinction in the manifest so future readers don't misinterpret.

- 2026-05-14 Auth-6 lesson — agreement-rate metric needs evidence asymmetry awareness — The audit's Agreement-Rate metric checks whether the audit's WFE-based verdict agrees with anti_overfit's coverage-based verdict. In a NARROW-EVIDENCE batch like #002, the most likely outcome is "both verdicts reject, agreement-rate is high (1.0) by mutual rejection". A naive reader could see "agreement rate = 1.0" and conclude "both metrics confirm the strategies are robust". The opposite is true: both metrics confirm the EVIDENCE is narrow. Lesson: when shipping an agreement-rate metric, document the "high agreement under mutual rejection" failure mode explicitly in the metric's definition — and require the audit verdict report to call it out when ≥80% of candidates fail BOTH gates. Otherwise the metric can be misread as a quality endorsement.

- 2026-05-14 Auth-6 lesson — incremental gate strategy works — The chain Auth-1 (sourcing) → Auth-2 (strategies) → Auth-3 (data) → Auth-4 (tests) → Auth-5 (execution) → Auth-6 (anti_overfit) → Checkpoint A preregistration → audit run made it possible to surface the "anti_overfit verdicts will FAIL because evidence is narrow" finding at Auth-6 BEFORE running the audit. If the audit had run on Path B (WFE-only CONDITIONAL verdict), this finding would only have surfaced inside the audit verdict — too late to choose a different path. Lesson: when an evaluation chain has gates that can fail for "evidence too narrow" reasons, run the gates BEFORE the evaluation, not concurrent with it. Each gate is cheap; the evaluation is expensive. Order matters.

- 2026-05-14 Checkpoint A prep lesson — preregister BEFORE computing — Mahmoud's explicit framing: "Lock the audit rules first. Then run the audit. Never compute first and decide rules after." This is non-negotiable because if metrics are computed before definitions are locked, the rules can be silently rewritten post-hoc to make a desired result look like a pass. The preregistration packet (6 docs) defines EVERY decision the audit will make in advance: which candidates, which windows, which metrics, which thresholds, which stop codes. Once signed, the audit code MUST follow it exactly; any deviation = new preregistration round. Lesson: for any audit-style evaluation in this codebase, the metric definitions + stop conditions + pass/fail rules must land in a signed preregistration BEFORE any computation. This applies to Checkpoint A here, and to any future "robustness", "promotion", or "ship-readiness" checks.

- 2026-05-14 Checkpoint A prep lesson — fixed-config WFE caveat — Walk-Forward Efficiency in the classical literature measures the stability of OPTIMIZED parameters: refit on IS window → evaluate on OOS window → WFE = OOS_sharpe / IS_sharpe. The 5 batch #002 strategies use FIXED parameters (their DEFAULT_CONFIG); they do NOT refit. Therefore WFE here measures "out-of-sample stability of a fixed strategy" — not parameter-optimization stability. This caveat MUST be documented in the preregistration (it is, in audit_metric_definitions.md § "Fixed-config caveat") so the metric is not silently reinterpreted later. Lesson: when adapting a classical metric to a non-classical setup, name the deviation explicitly at lock time. If a future batch adds parameter optimization, the WFE metric needs a new preregistration round.

- 2026-05-14 Checkpoint A prep lesson — companion evidence gaps surface late if not checked early — Anti_overfit verdicts and regime_score records DO NOT EXIST for the 5 batch #002 candidates. This was knowable BEFORE Auth-5 ran (the runner does not invoke anti_overfit_gate / regime_score, so the gap is structural) but only surfaced now at preregistration. Earlier surfacing would have given Mahmoud the option to run anti_overfit in parallel with Auth-5, saving an authorization round. Lesson: when an audit will eventually need companion evidence (anti_overfit, regime_score, research_plan), CHECK FOR ITS PRESENCE EARLY (at the earliest pre-flight gate, not at preregistration). If missing, surface it BEFORE the new candidates are committed so the user can fold the companion run into the same authorization.

- 2026-05-14 Checkpoint A prep lesson — friction-affine strategies enable cheap stress testing — All 5 batch #002 strategies are FRICTION-AFFINE: friction enters linearly as `position-delta × fee_rate`, and the strategies' state machines do NOT branch on fee_bps / slippage_bps (verified by Auth-4 test #19's forbidden-pattern scan and test #15's friction monotonicity). Therefore the audit can compute 1.5×/2.0× friction stress by DECOMPOSING recorded bar returns into (gross_return − friction_component) and rescaling the friction component — WITHOUT re-running the strategy. This is ~50× faster than re-execution and PRESERVES the trial-count log's append-only invariant. Lesson: when a strategy is friction-affine, friction stress is a closed-form post-hoc transformation, not a re-run. Encode the "friction-affine?" property as a contract field in the v2 schema if more strategies adopt it; the audit can then auto-detect when decomposition is valid vs invalid.

- 2026-05-14 Auth-5 lesson — strategy regression results on 2024 BTCUSD are NOT edge evidence — All 5 batch #002 strategies showed positive OOS returns (+7% to +79%), which sounds great but mostly reflects that 2024 BTCUSD spot was up ~125%. The regime_filter_overlay's +78.99% captured the most of the trend because it was long during the up-trend; volatility_targeting's +22.60% with 365 trades was smaller because daily rebalancing dampens the move. None of this is evidence of strategy edge — it's evidence of long-bias + 2024 being a bull year. Lesson: positive OOS returns on a single bull year are NOT a Checkpoint A signal. The audit needs WFE (IS sharpe vs OOS sharpe), bootstrap (vs zero-mean null), regime stress (does edge survive bear regimes too?), and friction stress before any edge claim is testable.

- 2026-05-14/15 BRAIN MEMORY REVERT NOTE — lessons from Auth-7..Auth-14 + Checkpoint A FAIL + Batch #004 planning are documented in the lab closure docs at C:/SPARTA_RESEARCH_LAB/robustness_audit_exp/. Key lessons to remember: (1) rank research directions by addressability x benefit-preservation x scope; (2) preregistration captures HYPOTHESIS not implementation; (3) standalone variant modules preserve independent auditability; (4) stop check has priority over baseline exits when overlay adds stricter condition; (5) for long-only binary positions, peak price tracking = peak equity tracking (mathematically equivalent); (6) Wilder ATR at t-1 is lookahead-free by construction; (7) honest negative results have research value; (8) multiple independent gates is the right structural design for blocking deployment; (9) planning memos are NOT authorizations; (10) friction stress is the bottleneck for high-turnover strategies; (11) stitched MaxDD != max-of-per-cell-MaxDD; (12) agreement rate of 1.0 in a fail-everything batch is NOT a quality signal; (13) DC-5 not triggered (correlations 0.0-0.66) means ensemble research is structurally viable; (14) locked preregistration filenames may conflict with lab whitelists (audit_trial_log.jsonl -> .json deviation). Full text in lab closure docs.

- 2026-05-14/15 Auth-15 lesson — disabled-stop-equals-baseline is the cleanest behavioral test for an additive overlay. For each of V1/V2/V3, setting the stop threshold to a value so loose it never fires (stop_fixed_threshold=0.99 / stop_trailing_threshold=0.99 / stop_atr_multiplier=1000) should produce bar_returns BYTE-IDENTICAL to the baseline strategy. This is a strong correctness test: it proves the overlay is purely additive (does NOT alter baseline behavior when dormant). The complementary test — setting a very tight threshold and verifying behavior DIFFERS — proves the overlay is active when enabled. Together: the overlay is wired correctly. Lesson: when authoring tests for an additive overlay, ALWAYS include (a) disabled-overlay-matches-baseline and (b) tight-overlay-changes-behavior. These two tests bookend the overlay's correctness without requiring pixel-perfect synthetic fixtures for specific trigger events.

- 2026-05-14/15 Auth-15 lesson — source-ordering tests verify priority without requiring impossible fixtures. To prove the stop check has priority over RSI/max_hold, the most defensible test is: inspect the source and verify the stop condition's line number is LOWER than the RSI/max_hold check. This is a structural test that documents the locked design. The alternative — engineering a synthetic fixture where BOTH conditions fire simultaneously — is fragile (depends on specific bar values) and may not catch all priority bugs. Source-ordering tests (via `src.find(...)` returning lower index) are robust and document the invariant clearly. Apply to any future priority-ordered state machine tests.

- 2026-05-14/15 Auth-15 lesson — peak-tracking for long-only binary is equivalent to peak-price-tracking. V2's trailing stop tracks peak close-price (not peak equity). For long-only positions with binary {0,1} sizing, the equity ratio since entry equals the price ratio since entry — so tracking peak price is mathematically equivalent + simpler than tracking peak equity. The trailing-stop trigger `close[t-1] < peak_price * (1 - threshold)` is equivalent to `current_equity_ratio < peak_equity_ratio * (1 - threshold)`. Lesson: prefer the LEANEST equivalent state in tests and in implementation. Don't track multiple quantities when one suffices. If the strategy class extends to leverage or shorts, peak equity becomes the right thing — but for current scope, peak price is cleaner.

- 2026-05-14/15 Auth-16 lesson — G16 (distinct OOS SHA across N records) can have EXPECTED collisions in additive-overlay batches. For Batch #004's 27 records (3 variants × 9 cells), only 15 unique `oos_bar_returns_sha256` values were observed. This is NOT a failure — it reflects the Auth-15-verified invariant `disabled-stop-matches-baseline`. In (symbol, year) windows where price action doesn't trigger any variant's stop (e.g., BTC 2023, BTC 2024, SOL 2023, SOL 2024 with low drawdowns), all 3 variants legitimately reduce to baseline bar_returns → identical SHA. Auth-16's task wording was "distinct **where expected**" — this collision pattern IS the expected case. Lesson: when designing an additive-overlay batch, anticipate that low-DD windows produce baseline-equivalent variant outputs and document the expected unique-SHA count BEFORE running. State the structural expectation ("variants will collide in windows where stops don't fire") in the preregistration so post-run G16 interpretation doesn't read it as a tampering signal.

- 2026-05-14/15 Auth-16 lesson — ATR-volatility-adaptive stops outperform fixed-level stops on the same RSI baseline. V3's ATR(14)-based 2.5× stop produced the highest mean OOS return (+11.23%), lowest worst MaxDD (42.28%), AND zero worse-than-baseline cells across 9 (symbol, year) cells. V1's fixed 10% stop was mixed (1 big win, 3 losses). V2's trailing 10% stop was uniformly worse than baseline (0 wins, 4 losses, lowest WF rate). The mechanism: ATR scales with realized vol → wider stops in low-vol regimes (let baseline run) → tighter stops in high-vol regimes (cap bear-year losses). Auth-13 preregistration predicted this exactly. Lesson: when adding risk-management overlays to mean-reversion strategies, prefer volatility-adaptive thresholds over fixed thresholds — especially when the strategy is regime-sensitive. Document this finding as the seed for any future Batch #005 design (e.g., ATR-stop + dynamic sizing).

- 2026-05-14/15 Auth-16 lesson — stream timeout recovery via Classification A/B/C/D is a forensic protocol, not panic. When a stream idle timeout interrupts an authorized execution mid-way, the correct response is NOT "rerun blindly" or "abort". It is to (1) inspect the file system + git state, (2) classify mutation level: A = no mutation (continue), B = partial state in lab only (continue with awareness), C = partial mutation in production state requiring careful audit, D = corrupted state requiring rollback, and (3) act per classification. Auth-16's recovery: snapshot was taken, runner was NOT written, no production state mutation → Classification A → continue cleanly. The classification is decided by EVIDENCE (sha-compare + glob + read), not assumption. Lesson: codify this 4-level classification in the agent's playbook for any future authorized-execution interruption. Don't blindly rerun; don't blindly abort; classify, then act.

- 2026-05-14/15 Auth-16 lesson — stitched-MaxDD vs cell-wise MaxDD measure different things. Batch #003's baseline rsi_mean_reversion had cell-wise worst MaxDD of 42.28% (SOL 2022) and stitched MaxDD of 51.40% (Auth-10 computation on the compounded 9-cell equity curve). The c8 criterion in Auth-13 references the stitched value (51.40%). All 3 Batch #004 variants beat 51.40% (42.28-44.67%) — but only V3 ties the cell-wise 42.28%. Lesson: when reporting MaxDD comparisons across batches, ALWAYS distinguish cell-wise (worst per-cell value) from stitched (compounded equity curve drawdown). These can differ by 10+pp. Pre-register which definition the criterion references; post-hoc choice of definition is a backdoor for rule-rewriting. Auth-13 did this correctly (c8 explicitly references the Auth-10 stitched number).

- 2026-05-14/15 Auth-16 lesson — additive overlay matches baseline byte-identically when dormant — and that's a structural property worth verifying explicitly. V3 (ATR-based) produced byte-identical SHA to baseline in 8 of 9 cells. The 1 differing cell (ETH 2022) is the case where the overlay fired and improved the outcome. This pattern is the desired shape for an additive overlay: never worse than baseline, sometimes better. V1 and V2 violate this shape (4-3 worse-than-baseline cells respectively). Lesson: when designing additive overlays, the "never-worse-than-baseline" property is structural goal #1. If a variant produces worse outcomes than baseline in any cell, its overlay logic is altering baseline behavior in a way that hurts. Codify this check as part of variant evaluation: count of worse-than-baseline cells should be 0 for a clean overlay. Use this as a screening filter BEFORE running expensive audits (anti_overfit, regime_score).

- 2026-05-14/15 Auth-16 lesson — variant-strategy v2 records inherit Auth-13/14/15 invariants automatically. The 27 v2 records produced under Auth-16 inherit: (1) lookahead-free strategy code (Auth-15 verified per-bar SHA-stability), (2) friction-affine bar-return decomposition (Auth-15 verified via friction monotonicity tests), (3) walk-forward sub-window aggregation in `window_metrics` (Auth-9 pattern), (4) the 6 strategy contract invariants (Auth-15 verified). No new contract work was needed at Auth-16. Lesson: when adding a strategy variant to an established framework, the per-strategy invariants should already be enforced by the framework + Auth-15-style tests — and the per-batch invariants (G16/G17/G18/G19) should be agnostic to the variant set. Treat invariants as code-level guarantees, NOT per-batch reverification work. Auth-16 ran in ~5 seconds because all invariants were structurally guaranteed.

- 2026-05-15 Deep Research Cycle #3 lesson — the right response to a chain of honest negatives on one data class is NOT another mechanic on the same class but a family whose RETURN IS A DIFFERENT OBJECT. #003-#006 (directional) and F5 (relative-value cointegration) all failed on OHLC-only; both are "price-pattern" returns. The meta-finding said the binding constraint is data scope. So the screening filter for "is this actually a new direction" is: does the strategy's P&L come from a genuine cash flow / structural premium computed on a different information set, or is it still a realized price move on the same set? Funding-carry (G1) passes (cash flow from the funding series); larger-universe momentum (G6/G7) fails (still OHLC price moves). Codify: novelty-vs-failed-lines must be scored on INFORMATION SET + RETURN SOURCE, not on mechanic cleverness. A high raw score with NX=1 should be tier-capped, not promoted.

- 2026-05-15 Deep Research Cycle #3 lesson — for any future funding/carry/basis work the #1 honesty risk is "fake yield": funding collected looks like edge but is erased by spot-perp basis convergence + full round-trip fees/slippage on BOTH legs + funding PAID in negative-funding regimes. The simulation must net all four BEFORE any metric is reported, exactly as the friction model was made mandatory for directional work. Liquidation/leverage need NOT be live-modeled to test G1 research-first: size the short perp at ≤1x effective and model a conservative maintenance-margin buffer; the research question is "does net carry survive costs", not "can we run leverage". Public historical funding + spot/perp price is available WITHOUT API keys (Binance/OKX/Bybit) so G1 is genuinely research-first.

- 2026-05-15 G1 planning lesson — a disciplined "GO" recommendation under a paused program must be BOUNDED TO EXACTLY THE NEXT GATE, never open-ended. The correct shape: recommend GO for *the immediately-next separately-signed gate only* (here: a data-acquisition + integrity gate), and explicitly enumerate the remaining sequential Mahmoud signatures (data gate → preregistration → backtest → anti_overfit/regime_score → … → deployment) so a GO can never be read as transitive authorization down the chain. Also: when a frozen gate threshold (anti_overfit symbol_count_tested ≥ 3) collides with a deliberately-minimal first scope (BTC-only to de-risk the mechanic), the right move is to FLAG the dependency in the scope doc (v1 BTC-only, ETH/SOL added before any future gate run) — never to soften the frozen threshold and never to silently expand scope. Bounding the recommendation + flagging-not-softening is the reusable pattern for advisory work inside a paused, gate-disciplined program.

- 2026-05-15 G1-Auth-1 lesson — for funding-carry data, the decisive integrity metric is NOT per-series row counts but the cross-series COMPLETE-TRIPLET coverage in the usable intersection (funding stamp has BOTH a perp 8h bar AND a spot 8h bar). Per-series spans differ (Binance: perp from 2019-09-08, funding from 2019-09-10, mark/index only from 2019-12-23, spot from 2017-08-17), so naive per-file coverage is misleading; the research window is governed by the intersection (here 2019-09-10 governed by funding/perp launch -> 100% triplet). Also: Binance's funding endpoint embeds a markPrice convenience field that is placeholder/empty for early history (4536/7319 rows pre-2023-11) — always treat embedded convenience fields as untrusted and source price from dedicated kline series; verify by independent count, not by assuming the field is populated. And: keyless Binance public market-data (fapi /fundingRate, /klines, /markPriceKlines, /indexPriceKlines uses pair=; api /api/v3/klines) is fully sufficient for G1 research acquisition — no API key needed; assert no-trading-endpoint by scanning the fetch log for forbidden paths, not by trusting intent.

- 2026-05-15 G1-Auth-2 lesson — for a carry/market-neutral preregistration the conservative-PRIMARY design is "continuous always-on hold that EATS negative funding", not a funding-sign filter. Reason: the sign filter has look-ahead temptation + turnover, and (critically) if you let a sign-gated variant be a pass route you reintroduce the post-hoc rescue trap (cherry-pick the regime that worked). Correct pattern: PRIMARY = zero-discretion continuous hold (most conservative, biases AGAINST false positives); SECONDARY = causal sign-gate as DIAGNOSTIC ONLY, pre-committed to never convert a failing PRIMARY into a pass. Also: make the re-hedge rule PARAMETER-FREE (rebalance every stamp on the accumulated delta-drift increment only) rather than a threshold band — a tunable band is a hidden researcher degree-of-freedom that a preregistration must eliminate. And restate the anti_overfit >=3-symbol collision every gate as a flagged structural dependency (BTC v1 -> add ETH -> add SOL) and NEVER as a threshold to soften — flag-don't-soften is the standing pattern for frozen-gate collisions.

- 2026-05-15 G1-Auth-3 lesson — "module parses / static validation" under a do-NOT-run gate must be AST/py_compile ONLY and must NEVER import the engine: importing executes module-level code (== running). Pattern: a separate validator that does ast.parse(open(file).read()) + py_compile.compile(doraise=True) (compiles to bytecode WITHOUT executing body); the engine itself must have zero module-level calls and a __main__ guard that does not call the sim. Recurring false-positive class (now seen twice: F5 'random.', G1 'credential'): a substring forbidden-pattern scanner trips on the module's own SAFETY DOCSTRING that names the very thing it forbids ("NO credential imports"). Correct disciplined fix = fix the SCANNER (tokenize-strip STRING/COMMENT tokens, scan code tokens only), NOT the module — the accurate safety docstring is correct as written; changing the module to dodge a scanner bug would be backwards. Always disclose the scanner correction honestly in the report.

- 2026-05-15 G1-Auth-4 lesson (HIGH VALUE) — unit tests are the layer that catches LOCKED-SPEC defects, and the disciplined response is to FAIL LOUDLY, not to make the test green. The G1 preregistration had a self-contradiction (L65 +funding_rate "receives ... income" vs L84/C3 -funding_rate); the engine implemented the literal wrong formula. Two anti-patterns to avoid: (1) silently flipping the engine sign to match economics (violates "don't change locked params" + hides that the prereg itself is broken); (2) weakening the test to assert the engine's inverted output (manufactures a green suite around a bug = the inverted fake-yield trap). Correct pattern: keep the economically-correct assertion, mark it @unittest.expectedFailure WITH an inline cited disclosure, keep engine+prereg unchanged, and escalate to a dedicated correction gate. KEY DETECTION INSIGHT: an internal-consistency check is NOT sufficient — reconcile_cashflow passed because the simulator AND the reconciler shared the same inverted sign; only an INDEPENDENT economic-ground-truth fixture (raw Binance fundingRate>0 => short earns) exposed it. Always include at least one economic-ground-truth test that does not derive its expectation from the code under test. Sign conventions for funding/borrow/carry P&L are the single highest-risk spec area — pin them to an external definition (exchange docs) in the preregistration, not to a formula that can silently invert.

- 2026-05-15 G1-Auth-4A lesson — the correct lifecycle for a locked-spec defect is: detect in tests (G1-Auth-4: fail loudly, disclose, do NOT silently fix) -> THEN a dedicated, explicitly-authorized correction gate (G1-Auth-4A: sign-only amendment + re-test). Do not collapse the two: fixing under the test gate would have been an unauthorized silent change to a locked parameter; deferring to a named correction gate keeps the audit trail clean and the change scoped. Scoping discipline that worked: amend ONLY the contradictory line + a correction note, change ONLY the 3 engine sign sites, flip ONLY the 2 affected tests; touch nothing else (design/costs/criteria/threshold/windows/data) and say so explicitly in every report. Verification discipline that worked: the proof the fix is RIGHT (not just self-consistent) is that the simulator AND reconcile were corrected together AND the two economic-ground-truth fixtures (expectations sourced from the exchange convention, not the code) now pass. Always re-confirm safety-static (stdlib-only/no-forbidden/no-write) after editing the engine even for a 1-char sign flip — a corrected suite must re-prove ALL invariants, not just the changed behaviour.

- 2026-05-15 G1-Auth-5 lesson (HIGH VALUE) — an implausibly good market-neutral result (Sharpe ~8.9, ~51%/yr, MaxDD ~5%) is a RED FLAG, not a win; treat "too good" as presumptive artifact until reconciled. The decisive catch here was the S7 cashflow-reconciliation gate: an INDEPENDENT unit-notional recomputation of total funding (0.794, == mean_rate x n_stamps) vs the simulator's gross (3.462) exposed that the engine accrues funding on a re-hedged notional that COMPOUNDS with the underlying's ~8x multi-year price rise -> "carry" was notional inflation, not yield. Generalizable rule: any P&L that accrues on a notional which rides the underlying must be reconciled against a fixed/unit-notional independent recompute BEFORE believing the headline; a passing internal/friction check is NOT sufficient (friction-stress S6 "passed" on the same inflated basis). Also: the SECONDARY-vs-PRIMARY contrast (GE-3) is a powerful pre-committed honest-negative trigger — when the selective/causal variant collapses (-1.21, 488 churned entries) while the always-on looks great, the always-on "edge" is entangled with holding-through-negative/turnover structure, not a real selectable carry. Preregistering BOTH an independent-reconcile check AND a selective-variant contrast is what makes a too-good result falsifiable. Discipline held: FAIL archived, not rescued/tuned/rerun; fixing the notional/withdrawal convention would be a NEW preregistration-design gate, not an in-gate edit.

- 2026-05-15 G1 close lesson — when a fired-invalidity result is closed, the disciplined output is CLOSURE DOCUMENTATION, not iteration: a close decision, a plain final-negative summary, a root-cause artifact analysis, an explicit no-next-gate decision, and a SEPARATELY-SCOPED research-only future-design memo that is explicitly NOT a rescue/continuation. Keep the "what could fix this later" ideas (fixed-notional / swept-cash / separate ledgers / margin model) firmly partitioned from the closed scope: they are questions for a NEW preregistration-design line needing its own top-level decision, never an in-place G1 retry. This partition is what prevents an honest negative from quietly mutating into an unbounded tuning loop. Reusable forward rule for any successor carry design: make the independent unit/contract-notional funding reconcile a BLOCKING pre-run gate (not a post-hoc S-criterion), define return as fixed-capital or swept-cash, keep a selective-variant (GE-3) contrast, and add an a-priori "too good" Sharpe/annualized tripwire that forces artifact investigation before any PASS.

- 2026-05-15 G2 planning lesson — when a family fails on an accounting artifact (G1 notional inflation), the right successor is not "try harder on the same structure" but a sibling whose STRUCTURE makes the failure mode impossible-by-construction. Dated futures expire and cash-settle => fixed per-contract notional + a deterministic per-contract reconciliation point; that is why G2 is the rational next sibling, not just "another carry". But structure only makes the fix TRACTABLE — it must still be designed in: the GO was deliberately issued BOUNDED + CONDITIONAL (next-gate-only) with the separate-ledger/fixed-capital/blocking-pre-run-reconcile/"too good"-tripwire model as a hard precondition (restart R3/R4), and the data-acquisition+integrity gate mandated FIRST and SEPARATE. Reusable pattern for "should we pursue family X after a related failure": (a) name the prior failure's root cause, (b) test whether X's structure removes it by construction vs inherits it, (c) if removable, GO bounded to the next gate with the remediation as a binding precondition; never an unconditional GO, never collapse data-acquisition into the planning gate.

- 2026-05-15 G2-Auth-1 lesson — Binance public archive: machine-readable listing is the S3 REST host (s3-ap-northeast-1.amazonaws.com/data.binance.vision?delimiter=/&prefix=...) returning ListBucketResult XML; the data.binance.vision/?prefix= host returns a JS HTML app and silently parses to ZERO (a probe caught this before the real run — always raw-dump an unexpectedly-empty listing, never trust silent-empty). Files still download from data.binance.vision/<key>. Expired delivery contracts are absent from live fapi exchangeInfo and REST klines won't serve them -> the archive is the only public source for the historical dated chain; derive expiry from BTCUSDT_YYMMDD and ANCHOR it against a live quarterly's deliveryDate (verify, don't assume). Cross-gate dataset reuse is legitimate + minimal-safe IF recorded by reference + re-hashed + asserted equal to the prior pin (explicit provenance). Per-contract settlement-price is usually not public; futures->spot convergence at delivery is the disciplined treatment, documented as a limitation. Don't over-acquire (8h/mark/index/OI) when daily answers a slow-moving-basis question. Also: the Bash tool cwd persists across calls — a prior `cd` into a data dir made later relative brain_memory appends silently fail (No such file) while a trailing echo still 'succeeded'; always use absolute paths (or cd /c/SPARTA_BRAIN) for brain_memory writes and verify the append actually landed.

- 2026-05-15 G2-Auth-2 lesson — the structural fix for a fake-yield/notional-inflation failure (G1) is two-fold and must be baked into the preregistration, not bolted on later: (1) FIXED initial capital + FIXED per-contract notional that never scales with the underlying's price (removes the inflation channel by construction); (2) convert the reconcile from a post-hoc success criterion (G1's S7, which let the artifact reach the metric battery) into a BLOCKING PRE-FLIGHT that ABORTS before any metric is produced on mismatch. Add an a-priori "too good" tripwire (implausible ann/Sharpe forces artifact investigation pre-PASS) so an implausible number can never be reported as a clean win. Generalizable: when designing a successor to an artifact-failed family, enumerate the prior root cause and show in the prereg WHERE each remedy structurally lives (fixed-notional math; pre-flight abort gate; tripwire; selective-variant contrast; beta/convergence neutrality proof) — and exclude incomplete/live units (here unexpired contracts) from scoring to prevent look-ahead. Dated futures' expiry+settlement gives a natural per-contract reconciliation anchor that a perpetual lacked — exploit that as the reconcile basis.

- 2026-05-15 G2-Auth-3 lesson — the G1->G2 remediation must be visible in the CODE STRUCTURE, not just prose: FIXED_NOTIONAL is a module constant used directly in _contract_pnl with NO code path multiplying it by price (the inflation channel is structurally absent, not merely "discouraged"); and blocking_reconcile is wired so success_evaluation returns FAIL immediately on reconcile_abort BEFORE any S-vector is considered (pre-flight, the explicit fix for G1's post-hoc S7). When implementing an artifact-hardened successor, encode each remedy as an invariant a static reader can verify (constant-not-scaled; abort-gates-metrics; DIAGNOSTIC_ONLY/can_rescue=False) so the function inventory itself proves the failure mode is designed out. Also: applying the tokenize-strip code-token scanner PRE-EMPTIVELY (lesson carried from F5 'random.' / G1 'credential') meant the G2 static validator passed first try with no module edit — institutionalizing a known false-positive fix upstream avoids re-litigating it each gate.

- 2026-05-15 G2-Auth-4 lesson — distinguish a RESULTS-NEUTRAL robustness/implementation-faithfulness fix from a LOCKED-SEMANTICS change. The None-expiry crash in validate_inputs prevented the engine from REPORTING the prereg's GI2 "missing expiry -> invalid"; fixing it (a None guard) makes the engine do what the locked spec already said, changes no parameter/accounting/threshold/cost/strategy, and alters no computed result -> correct to fix + disclose under the test gate (same class as the F5 validator-not-semantics fix), NOT a G1-style sign defect requiring a separate correction gate. Litmus: does the fix change any number a passing run would produce, or any locked threshold/cost/accounting/strategy rule? If no -> disclosed robustness fix is in-scope; if yes -> stop, disclose, escalate to a correction gate (G1-Auth-4A precedent). Also reaffirmed: economic-ground-truth fixtures (expectations from the exchange/no-arbitrage identity, not the code) are what actually prove an artifact-hardened engine is correct — here they confirmed fixed-notional has NO price-scaling path and the blocking reconcile ABORTs on a ledger mismatch (the two structural anti-G1 guarantees), independent of internal consistency. Keep test helpers module-level; never cross-inherit unittest.TestCase classes (it silently re-runs the parent suite under every child and explodes the count).

- 2026-05-16 G2-Auth-5 lesson (HIGH VALUE) — there are TWO kinds of honest negative and they must be reported differently: (A) G1-class = the NUMBER IS FAKE (reconcile failed, +343%/Sharpe 8.9 notional-inflation artifact); (B) G2-class = the NUMBER IS REAL but does not clear the FULL conjunctive bar (reconcile PASSED to 4e-15, modest +6.2%/yr/Sharpe 1.31/beta~0/cost-surviving, fails only on S5 settlement-measurement-precision + S8 a 4e-15 float-epsilon ordering artifact). Both are FAIL/honest-negative and neither is advanced — but the write-up must state which, because (B) is genuine evidence the structural anti-fake-yield design WORKS and that a thin, real, market-neutral dated-basis carry exists yet is not certifiable on public daily data. Reusable rules: (1) a strict measurement-precision gate (S5 conv-err 0.5%) will correctly fail a real edge when the data proxy (no public per-contract settlement price -> spot-at-delivery on daily bars) is too coarse — that's the gate working, not a bug; do NOT loosen it under the run gate. (2) Reconciliation/ordering checks that compare a recomputed-sum vs an accumulated-total MUST use the SAME tolerance (1e-6), or a zero-tolerance strict inequality will flip on ~1e-15 float non-associativity and produce a spurious FAIL component (S8). Surface it, disclose it, do NOT silently fix under an execution gate (G1-Auth-4->4A precedent); any correction is a separate explicit gate. (3) "Too good is a red flag" has a converse: "plausible + reconciled + market-neutral + cost-surviving" is the signature of a REAL but thin edge — still gate it honestly, never round a FAIL up to a pass because the economics look sane.

- 2026-05-16 G2 post-fail lesson — when a result is REAL (reconciled, market-neutral, cost-surviving) but FAILS only on non-economic criteria (a data-precision gate + a float-epsilon artifact), the disciplined recommendation is still usually CLOSE (A), not reopen — because (a) the economics are already characterizable without a rerun (here: thin, contango-regime-fragile ~6%/yr), so a corrected rerun yields informational confirmation, not a strategic change; (b) reopening invites the open-ended-iteration trap the program repeatedly identified; (c) even a corrected PASS faces the full downstream chain (anti_overfit >=3 symbols, regime_score, robustness, paper arena, 6 gates) for a modest, regime-fragile prize. Reusable decision rule: separate "is the result TRUE?" from "is the result WORTH PURSUING?" — G2 is true-but-thin; truth doesn't oblige pursuit. If reopening is chosen anyway, the ONLY valid mechanism is a single explicitly-authorized preregistration-amendment gate that fixes ALL non-economic blockers together and is RE-LOCKED before exactly one fresh run (never piecemeal: a data-only gate that leaves a known float-epsilon FAIL in place is dominated/pointless). Never silently correct even a vacuous post-lock criterion (S8) under the gate that produced the result — falsifiability of the whole prereg framework depends on it; disclose and route to a separate amendment gate (G1-Auth-4->4A precedent).

- 2026-05-15T22:46:53 - pytest lesson marker: read-only analytics before automation

- 2026-05-15T22:47:17 - No repeated issue was detected in parsed trade history; improve trade tagging before drawing stronger conclusions.

- 2026-05-15T22:47:17 - Parsed history shows 0 loss(es) out of 2 trade(s); focus review on losing clusters, not isolated trades.

- 2026-05-15T22:47:17 - Missing fields limit analysis quality: strategy, realized_r, expected_r should be logged for future trade reviews.

- 2026-05-16 G2 close lesson — the disciplined endpoint of a long research arc is a CLEAN CLOSE with the strongest finding archived honestly, not a marginal rerun. "Strongest result" and "deployable" are orthogonal: G2 was the strongest (real/reconciled/market-neutral/cost-surviving) AND non-deployable (thin/regime-fragile/fails S5+S8) — both stated plainly, neither inflated. Closing here (vs Option C) was correct because the result was already fully CHARACTERIZABLE without a rerun, so a corrected rerun would have been informational confirmation at the cost of the open-ended-iteration trap. Reusable: when every remaining blocker is non-economic but the economics are already known to be thin/fragile, the EV of reopening is low and the EV of disciplined closure is high — close, archive the finding as knowledge, update memory so the chain's completeness ("no deployable edge found; discipline intact") is the durable takeaway, and require any reopening to be a fresh top-level decision (never automatic). The whole G1->G2 sequence validates the anti-fake-yield architecture (fixed notional + blocking pre-flight reconcile): it caught a fake (+343% G1) and certified-then-honestly-rejected a real-but-thin (G2) — that architecture is the single most reusable asset for any future carry/basis research.

- 2026-05-16 G2-Auth-6 lesson — a non-economic FAIL driver can be empirically de-risked WITHOUT reopening the strategy: a pure data-precision gate (acquire official settlement, recompute the S5 ratio read-only with the corrected reference, same F_last) is in-scope and decisive (mean conv-err 1.60%->0.23%) while NOT a rerun (no engine/sim/v2/threshold). This cleanly separated "is S5 fixable?" (yes, ~7x) from "should G2 be reopened?" (still a separate fresh top-level decision; data sufficient to JUSTIFY != authorize/trigger). Reusable: when a closed honest-negative failed on a measurement/data criterion, a tightly-scoped data-only verification gate can confirm the criterion is instrumentation (not edge) before anyone commits to a costly amendment+rerun — keeps the open-ended-iteration trap closed while still gathering decision-grade evidence. Also: Binance keyless /futures/data/delivery-price returns only the recent ~17 quarterly deliveries (not the full back-history); earlier contracts need index-1m reconstruction (avg last 60 min pre-08:00 UTC, Binance's documented settlement rule) and the very earliest may be unavailable (210326 missing) — always probe coverage span first and document missing rather than impute. And restate the discipline: even favorable data does not retro-justify changing a locked criterion under a data gate; any S5/S8 change is a separate re-locked preregistration-amendment gate (G1-Auth-4->4A pattern).

- 2026-05-16 G2-Auth-7 lesson — the disciplined way to remediate non-economic FAIL drivers is a SINGLE explicitly-authorized preregistration-amendment gate that (a) changes ONLY the non-economic items (settlement reference + S8 float tolerance), (b) freezes the per-contract data source from a prior pinned snapshot so there is NO post-result source selection, (c) handles the one un-acquirable datum (210326) by a pre-committed data-driven EXCLUSION rather than a bespoke unvalidated reconstruction (special-casing a single point is itself a researcher DoF), (d) locks the criterion definition that has a known tail issue (S5 mean-vs-max) NOW so it cannot be switched post-hoc, and (e) hard-caps to ONE rerun with explicit NO-re-amendment finality to permanently close the open-ended-iteration trap. Justify any tolerance numerically by the gap between the observed artifact (4.27e-15) and the smallest real violation (~1e-4): pick a value orders above noise and orders below any real bug (1e-9). Reusable test for "is this an amendment or a rescue?": does it change any economic threshold/cost/notional/strategy, or change a number a passing run's P&L would produce? If no (here: settlement never enters P&L; S8 is vacuous) -> legitimate amendment, locked before rerun, falsifiability intact (G1-Auth-4->4A). Always restate the honest ceiling so a "READY" verdict is not misread as "about to profit": certification != deployment != money; a thin regime-fragile edge stays thin even when certified.

- 2026-05-16 G2-Auth-8 lesson — a clean PASS is the rarest outcome and demands MORE discipline, not less: report it without celebration, separate "passed a falsifiable preregistration" (true, historic for the program) from "deployable/profitable" (NOT: thin ~5.6pct/yr, ~92pct contango-bull-concentrated, single-symbol, behind anti_overfit>=3-symbols + 5 more gates). The pre-authorized engine change worked because it was (a) specced+locked in a prior gate (G2-Auth-7), (b) ADDITIVE + default-disabled so the frozen 38-test suite proves byte-identical legacy behaviour, (c) static-diff-bounded to exactly the authorized hunks, (d) re-tested AFTER applying to prove behaviour-preservation. That is the template for modifying a locked engine under an execution gate without breaking falsifiability: pre-authorize the exact diff, make it default-off, prove via the frozen test suite, disclose the sha delta. Confirmed: the two amendments were non-economic (settlement never enters gross P&L; S8 was a 4e-15 artifact) so the FAIL->PASS flip came purely from correcting measurement; economics moved ONLY by the pre-committed 210326 exclusion, exactly as G2-Auth-6 predicted; when you can predict the rerun outcome from prior analysis, the rerun is confirmation and the discipline question becomes "is confirming worth it". Standing rule reaffirmed: PASS != deploy; never auto-advance; downstream is always a fresh top-level decision.

- 2026-05-16 G2-Auth-10 lesson — a structural data-availability fact can be definitively settled cheaply BEFORE any acquisition: one complete (untruncated) keyless S3 listing of the um universe (843 symbols) conclusively answered "is there a 3rd dated symbol?" (no) — always probe the FULL authoritative listing first; it converts a months-long open question into a one-call fact and bounds the whole gate. Reusable data-integrity gotcha now seen for real: Binance public ARCHIVE timestamp units are NOT uniform — spot monthly klines switched openTime from milliseconds (13-digit) to MICROSECONDS (16-digit) in newer files; futures um dated files were still ms. Any archive ingestion MUST normalize timestamp units (detect digit-length; 16-digit -> //1000) BEFORE bucketing/joining, or cross-series metrics silently corrupt (here a bogus 70.6% coverage that initially looked like an ETH gap; and a fromtimestamp OSError exposed it). Bake unit-normalization into every future acquire_*/validate_* script. Also: when an instrument-class cap is STRUCTURAL (exchange simply does not offer the product), report it as final and resist substitution pressure (perp/COIN-M) — softening the frozen anti_overfit symbol_count or blending instrument classes to "reach 3" would manufacture a fake pass; the disciplined outcome is to accept the 2-symbol cap and conclude the line.

- 2026-05-16 G2 final-expansion-close lesson — the disciplined END of a multi-year research arc is a precise dual statement reported together without inflation: "strongest CERTIFIED result" AND "structurally NON-DEPLOYABLE, here is exactly why". A frozen gate (anti_overfit symbol_count>=3) that the available data structurally cannot satisfy is the gate WORKING, not an obstacle to engineer around; accepting the 2-symbol cap (vs softening/substituting/forcing a 3rd) is the integrity-preserving outcome and is itself a complete, valuable result. Generalizable closure pattern: when an instrument class structurally caps the study below a frozen robustness threshold, CLOSE the line with (a) the certified positive stated plainly, (b) the structural blocker proven by an authoritative census not a search, (c) explicit enumeration of every forbidden shortcut and confirmation none was used, (d) the honest "not deployable + why + what a NEW line would require", (e) memory updated so future sessions inherit "no deployable money-maker found program-wide; any restart is a fresh different-data-class line under R1-R6". The whole program's value was the discipline: zero capital risked on unproven/fake edges; G1 fake-yield caught; G2 honestly certified-then-capped.

- 2026-05-16 S/R planning lesson — "we never tested mechanic X" is NOT sufficient grounds to GO; the program's binding constraint is DATA SCOPE / no-economic-edge, not mechanic novelty. A new but directional, OHLC-only, no-cash-flow family on the exhausted BTC/ETH/SOL daily set is a forbidden-repeat (F-6) regardless of how clever/mechanizable the mechanic is, and recommending it would re-open the open-ended-iteration trap. Correct pattern for any "should we test new mechanic Y?" planning gate: do the full honest analysis (define it rigorously, mechanize it, score it) so the verdict is grounded not dismissive, then test it against restart R1-R6 + forbidden_repeat_patterns + the economic-edge axis — if it has no economic source AND adds no new data class, the disciplined answer is NO-GO even though the mechanic is novel. Reusable filter: novelty-of-mechanic is necessary-not-sufficient; the GO bar is (genuine economic edge) AND (new/edge-bearing data class) AND restart R1-R6, with the carry/basis line as the dominance benchmark.

- 2026-05-16 H1 lesson: for an integrity/anti-fake-yield data gate, environment provenance is part of data integrity. A TLS-intercepting proxy (cert verify fail) is disqualifying even though bytes might flow; "probably not tampered" is not acceptable provenance. Correct response is fail-closed + deliver tooling, never bypass verification or fabricate PENDING numbers.

## 2026-05-16 — H1-Auth-1 lessons
- Anomaly classification before judgement: SOL funding off_interval=101
  looked like a cadence defect; precise diagnosis (histogram + date
  localisation) showed 98x2h + 3x4h ALL within 2022-11-09..18 = the
  FTX-collapse week. Binance raises perp funding frequency during
  extreme volatility. ALWAYS localise an anomaly in time and decompose
  it before calling it a defect; a real captured economic event is the
  opposite of missing data (0 gaps/missing/dupes confirms denser, not
  corrupted).
- Strict-boolean honesty: a hard sufficiency boolean (here
  all_funding_8h_clean -> usable=false) must NOT be softened to flip
  the headline. Report the literal machine verdict AND the disclosed
  analyst reading side by side (same discipline as G2-Auth-5 honest
  FAIL, G1-Auth-4 escalate-not-silently-fix).
- REST vs archive timestamp units: the G2-Auth-10 us/ms archive hazard
  did NOT recur because H1 pulled exclusively from REST (uniform
  13-digit ms). Acquisition channel choice (REST vs data.binance.vision
  archive zips) directly determines whether the us-normalisation
  hazard applies.
- Perpetual-funding universe lifts the structural 3-symbol cap that
  permanently bounded the dated-futures arc (only BTC/ETH have USD-M
  dated chains). Same-class symbol availability is a property of the
  instrument class, not of effort: dated=2 max, perp>=3 feasible.

## 2026-05-16 — H1-Auth-2 lessons
- Reuse the certified template, do not reinvent: the G2
  fixed-accounting model + success/failure criteria + cost +
  invalidity docs are the program's proven anti-fake-yield asset. H1
  preregistration was built by adapting them to the perpetual /
  no-settlement / multi-symbol case (settlement-convergence ->
  basis/mark-drift; roll calendar -> funding-stamp accrual; single
  symbol -> 3-symbol basket with a single-symbol-dominance kill).
  Mirroring a certified design is faster AND more defensible than a
  fresh one.
- Lock known-defect conventions UPFRONT: G1 lost a whole correction
  gate (G1-Auth-4A) to a funding-sign contradiction discovered after
  results. H1 locks the Binance/L65 sign convention in the
  preregistration itself = zero sign DoF, no post-hoc flip possible.
- Carry-specific kill conditions a single-symbol prereg lacks: a
  multi-symbol basket needs an explicit single-symbol-dominance
  invalidity (GR-5, >70 pct of WA net from one symbol) or a 3-symbol
  basket that is really 1 symbol would pass while defeating the
  anti_overfit purpose.
- Preregistration readiness is conditional, not binary: "ready" =
  ready for a SEPARATE implementation gate, with the honest-prior
  caveat carried as a binding pre-commitment (a likely FAIL is an
  acceptable, expected outcome) so a thin/negative result is not later
  reframed as surprise or rescued.

## 2026-05-16 — H1-Auth-3 lessons
- Static validation must never import the engine: ast.parse +
  py_compile.compile only (both produce bytecode WITHOUT executing
  module code), and scan a tokenize stream with STRING+COMMENT tokens
  removed so safety docstrings ("no credential imports", "no
  order/trade placement") do not false-positive. This is the proven
  G1/G2 pattern and it held again here (all_pass=true, 0 false hits).
- Engine has zero write API on purpose: simulate/metrics return dicts;
  persistence is deferred to a future separately-authorized runner.
  This makes "no results produced / no v2 records" structurally true
  at the implementation gate, not merely promised.
- __main__ guard should actively refuse to run, not just be absent:
  the H1 engine __main__ prints an implementation-only refusal and
  exits, so even accidental execution computes nothing.
- Closed-form sizing removes a hidden DoF: equal-USD-notional under
  fixed C0 solved as U = C0 / sum (1+F/S)(1+feeslip) is deterministic,
  avoiding any iterative/discretionary capital allocation that could
  later be tuned.

## 2026-05-16 — H1-Auth-4 lessons
- Synthetic timestamp fixtures MUST be 8h-epoch-aligned for the perp
  funding engine: it buckets via round(t/8h)*8h and compares to raw
  kline openTime; an unaligned synthetic B0 makes the engine
  (correctly) skip every bucket and crash min() on an empty set. Real
  Binance funding/kline stamps are always 8h-aligned, so this is a
  fixture-domain requirement, not an engine bug. Reusable for any
  future perp-funding fixture.
- When a test and the engine disagree on a count, check whether the
  engine is implementing a LOCKED rule the test forgot: here 6212 vs
  6213 was the engine correctly folding the locked SOL
  incomplete-triplet skip into the shared window. Fix the test
  expectation (and assert the reconciliation), NEVER the engine -
  changing the engine to match the stale expectation would have
  broken a locked rule = a forbidden rescue. Same discipline as
  G2-Auth-4 (fix fixtures, not the engine).
- Importing an engine for unit tests is safe ONLY because H1-Auth-3
  statically proved no module-level execution and a refusing __main__;
  that static guarantee is what makes the unit-test gate non-executing
  by construction.

- 2026-05-16 When asked to extract ideas from an external trading video: if no transcript text is actually supplied, do NOT fabricate quotes or imply profitability — analyze only the explicitly-provided summary and say so. The durable lesson from such content is almost always the validation discipline (reproducible backtest + visible validation; reject black-box capital agents), NOT the promoted automation. Map every operational idea onto our evidence gates and default to RESEARCH_ONLY/BLOCKED rather than SAFE_NOW.

- 2026-05-16 Knowledge sync of trading research notes (decisions.md, next_actions.md, trading_lessons.md, trading_research/*) into Obsidian is safe ONLY as a sanitized one-way copy with a secret-skip gate and knowledge-only frontmatter. A vault is a notebook, never an execution path: no trade can originate from a synced note, and a note that looks secret-bearing is dropped whole rather than partially copied. Fail-closed when the vault is absent so a missing notebook can never silently degrade into "write somewhere else".

- 2026-05-16 Secret sanitizers must be precise, not just conservative. A skip-on-suspicion gate that flags ordinary prose (any 12+ lowercase words) and documented sha256 provenance hashes is technically "safe" but silently buries the most valuable knowledge (the decision log) and makes the feature useless. Right design: detect the ACTUAL shape of the secret (BIP39 mnemonic = standalone fixed-length short-word line; private key = long hex ADJACENT to a key/secret/wallet label) so a labelled integrity hash and English sentences pass while real credentials/keys/mnemonics still skip. Precision improvement != weakening, as long as every genuine-secret class is still caught and verified by a locked regression test.

- 2026-05-16 Adding a new outbound capability safely = replicate the existing audited-boundary pattern, never relax the global gate. The right move for Google/YouTube search was a SECOND single-file egress held to STRICTER positive constraints (fail-closed, allowlisted host, GET-only, secret never surfaced, dedicated behavioral verifier with the network fully mocked), with external_http still NEVER acknowledged for every other module. External trading "ideas" enter permanently quarantined as claims needing local verification — discovery is not evidence; an external mention can never become a high-confidence candidate or trigger an alert without the local evidence gates. Recurring lesson reaffirmed: the safety verifier scans RAW source, so even a comment that names a forbidden token (here `urllib.request` in an import comment) self-trips it — keep prose in safety-critical files literal-free.

- 2026-05-16 A fail-closed `except Exception: return []` with no observability is undiagnosable by construction. When a swallowed error path can also mean "no results" or "filtered", you cannot tell misconfiguration (Google CSE not web-scoped / API not enabled / bad key / quota) from genuinely-empty results.
