Fix = thread a secret-safe diagnostic accumulator (counts + sanitized error class/HTTP-status/reason codes, with any token-shaped substring redacted, and NEVER the keyed request URL or raw payload) so the next run states the exact cause. Also: normalization that runs OUTSIDE the try/except can crash the "never raises" boundary on an unexpected payload shape — guard shapes with isinstance and skip, don't trust the API to be well-formed.

- 2026-05-16 The YouTube-only external research stream is useful as a SCAM/CLICKBAIT filter signal but weak for serious research: trading-first top-10 = ~80% clickbait/noise, 1 AI-indicator hype-scam, only 1 genuinely useful item (anti-overfit / permutation-testing strategy-development methodology). Do not judge external-search value on a YouTube-only sample, and do not invest in promotion machinery (14D local notes) until higher-signal sources (papers/blogs/docs/GitHub via Google Custom Search) are actually flowing. Quarantine + human triage correctly kept all of it EXTERNAL_CLAIM_ONLY/NEEDS_VERIFICATION; the cheap win so far is teaching the junk filter, not collecting candidates.

- 2026-05-16 A preregistration is only as good as the fidelity of its locked input contract. Phase 14J locked placeholder CSV input paths before confirming the real frozen dataset's actual shape (Binance JSON dump); Phase 14K then correctly returned INVALID on the exact-path/provenance mismatch rather than adapting. Lesson: when authoring a preregistration, bind it to the ACTUAL data artifact paths/format verified by existence beforehand — but if a mismatch is discovered at run time, INVALID + a fresh preregistration is the integrity-preserving path; never retro-fit the sealed contract to the data. The harness behaved exactly as designed: honest INVALID, no fabricated PASS, no gate softening, trading stays PAUSED.

- 2026-05-16 End-to-end external-claim verification (Phases 14B->14M) on the GitHub funding-rate-arbitrage item resolved to a disciplined REJECT: under conservative, preregistered, hash-sealed cost assumptions the strategy never clears its own round-trip transaction cost (~60bps vs ~1bp/8h funding), so it makes zero trades and shows no edge OOS across BTC/ETH/SOL. Lesson reaffirmed: realistic fee+slippage modelling kills most "funding yield" claims before any alpha question; a preregistration that fixes costs honestly will reject thin-carry strategies by construction. The harness behaved exactly as designed across the whole arc — quarantine, static-only inspection, independent re-implementation, sealed preregistration, hash-bound single run, honest negative, no promotion, trading stays PAUSED.

- 2026-05-16 Name-shape data probes that AUTO-CONFIRM on the first filename
  match are fragile across time. The NQ/MNQ module set
  data_contract_status=CONFIRMED as soon as any nq/mnq-named path
  existed, so when the operator later staged C:\SPARTA_RESEARCH_LAB\nq_mnq_opening_range
  its prereg flipped out of NEEDS_DATA_CONTRACT and 2 of its tests
  broke with ZERO code change on that module. How to apply: a Phase-01
  preregistration-only data probe must treat name-shape hits as
  ADVISORY transparency only and keep
  data_contract_status=NEEDS_DATA_CONTRACT until a SEPARATE explicitly-
  authorized data-contract phase confirms exact symbols/fields/
  timestamp+OHLCV rules/sha256 provenance. crypto_regime_prereg.py
  implements this hardened design (name_shape_hits_confirm_a_contract
  =False; always NEEDS_DATA_CONTRACT in Phase 01) and stayed correct
  even with 50 name-shape hits present. When mirroring an existing arc
  module, copy structure but HARDEN the auto-confirm logic; never let
  path-shape existence alone seal or flip a preregistration verdict.

- 2026-05-16 An arc's own regression test must NOT assert the shared safety
  verifier's GLOBAL cross-arc status (sv["status"]). Under concurrent
  multi-arc development (a parallel agent building crypto_regime + the
  operator staging NQ data) the global aggregate flips transiently:
  test_sparta_commander_stat_arb_pair_prereg.py's first run hit one
  transient FAIL while standalone runs were 8/8 PASS, because a sibling
  arc's volatile environment momentarily contaminated the aggregate —
  and "fixing" it would require touching another arc, which is
  forbidden. How to apply: a new arc's safety regression test should
  assert ONLY what that arc owns and is deterministic — its module is
  registered, exists, has zero violations, contributes no violating
  file, and report-path isolation holds — never the cross-arc global
  PASS. This complements the name-shape-auto-confirm fragility lesson:
  both are about not coupling a new arc to volatile shared/global state.

- 2026-05-16 A data-contract discovery phase needs THREE distinct
  not-ready verdicts, not one. crypto_regime_data_contract_discovery
  separates NEEDS_DATA_CONTRACT (no arc-specific dataset exists at
  all -> one must be DEFINED and staged; sibling/look-alike folders
  are advisory-only and must NOT be reused) from NEEDS_DATA_FIX
  (an arc-specific dataset IS staged but fails shape/symbol/format/
  timeframe/frozen checks -> fixable) from INVALID (contradictory
  staging: the path is a file, or a filesystem error). The original
  NQ discovery collapsed the first two into NEEDS_DATA_FIX. How to
  apply: never let a superficially-named sibling folder (e.g.
  regime_detection_exp for a "regime" arc) satisfy a contract -
  classify every non-expected lab child OTHER_ARC_ADVISORY_ONLY,
  never descend into or hash it, and require the operator to stage a
  *named, arc-specific* frozen root before any READY is even
  possible. Discovery confirms existence/provenance only; it never
  parses bars and never infers a contract across arcs.

- 2026-05-17 The documented Phase-14B TLS-interception block also covers
  data.binance.vision (not just Google): this machine's proxy/AV
  injects an RFC-malformed CA so even the LEGITIMATE full-verification
  paths fail - OpenSSL rejects it ("Basic Constraints of CA cert not
  marked critical"); Windows-Schannel TRUSTS the chain but cannot
  check revocation (CRYPT_E_NO_REVOCATION_CHECK) because the proxy
  breaks OCSP/CRL. How to apply: for any external download on the
  SPARTA machine, expect this block; the correct response is to
  (a) build the fully-verifying downloader with NO insecure/
  verify=False/bypass option at all, (b) emit an honest
  NETWORK_BLOCKED_NOT_ACQUIRED manifest with zero fabricated bytes,
  and (c) surface the choice to the operator (clean network / disable
  HTTPS inspection / explicitly authorized revocation-only-but-still-
  chain-verified) rather than silently relaxing TLS. Never conflate
  "revocation freshness unverifiable" (chain still trusted) with
  "--insecure" (no trust) - but still do not relax even the milder
  one without explicit operator authorization.

- 2026-05-17 The SPARTA crypto-acquisition block is MULTI-LAYER, not just
  TLS. Operator re-ran crypto_regime_data_acquire.py --os-trust on
  SPARTA: the failure mode CHANGED from `SSL: CERTIFICATE_VERIFY_
  FAILED` (TLS handshake rejected) to `xml.etree ParseError:
  mismatched tag, line 6 col 2`. That ParseError means the HTTPS
  request SUCCEEDED and returned a body, but the body was a non-XML
  page (classic signature of a proxy/AV HTML block/interstitial page
  served instead of the Binance S3 listing XML) — i.e. the
  interception moved to the CONTENT layer even though the cert now
  verifies. Net result identical: NETWORK_BLOCKED_NOT_ACQUIRED, 0
  files, nothing fabricated; the script correctly refused to treat a
  block page as data. How to apply: on the SPARTA machine, "TLS now
  verifies" does NOT mean acquisition works — expect content-layer
  interception too; the only sound path remains Option A (run the
  unchanged safe downloader on a genuinely clean machine/network,
  verify sha256 vs published .CHECKSUM there, copy data+provenance+
  manifest back as a unit). Never add an insecure bypass; never
  fabricate; never parse a non-XML body as data.

- 2026-05-17T15:36:49 - No repeated issue was detected in parsed trade history; improve trade tagging before drawing stronger conclusions.

- 2026-05-17T15:36:49 - Parsed history shows 0 loss(es) out of 2 trade(s); focus review on losing clusters, not isolated trades.

- 2026-05-17 A backtest engine that recomputes nested rolling windows inline
  PER bar (here: a 336-deep reference loop each doing a 48-bar
  max/min, called per bar, per entry+exit, across 6 simulations ~
  O(10^9-10^10)) is non-completing on ~200k bars and will silently
  hang / auto-background. How to apply: precompute ALL rolling
  features ONCE per symbol into arrays (rolling sums for MAs,
  monotonic-deque for rolling max/min, single trailing pass for
  percentile/median), make the per-bar regime/signal O(1), and
  compute per-symbol state ONCE (reuse for both slippage settings) -
  do NOT call precompute inside the per-variant simulate. Discipline:
  a non-completing performance defect is NOT a "result to improve" -
  stop the stuck run (verify it wrote nothing + baselines intact),
  fix IMPLEMENTATION ONLY with params/thresholds/signal-logic/costs
  byte-identical, validate on synthetic data (independent reconcile
  must match), THEN the single authorized run (G2-Auth-4 precedent).
  Keep an independent two-path PnL reconcile as a hard gate so the
  verdict (here a clean REJECT) is provably real, not an artifact.

- 2026-05-17 LESSON: An output sanitizer must not rely on pattern ORDER — a broad phrase rule ("price target") consumed the token "target" before the numeric rule could fire, leaking a bare "$500"/"10x". How to apply: for safety sanitizers, add INDEPENDENT catch-all rules for the raw dangerous primitives themselves (bare $<num>, <num>x leverage) in addition to phrase rules, so no single replacement order can let a primitive survive. Also: a safety DISCLAIMER that legitimately negates forbidden language ("this is NOT a price prediction") will trip an over-broad test scan — scan only the CRITIQUE CONTENT fields, not meta/disclaimer fields (same class as the prose self-reference trap).

- 2026-05-17T15:45:33 - pytest lesson marker: read-only analytics before automation

- 2026-05-17T15:47:39 - No repeated issue was detected in parsed trade history; improve trade tagging before drawing stronger conclusions.

- 2026-05-17T15:47:39 - Parsed history shows 0 loss(es) out of 2 trade(s); focus review on losing clusters, not isolated trades.

- 2026-05-17T15:47:39 - Missing fields limit analysis quality: strategy, realized_r, expected_r should be logged for future trade reviews.

- 2026-05-17 LESSON: A "read-only" external MCP server is not read-only by default — the canonical TradingView MCP ships 78 tools where the majority mutate state and one (ui_evaluate) is arbitrary JS execution inside a paid logged-in desktop session, plus enabling CDP :9222 creates an unauthenticated local control surface any process can drive. How to apply: when wiring any third-party MCP, enumerate EVERY tool, classify read vs write, hard-DENY writes at the Claude Code permission boundary AND re-enforce a read-only allowlist in our own client code (defense in depth), time-box/close the debug surface, and never trust the vendor's "no broker / local-only" claim as sufficient — gate it behind our static-inspection + verifier pattern and a forbidden-field output validator before any execution.

- 2026-05-17 LESSON: A reusable "static inspection runner" can silently clobber another arc's artifact — scripts/run_external_static_inspection.py hardcodes its output to reports/external_research_hunter/phase14e_static_inspection.{json,md} (the funding-arb Hunter pack) regardless of which folder it inspects, because it calls generate_phase14e_pack(local_path=...) without overriding json_path/md_path. How to apply: before reusing any existing "run X on a folder" tool for a NEW target, trace its OUTPUT paths, not just its input/safety flags; if the writer supports explicit output-path args (this module's _p()/generate_phase14e_pack do), invoke the audited FUNCTION directly with target-specific paths instead of the convenience runner, and never edit the audited module just to relabel output — document the provenance caveat instead.

- 2026-05-17 LESSON: An operator's "it is staged" assertion must be filesystem-verified before any scan — here the authorized path (and any *tradingview* folder / SOURCE.txt) was entirely absent under external_repos_static\ despite being reported as staged. Compounding trap: the audited scanner's inspect_local_path returns inspected=True (and the pack reports "TEXT_ONLY_SCAN_COMPLETE") even when the target path does NOT exist (the scan loop is guarded by `if base.exists():` but the inspected flag is set purely from `local_path is not None`). How to apply: before invoking generate_phase14e_pack, hard-check Path(local_path).exists() AND that it is non-empty; on absence, fail closed with NEEDS_OPERATOR_FIX and DO NOT write a scan pack (it would falsely read as a completed 0-file scan) — only write the honest risk report, mirroring the SPARTA NEEDS_DATA_CONTRACT/NOT_RUN pattern.

- 2026-05-17 LESSON (recurrence): the prose self-reference trap struck again — an isolation test that raw-text-scanned a module's source for forbidden tokens ("from sparta_commander", "strategy_lab", "review_queue", "eval(") false-FAILED because the module's own honest SAFETY DOCSTRING legitimately names exactly what it must NOT import. How to apply: security/isolation tests that assert "module does not import/forbidden-call X" must parse the AST (ast.Import/ImportFrom module roots + ast.Call func names + os.system attribute) NOT grep raw text, so docstrings/comments that describe the guarantee cannot break the test that enforces it. Same class as the earlier sanitizer-ordering / disclaimer-scan traps: scan the CODE SEMANTICS, never the prose that documents the safety property. Module code stayed correct; only the over-broad test was fixed.

- 2026-05-17 LESSON (3rd recurrence, now codified): the prose self-reference trap reappears whenever a SAFETY artifact must honestly NAME the very things it forbids. Phase 3B's disabled MCP template legitimately says "_authorizes: NOTHING…does not edit ~/.claude/.mcp.json", "_env_note: no API key/token/secret/credential" — and an over-broad test value-scan + a long-token entropy regex false-FAILED on those honest fields and on long permission identifiers. How to apply (general rule now): when validating a config/JSON safety artifact, partition fields into DOCUMENTATION (keys starting with `_` or ending `_note`/`_authorizes`) vs OPERATIVE, and scan ONLY operative fields for forbidden tokens/secrets; never use a blanket high-entropy/long-token regex on a file whose legitimate content is long identifiers/permission patterns. Same family as: AST-based import isolation tests (not raw grep), and scanning critique-content not disclaimer fields. The artifact stayed correct every time; only the over-broad TEST was fixed.

- 2026-05-17 LESSON: when a "perform the read" phase is requested but the read is impossible without crossing a hard boundary (no MCP server/transport registered; would require forbidden install/clone/.mcp.json/CDP changes), the ONLY correct move is fail-closed ABORT + honest NOT_RUN artifact — never fabricate the observation to make the phase "succeed". How to apply: verify preconditions read-only FIRST (config/tool-registry/transport flags), map them against the explicit abort conditions, and if unmet emit a NOT_RUN record with empty/null data fields + an explicit "no read performed" context; still run the safe local part that proves the control works (here: route tool names through firewall.guard() to produce a real deny-by-default trace) so the phase yields evidence without breaching scope. Inventing chart data to satisfy the request would be the cardinal failure ([[feedback_no_hype_trades]]); the disciplined abort IS the win, exactly like the crypto-regime/funding-arc honest negatives.

- 2026-05-17 LESSON: a multi-agent trading framework can be fully evaluated for architecture-borrowing via READ-ONLY public-repo web inspection (README + package tree) — no clone/install/run needed, which keeps SPARTA's static-only discipline intact while still yielding a grounded role/graph/debate/memory map. How to apply: for "study this repo as an architecture reference" tasks, prefer web read of README + directory tree + key module names over cloning; that is sufficient to compare against our architecture and to separate borrowable IDEAS (firm decomposition, adversarial debate, risk red-team, manager memo, decision memory) from forbidden MECHANISMS (execution/simulated-exchange/auto-promotion/live-data keys). Borrow ideas re-implemented under our gates; never integrate a framework that ships an execution path.

- 2026-05-17 LESSON: bash heredocs (`python - <<'PY'`) for sealed-design generators are fragile on this Windows/bash when the body contains quotes/regex/separators — they fail with "unexpected EOF looking for matching quote". How to apply: for any hash-sealed report generator, do NOT pipe a heredoc; Write a transient stdlib .py to tmp/, run it with the venv python, independently re-derive the seal from the written file (stored==recompute), then delete the generator (no residue). This both avoids the quoting trap and gives a built-in seal self-verification step (same proven crypto-regime "temp generator created/run/deleted" pattern).

- 2026-05-17 LESSON: A web-only inspection of an external repo produced a MATERIAL FACTUAL ERROR — it claimed TradingAgents ships a "simulated exchange / order executed" flow, when a direct read-only clone + source grep of v0.2.5 (commit 61522e1) shows NO broker/order/exchange/place_order/submit_order/create_order symbol anywhere, .propagate() returns (final_state, parsed_rating) not an order, and the LangGraph terminates at Portfolio Manager -> END. The error was in the *cautious* direction but still wrong, and it mis-stated the actual disqualifier (epistemic/governance risk, not an execution path). How to apply: for any "evaluate an external repo" task, prefer an isolated read-only clone + AST/grep over the actual pinned commit to README/web/paper prose; treat README/paper architecture descriptions as EXTERNAL_CLAIM_ONLY/NEEDS_VERIFICATION (older docs often describe a "simulated exchange" the current code dropped); always record commit SHA + the exact negative-finding search terms as evidence. Same family as the TradingView "operator's 'it is staged' must be filesystem-verified" and "scan code semantics not prose" lessons: verify against the artifact, never its description.
- 2026-05-17 LESSON: When the deliverable path already holds a file you did NOT create and its content contradicts your source-verified findings, the overwrite-safety rule applies — surface the specific discrepancy (with evidence) and ask the operator rather than silently overwriting; "keep both side by side" (retain the superseded artifact + a correction notice/addendum) preserves provenance without leaving a false claim as canonical. How to apply: never silently clobber a non-self-authored report; a parallel session may have produced it — diff conclusions vs basis, escalate the factual conflict, let the human choose.


## 2026-05-17 — Validator must not assume one timestamp serialization
- The Step-2B file was written by the DEPRECATED parallel tool via
  pandas df.to_csv(), so ts_event is 'YYYY-MM-DD HH:MM:SS+00:00'
  (space-separated, +00:00), NOT the 'YYYY-MM-DDT...Z' form the
  canonical tool's DBNStore.to_csv(pretty_ts) would have produced.
- v1 validator hard-coded the ISO-T parser -> every row failed ->
  first_ts=None -> crash. Fix: normalize T->space, slice [:19],
  strptime '%Y-%m-%d %H:%M:%S'; tz check accepts +00:00 OR trailing Z.
- Lesson: when validating data produced by a different tool than the
  canonical one, INSPECT the actual on-disk format (read-only) before
  writing parsers; support both serializations defensively.

- 2026-05-17 LESSON: two recurring TEST-ONLY false-failure classes hit again while building the SRFB scaffold; both confirmed the SAFETY LOGIC was correct and only the test/scope was over-broad. (1) Windows Path.write_text translates \n->\r\n, so a fixture that hashes content.encode() but writes via write_text produces hash != on-disk bytes -> the sha256 gate CORRECTLY fires sha256_mismatch. Fix: fixtures that feed a hash-checker must write_bytes(raw) and hash the SAME raw bytes (never write_text for hashed fixtures). (2) A path/token guard that scans the whole ABSOLUTE path false-trips because pytest names its tmp dir after the test function (e.g. test_no_review_queue_... -> ancestor contains 'review_queue'). Fix: scope forbidden-token scans to the CALLER-CONTROLLED portion (path relative to the allowed base) while keeping containment on the absolute path. Same family as the AST-not-grep and prose-self-reference traps: scan the operative/controlled surface, never the incidental wrapper.


## 2026-05-17 - Concurrent sessions corrupt the single-truth assumption
- Two sessions worked the same C:\SPARTA_RESEARCH_LAB
q_mnq_
  opening_range tree. The other session OVERWROTE the shared Step-3
  report with a different methodology -> opposite freeze decision.
  An authorization premised on a prior result can be silently
  invalidated by a parallel writer.
- Always RE-READ the actual on-disk artifact before confirming a
  premised status; never confirm from memory/summary. If on-disk
  contradicts the stated premise: surface it, do not fabricate the
  confirmation, do not overwrite the other session's file, proceed
  only with the conservative (stricter) interpretation + explicit
  conflict disclosure.
- Tooling: Glob silently returned 'No files found' for this lab path
  (not in the Glob working-dir allowlist) while the files plainly
  existed. Use Bash `ls`/`test -f` to enumerate non-primary lab
  trees; do not trust an empty Glob there as ground truth.

- 2026-05-17 LESSON: distinguish a BINDING seal from an INDEPENDENT CONTENT seal in multi-phase sealed pipelines. A phase report that sets report_seal_sha256 to the prior phase's design seal is a deliberate chain-binding reference, NOT tamper-evidence of its own bytes - and that ambiguity should be made explicit BEFORE later phases depend on it. How to apply: every phase report should (a) re-derive+echo the immutable upstream binding seal (mismatch=>abort) AND (b) carry its own file-content sha256; when a prior report conflated them, clarify ADDITIVELY (new addendum + computed content digests + a self-sealed convention doc) and never rewrite the already-published report (preserve its bytes; the addendum verifies them unchanged).


## 2026-05-17 - Independently re-verify cross-session seals; don't rubber-stamp
- Asked to 'confirm seal verifies', I recomputed sha256 over each
  JSON minus the seal field (standard convention). Step-4 verified;
  the Step-3 reconciliation addendum's seal did NOT reproduce. Always
  independently recompute - never accept a claimed seal at face
  value, and report a non-reproducing seal honestly rather than
  asserting 'verifies'.
- Separate the SUBSTANTIVE conclusion from the HISTORICAL claim: the
  gap reclassification was sound even though the addendum's 'never
  persisted' history was imprecise. Reconcile additively - preserve
  the conservative artifact, record supersession, flag imprecisions,
  do not overwrite or re-litigate an operator-accepted outcome.
- Minor tooling: do not leave a heredoc terminator token (e.g. a
  bare 'PY') inside Write-tool Python file CONTENT; it executes as
  code and NameErrors. Harmless only because it was the last line
  after all writes; still avoid.

- 2026-05-17 LESSON (reinforced): a "draft X" request whose deliverable ALREADY EXISTS sealed must trigger surface-evidence-and-ASK, never silent overwrite/regenerate - regenerating a sealed prereg destroys its immutable hash and creates a competing artifact. How to apply: before writing to a sealed-artifact path, glob/stat the target; if a sealed file exists, read+verify it (string-equality of the hash to the authoritative expected value, internal consistency prereg==report_seal, upstream seal bindings, required sections, plus record raw-file sha256 as tamper-evidence) and emit an ADDITIVE verification addendum only. Also: an empty/absent seal_method is a real documentation gap - inability to re-derive a hash by standard methods is NOT proof of tampering when the value matches the authoritative expected string and bindings are intact; report it honestly as DOCUMENTATION_GAP and recommend the next checklist lock the exact seal_method (same binding-vs-content-seal convention lesson as the SRFB Phase-2 clarification). Path note: native Windows python.exe cannot open Git-Bash /c/... paths - use C:/... ; bash builtins (stat/ls) accept /c/.. so cross-check carefully before concluding "file missing".


## 2026-05-17 - 'Hash matches expected' != 'independently re-derivable'
- Step-5 prereg report_seal/prereg_hash textually equals the
  operator-stated expected value (the asked confirmation) yet does
  NOT reproduce under SPARTA's standard canonicalization. Report
  BOTH facts distinctly: (a) stated == expected (confirmation
  satisfied), (b) std-convention recompute differs (operator tool
  uses a different canonicalization; non-blocking; read-only; not
  tampering). Never collapse (a) into a false 'cryptographically
  verified'.


## 2026-05-18 - CME Trading-Hours export is forward-window only
- The cmegroup.com Trading-Hours export returns populated rows only
  for a recent/forward window; historical-date cells come back
  BLANK even for normal trading days. It is NOT a multi-year
  holiday/early-close source (confirms the earlier acquisition-
  options finding empirically). For historical calendar evidence
  use the official CME holiday calendar PDF/printable, not the
  Trading-Hours export.
- Reading .xlsx via stdlib zipfile+ElementTree (resolve
  sharedStrings, map A1 refs) is a reliable no-dependency way to
  extract exact cell text as evidence - preferable to a library
  that could reinterpret values.


## 2026-05-18 - Verify referenced input filenames against disk
- The task referenced gate2_39_date_filled_csv_preparation_report
  .json and gate2_calendar_source_inventory.csv; neither existed
  under those names. Always enumerate the dir and confirm exact
  filenames before 'reading' them; disclose absent/renamed inputs
  honestly and use the real on-disk artifacts rather than assuming
  the requester's names are correct.


## 2026-05-18 - INTEGRITY EVENT: scaffold from immutable source, not mutable
- My first this-turn run produced a FALSE GATE2_SATISFIED. Root
  cause: a concurrent session overwrote FILLED.csv (18b3668e/10:58
  -> f8e0cbf3/11:11) relabeling 29 NEEDS_OPERATOR_REVIEW as
  EXCLUDED; my carry-forward predicate (classification !=
  NEEDS_OPERATOR_REVIEW) then treated EXCLUDED as evidence-backed
  => all-39/satisfied. Caught at verification (impossible
  'export=32'), corrected: rebuilt from the IMMUTABLE template +
  intact source_inventory.csv + the PDFs.
- Lessons: (1) build derived artifacts from an immutable/own-
  verified source, never a mutable file another session can rewrite;
  (2) an allow-list predicate ('is it evidence?') beats a deny-list
  ('is it NOT needs-review?') - a new label (EXCLUDED) silently
  passed the deny-list; (3) always re-verify the input hash you
  think you're consuming before consuming it; (4) only overwrite my
  OWN erroneous same-turn outputs - never the concurrent session's
  file; flag the divergence for human reconciliation.


## 2026-05-18 - OTC advisory != futures-session evidence; verify the binding-map covers prior dates
- An OTC Holiday Advisory ('CME Clearing open to clear OTC trades')
  does NOT establish CME equity-index FUTURES Globex closure -
  classify SECONDARY_OTC_EVIDENCE and keep NEEDS_OPERATOR_REVIEW;
  never upgrade to FULL on OTC alone. Settlement-times notices give
  the SETTLEMENT time (12:00 CT) not the Globex trading close
  (12:15 CT=13:15 ET) - record both, op_verified=false for the
  cross-referenced time.
- Counting-guard caught a real omission: the binding map initially
  missed a previously-bound date (2022-06-20); the assert
  (np==29) failed BEFORE any file was written, so nothing wrong
  was persisted. Lesson: keep a hard conjunctive count assert
  before writing, and when rebuilding a full map re-include
  ALL previously-bound dates, not just the new batch.

- 2026-05-18 LESSON (Step-5A OR-breakout closed negative): the full sealed gate
  chain WORKED and correctly produced an honest REJECT, but the deliberately-hard
  CHEAP checks (monthly / OR-range-decile / regime concentration; walk-forward per
  window) were what killed it — they should run in a lightweight non-promotable
  Tier-1 triage BEFORE the heavy chain (triage framework now authored). Also: an
  OOS-positive headline that survives economic-threshold + alternate splits +
  cost-stress can still be a concentrated/regime-dependent non-edge; NQ/MNQ are
  correlated (effective N=1) so "both positive" is not independent confirmation.
  And: brain_memory drifted far behind the sealed on-disk truth because controller
  sessions deliberately did not update it — reconcile memory promptly (or future
  sessions act on a stale picture). How to apply: prefer cheap rejection first;
  treat sealed on-disk artifacts as authoritative; keep one session per folder;
  never fabricate a rule to satisfy a run (the disciplined INCONCLUSIVE/REJECT is
  the win, per [[feedback_no_hype_trades]]).

- 2026-05-18 LESSON (H5 lead-quality gate): technical lead discovery must NOT
  allow shallow / clickbait title-link-snippet leads to advance. Shallow Brave/
  YouTube/GitHub-metadata leads cannot produce rule-complete strategies (S-chain
  synthesis = 0 hypotheses; H4 = 0 advanced of 17). Only serious CODE_SOURCE/
  PAPER_SOURCE candidates with explicit rules, methodology evidence, cost
  awareness, data availability, rejected-memory clearance, and operator
  attestation should ever be staged. How to apply: separate "operator believes
  this is worth a human look" from "system is allowed to extract it" — the latter
  (H3e) stays a distinct, separately-authorized step; require operator-staged H5
  validation BEFORE any extraction discussion; keep weak corpora honestly at zero
  candidates rather than forcing advancement (per [[feedback_no_hype_trades]]).

- 2026-05-18T23:53:30 - No repeated issue was detected in parsed trade history; improve trade tagging before drawing stronger conclusions.

- 2026-05-19 LESSON (full-suite run mutated a protected file): "Run the full
  discoverable suite" is NOT a safe instruction when the suite contains tests
  that exercise REAL build paths writing protected artifacts (here
  sparta_commander external_finding_review tests overwrote the live
  review_queue.json, and the in-repo isolation guard
  test_tests_cannot_write_the_real_review_queue is itself broken/FAILING). A
  protected-file no-mutation boundary can be violated indirectly via a test
  suite even when the agent never writes the file directly. How to apply: before
  running any broad suite under a no-mutation boundary, (1) enumerate which tests
  touch protected paths and deselect them, or run in an isolated copy/tmp; (2)
  snapshot+verify the protected file's sha BEFORE and AFTER and STOP + surface
  immediately on any change (done here); (3) treat conflicting instructions
  ("run full suite" vs "do not mutate X") as a contradiction to resolve by
  scoping, not by hoping isolation works; (4) never rely on an in-repo guard
  test you have not just verified passing. Honest disclosure of the breach and
  halting unilateral remediation is the correct behaviour (per
  [[feedback_no_hype_trades]] / operating_rules surface-contradictions).

- 2026-05-19 Env-var auth failures on Windows: a User-scope key change does
  NOT reach an already-running process or its children (env block is copied
  at process creation). Boolean presence can be True while the in-process
  value is the stale/old key -> persistent 401 that key "replacement" alone
  does not fix. The only reliable remediation is a full process restart (or
  same-session $env: set before launch); the only reliable proof is a
  successful authenticated round-trip (get_cost returning a number), not a
  presence check. Verified here: PID 35468 -> 17916, 401 -> success.

- 2026-05-19 Don't derive a CASH-EQUITY session calendar from FUTURES data.
  CME equity-index futures (NQ) keep trading a shortened Globex session on
  days the cash-equity RTH is fully closed (Presidents'/Memorial/Juneteenth/
  Jul-4/Labor/Thanksgiving) and can close before the 09:30 ET RTH window
  (Good Friday 08:15 CT). A futures-bar-presence rule will systematically
  call those HALF_DAY/anomalous, never FULL_HOLIDAY -> fail-closed 18-anchor
  cross-validation correctly catches it. Use the official CME equity Holiday
  Schedule documents as the calendar authority; reserve futures data for
  intraday session-shape, not holiday classification. Also: window-batch
  Databento pulls + reuse-cached resumable recovery is the right pattern for
  transient 504s (no rule change, no parallel/loop retry).

- 2026-05-19 (Break-and-Bounce post-mortem - Hunter Brain learns):
  verifier-VALID + sealed spec is NECESSARY but NOT SUFFICIENT - trigger
  frequency + data feasibility decide the diagnostic. Calendar-complexity-
  cost is a real budget item that can consume more turns than the
  diagnostic itself (S2.v2/v3 + I3/I4/I5R1-4 chain). Conjunctive subjective
  candle patterns + multi-timeframe retests + narrow entry windows + many-
  gate ANDs = low trigger frequency by construction. Bounded S2a-derivation-
  cluster 1m corpus is NOT a substitute for continuous intraday data; future
  Tier-1 candidates must declare data-coverage requirements upfront. Shallow
  sources (Brave/YouTube title+snippet) cannot manufacture rules - empirically
  confirmed by S4 synthesis dry-run (141 records -> 0 hypotheses). Rules
  live in code (GitHub/QuantConnect) and explicit papers (arXiv); deprioritize
  shallow narrative sources. Failed-fast is GOOD - converting B&B into
  permanent rejected-memory + warning-labels + prechecks is more valuable
  than the rejection itself.

- 2026-05-19 (Regime Intelligence Layer Phase 1 build): Building an additive
  read-only intelligence module is much cheaper than touching live trading
  logic. The 4 mandatory safety labels (EXTERNAL_CLAIM_ONLY,
  NEEDS_VERIFICATION, NO_TRADE_SIGNAL, NO_EXECUTION_PERMISSION) belong on
  every output of every advisory layer - they survive copy/paste into chat,
  PRs, and dashboards in a way that prose disclaimers do not. The
  fail-closed output-path check (refuse to write anywhere whose final segment
  is not regime_intelligence/) is a tiny amount of code that prevents an
  entire class of accidental cross-module writes. AST-level safety scans
  on the module's own .py files (no broker/order/execute SDK imports, no
  network imports, no forbidden call identifiers) are robust to docstrings
  that legitimately mention the policy keywords - much better than naive
  text greps. Walk-forward leakage protection by explicit prefix slicing
  (and asserting no classified index exceeds the current step) is simpler
  and more auditable than a time-aware DataFrame; for an intelligence layer
  this is the right level of rigor. Stickiness banding thresholds
  (medium>=0.45, high>=0.70) chosen so that a fair-coin-between-3-states
  base rate (~0.33) lands in "low" - keeps the labels meaningful instead
  of producing high-stickiness reports on random walks.

2026-05-19 - LESSON: An idea-memory schema is the right place to encode the
  discipline learned from a real rejection. The Break-and-Bounce closure
  produced 4 warning labels, 2 prechecks, 1 hold-gate, 1 rejected-memory
  record - all enforced at runtime in M4R1/M4R2. S2 lifts that
  enforcement up to the *shape* of every stored idea: rule fields must
  be present-as-keys (missing fact -> honest 'unknown', never invented);
  M4R1 enrichment must be present-as-keys; promotion/live-signal fields
  fail-closed; verdict domain deliberately omits any PASS outcome. Once
  this lives in the schema, no later phase can accidentally bypass it -
  not by dropping a field, not by relabelling, not by adding a
  'promote_to' key. The discipline becomes structural, not procedural.
  Additive design preserved the legacy S1 schema byte-equivalent and
  kept 18/18 legacy tests green, so nothing already depending on S1
  breaks. The 'present-as-keys with explicit "unknown"' pattern is the
  honest way to record gaps: it makes the gap visible in JSONL,
  searchable, and impossible to confuse with an actual rule. Default to
  this pattern whenever a schema represents partial knowledge that may
  later be filled by extraction.

2026-05-19 - LESSON: A schema/grader/preflight chain that has only been
  tested on tiny synthetic unit fixtures still needs an end-to-end
  rehearsal on a mixed-realism corpus before the operator runs any real
  source. The S2C dry-run discovered two useful signals: (1) the
  CALENDAR_COMPLEXITY_COST warning label fires liberally on candidates
  where calendar_semantics is ambiguous, not just on the cash-RTH-on-
  futures trap - this is the right side to err on, but the label is now
  understood to mean 'calendar deserves scrutiny' rather than
  'definitely the B&B trap'. (2) The B&B resubmission was caught by
  candidate_id match alone, before any of the rule heuristics had to
  fire - which is the strongest possible signal that rejected-memory
  works as designed. Lesson: when you have rejected-memory, set the
  candidate_id deterministically based on strategy_family so identical
  ideas under different titles still match. Lesson: hold-gate
  downgrades-but-doesn't-reject the arXiv-style fixture (correct
  behaviour) - this distinguishes 'we don't know yet' from 'this is
  wrong', which is what makes the M4R1 grader useful for prioritization
  rather than just filtering.

- 2026-05-19 (Regime Intelligence Layer Phase 2 build): Path-bounded
  loaders are a small amount of code with a large safety surface - one
  Path.resolve().relative_to(FROZEN_INPUTS_DIR.resolve()) check makes
  the entire module immune to "accidentally read the wrong file" and
  to symlink-escape paths. SHA-256 of the source CSV in every report is
  cheap (64KiB chunked) and lets a reviewer reproduce results months
  later without needing to remember which version of which file
  produced the report. Sorting + duplicate-timestamp rejection (instead
  of "deduplicate silently") catches operator mistakes loudly: silent
  dedup masks the kind of off-by-one CSV-merge bugs that look fine
  until walk-forward statistics start drifting. The "render a Source
  data section only when source_csv_name is present" pattern lets
  Phase 2 enrich Phase 1 reports without changing Phase 1 tests or
  callers - additive-only metadata is cheaper than versioning the
  report schema. Putting a local .gitignore inside the operator
  drop-zone (allow .gitignore + README.md, ignore everything else) is
  more discoverable than editing the root .gitignore - the operator
  reads the folder they are putting files into. Test helpers that
  generate dates from datetime + timedelta avoid an entire class of
  "2024-01-32 is invalid" off-by-one bugs that string formatting
  produces; the loader caught it correctly via unparseable-timestamp,
  which doubled as a fortuitous integration test of the fail-closed
  path.

- 2026-05-19 (Regime Intelligence Phase 3A staging utility build): A
  staging utility that imports the production loader and re-loads its own
  output as a self-check is a tight feedback loop: any subtle drift
  between the writer's format and the reader's expectations fails loudly
  the same turn the writer is changed. Cheaper than maintaining a
  separate "writer schema" alongside the reader. Self-bootstrapping the
  repo root into sys.path at the top of a tools/ script is a small
  amount of code that makes `python tools/foo.py` work from any CWD
  without forcing operators to remember PYTHONPATH or `python -m`
  conventions. Use `Path(__file__).resolve().parents[1]` to avoid CWD
  dependence. Validating asset/timeframe through a strict regex
  (`[A-Za-z0-9._-]+`) AND an explicit reject of `.` / `..` covers both
  filename-injection paths and an edge case the regex alone would let
  through. Hashing the source before and after the run and asserting
  equality is a one-line invariant that proves "read-only with respect
  to the source" in a way that is auditable rather than aspirational.
  Refusing in-place overwrite when input and output paths resolve to the
  same file is a separate check from "output already exists" — they sound
  similar but cover different operator mistakes (the second protects
  against silent data loss when the operator points the tool at a
  previously staged file with the same target name; the first protects
  against destructive `--overwrite` on the source itself).

2026-05-19 - LESSON: when an operator-facing schema must be parsed by internal graders that use a different taxonomy, the cleanest design is a small explicit data-only mapping inside the orchestrator (here: github/quantconnect/tradingview -> CODE_SOURCE, arxiv -> PAPER_SOURCE, youtube_transcript -> VIDEO + operator_notes alias to operator_rationale). This kept the driver pure-stdlib while still letting the H4 grader fire on the right code-paths. Lesson: credential leakage prevention is structural - the recursive credential scanner counts hits but NEVER returns the matched substrings, so even if a caller dumps the result dict to a log or ships it to telemetry, no secrets escape. Lesson: the dispatch-injected pattern (M4R2, now S2E) makes module isolation enforceable by AST scan; test_driver_does_not_import_any_domain_module is a one-line proof that the deny-by-default contract holds. Lesson: a canary-file source_url test (point the URL at a path on disk that does not exist; assert it stays absent) is a clean proof that the driver does not fetch. Cheaper than reading the source to look for fetcher imports, and survives future code changes automatically.

- 2026-05-19 (Regime Intelligence Phase 3B Binance public klines build):
  Restricting the entire network surface to one file (the fetcher), keeping
  sparta_regime_intelligence byte-unchanged, and confining urllib to that
  single file is a small architectural decision that makes the safety
  story trivial to verify: AST scans on the package keep passing, and the
  fetcher's own AST + source-literal scans cover the only place where
  network actually happens. URL safety is much more robust when you
  normalize the URL (lowercase + strip every non-alphanumeric) before
  substring-matching against forbidden fragments - "apiKey", "api_key",
  "api-key", "API KEY" all collapse to "apikey" and one rule catches
  them all. Always include BOTH "signed" AND "signature" - they share a
  prefix but neither is a substring of the other; missing one is a real
  hole (caught by the test failure on first run). Autouse "ban real
  network" fixture (replace _http_get_json with a raising stub) is
  cheap insurance: a test that forgets to inject a fake errors out
  loudly instead of silently making real HTTP calls during pytest. The
  duplicate-ISO-date check after dedup catches a class of upstream-bug
  where a "1d" interval response unexpectedly includes intraday bars -
  output stays canonical or fails closed, never produces a corrupt CSV.
  Detecting "no env / no credential leaks" via a small set of source-
  literal substring checks (`X-MBX-APIKEY`, `load_dotenv`, `API_KEY`,
  `Authorization:`, `Bearer `, `import hmac`, `hmac.new`, `.env`) is a
  pragmatic alternative to trying to fully prove "the tool reads no
  secrets" - any future refactor that introduces a signed-request code
  path fails the test loudly. Pinning symbol to BTCUSDT and interval to
  1d in this phase (even with default arg values) is intentional scope
  control: future phases can add more symbols/intervals with their own
  separate authorizations.

2026-05-19 - LESSON: deny-by-default fail-closed is a VALUE-PRODUCING outcome, not an error. The S3 dry-run hit the structure gate exactly as designed and produced a sealed report explaining (a) why the batch was rejected, (b) what the operator needs to change to make a future run meaningful, (c) byte-proof that no production state was touched, no URL was fetched, no schedule enabled, no Telegram sent. The system caught the placeholder-only batch BEFORE any S2 canonicalization or preflight assessment could run. Lesson: when an operator-facing template file ships with placeholder strings, the deny-by-default driver gate is the right place to surface the "this is still a template" signal - faster than letting placeholder content flow through canonicalization and produce a HOLD-only outcome that the operator then has to debug. Lesson: separate "structural failure" (file is a list, not a dict) from "content failure" (the records are placeholders) in the report - they require different operator actions. Lesson: always include the operator-action-required-to-proceed checklist in a fail-closed report so the operator does not have to read the driver source to figure out the contract.

2026-05-19 - LESSON: when an operator says they corrected a file and the diff shows only cosmetic renaming (PASTE_*_HERE -> PASTE_REAL_*) without filling in real content, the fail-closed gates catch it. The S2 schema required-present gate (strategy_family/provenance_seal/producing_run_seal) fired on every record - a different gate than the prior structure-gate failure, but the same posture: reject fast, record honestly, do not invent. The staged outputs are still written (input snapshot, intake memory JSONL with canonical-but-invalid records, sealed preflight, empty survivors, full rejected list) because the BATCH passed input validation - per-record S2 failures are recorded per-item rather than failing the whole batch. This gives the operator a paper trail of "here are the canonical record_ids your candidates WOULD have had, here are the exact fields each one is missing" - much more useful than a single fail-closed shrug. Lesson: report cosmetic-only corrections honestly. Better to point out that PASTE_REAL_* is still a placeholder than to silently let it through and produce a HOLD-only outcome the operator then has to debug.

- 2026-05-20 (Regime Intelligence Phase 3D parameter sensitivity sweep -
  empirical findings from real BTCUSDT 2023-2025 frozen CSV):
  Single-setting regime classifications at boundary returns are unreliable
  proxies for "current state" - the BTCUSDT 2025-12-31 "bear" call at
  lookback=20/thr=±0.05 with rolling return -5.26% flips to "sideways"
  the moment the threshold widens to ±0.07. Operator-facing reports
  should always be accompanied by a sensitivity table, not a single
  setting, when the rolling return sits within ~30% of the threshold
  boundary. Stickiness as a qualitative property is more robust than a
  specific regime call: across all 12 settings, no regime ever dropped
  out of the medium-or-high band, and 6/12 kept all three regimes in
  the high band - so "BTCUSDT daily regimes persist when classified at
  daily resolution" survives the sensitivity sweep even though the
  exact current-day label does not. The "bull and bear never flip
  directly, always via sideways" property is NOT a property of the
  market - it's a property of the LONG-WINDOW classifier. At lookback=10
  with tight +/-3% thresholds, the data does show small but non-zero
  direct flip probabilities (up to ~1.6%). This is a useful negative
  result for future analytical claims: don't quote "P(bull->bear)=0"
  without quoting the lookback that produced it. Writing the sweep tool
  with unique per-run filename stems (lb<N>_thr<P>pct_<batch_ts>) was
  necessary because UTC-second-resolution timestamps collide for 12
  rapid sequential calls - a small papercut you only catch when you
  actually run the sweep. Embedding the same _TEST_REPORT_DIR override
  hook the Phase 2 runner uses means the sweep tool naturally redirects
  output during tests with zero extra wiring.

- 2026-05-20 (Regime Intelligence Phase 3E consensus scoring): A
  consensus layer over a parameter sensitivity sweep is structurally the
  honest way to surface fragility - reporting bull/sideways/bear vote
  counts and a dominant_vote_share alongside the dominant regime turns
  "BTCUSDT is bear" into "BTCUSDT is sideways-dominant with mixed
  confidence and zero bull votes" which is both more informative and
  harder to misuse. Three small boolean flags (defensive_bias_flag,
  bullish_bias_flag, regime_uncertainty_flag) each encode a single rule
  with explicit thresholds; this is more auditable than a single
  composite "risk_on/risk_off" verdict because a reviewer can challenge
  each threshold independently. Strict-less-than vs >= in threshold
  comparisons matters - "regime_uncertainty_flag true if share < 0.75"
  produces a clean boundary at exactly 0.75 that any reviewer can
  reproduce; "share <= 0.75" would have shifted that boundary point and
  changed flag values for a real edge case. Tie-breaking dominant_regime
  in a fixed canonical order (bull->sideways->bear) makes the chosen
  dominant deterministic in 3-way ties; in those cases the share is
  guaranteed to be <0.50 so the dominant label is overridden by the
  no_consensus confidence value anyway, but determinism keeps the JSON
  byte-stable across runs. Schema versioning the summary (1->2 when
  adding consensus) is a one-line cost that lets future consumers detect
  the field set.

2026-05-19 - LESSON: an operator iterating on a staged batch can introduce a NEW failure mode per round even while fixing the prior one. Round 1 fixed: structure-invalid; round 2 added required-present fields. Round 3 had a NEW shape of failure: a PowerShell here-string wrapper accidentally pasted alongside the JSON content, corrupting the file to non-JSON. Lesson: in a fail-closed pipeline, this kind of operator-side mishap should not silently propagate; the driver will fail-closed cleanly at INPUT_LOAD_FAILED on the next attempt. Lesson: when an operator file changes between driver-run-time and report-write-time, the report must faithfully reflect the driver-run-time snapshot (sha + size + content) AND flag the post-run anomaly - not retroactively re-grade or silently mask the change. Lesson: useful to keep showing the operator the cumulative fail-closed-gate progression across runs (INPUT_STRUCTURE_INVALID -> missing-required-fields -> missing-created_at_utc) as a visible map of "you fixed N gates; here is the next one" - more motivating than a single fail-closed status code. Lesson: when surfacing a post-run anomaly, report what the wrapped content APPEARS to be (3 GitHub candidates with real content) so the operator does not have to wonder "did Claude lose my work?" - the content is preserved verbatim inside the wrapper; only the wrapper needs to be stripped.

- 2026-05-20 (Regime Intelligence Phase 3F cross-window comparison
  2020-2022 vs 2023-2025): Running the SAME parameter sensitivity +
  consensus sweep across two non-overlapping operator-staged 3-year
  windows is the smallest piece of out-of-sample evidence available
  without backtest infrastructure - and it produced one robust finding
  and one falsified claim. ROBUST: high-stickiness-as-a-property,
  defensive-consensus-with-zero-bull-votes, and uncertainty flag fire
  in BOTH windows, with very similar shape (dominant=sideways/mixed
  confidence/zero bullish bias). The qualitative read survives the
  window change - that is worth keeping. FALSIFIED: the Phase 3D/3C
  claim "bull<->bear transitions only happen via sideways" relied on
  the calmer 2023-2025 window. In 2020-2022 (March 2020 + 2022 H1/H2
  crashes) direct flips appear in EVERY single one of the 12 settings,
  with P(b<->bear) up to ~3%. The pattern was an artifact of the
  classifier + the regime mix of that specific period, not a property
  of BTCUSDT daily structure. Lesson: every analytical claim from a
  single sweep needs a second window before being asserted as a
  property of the asset. Lesson: tight-threshold short-lookback
  settings are the most sensitive to the underlying volatility regime
  - the lookback=10/thr=+/-3% combo shows direct flip probabilities
  ~4x larger in 2020-2022 than in 2023-2025, which means that exact
  setting is the best "detector" for whether the underlying period is
  volatility-rich or volatility-lean. Lesson: the coincidence of both
  windows ending with 60-day rolling return ~-20% (-19.24% Dec 2022,
  -20.39% Dec 2025) is N=2 evidence and explicitly not interpretable
  as cyclical structure; resist the urge to read it as one. Recording
  the coincidence is fine, claiming a "pattern" is not.

- 2026-05-20 (Regime Intelligence Phase 3G cross-window comparison tool):
  A reusable comparison tool that auto-derives "what replicated / what
  changed / what is robust / what to retire" from N input summaries is
  cheaper than narrating each comparison in chat and produces an
  auditable artifact. The tool's interpretation rules should be simple,
  threshold-based, and explicit (dominant-agreement, flag-triple agreement,
  share spread > 0.15, stickiness count delta <= 1, direct-b2b ratio
  spread >= 0.25) - a reviewer can challenge any single threshold without
  having to re-derive the analysis. Best-effort provenance is the right
  default: opportunistic follow of rows[0].report_json -> source_csv_hash
  works for sweep summaries that were just produced (per-run reports
  exist), gracefully returns None if reports were moved or pruned. Don't
  hard-fail on missing optional provenance; reserve fail-closed for
  *required* contract violations (missing consensus block, missing safety
  labels, fewer than 2 inputs). A test that scans BOTH the rendered MD
  AND the JSON output for a list of trade-recommendation phrases ("you
  should buy", "go long", "place an order", etc.) is a cheap insurance
  against future interpretation strings drifting into action language.
  Use phrase-level checks, not single-word checks - "long" is a legitimate
  technical term ("long lookback") that doesn't constitute a
  recommendation, but "go long" does. The auto-generated cross-window
  finding ("flips only via sideways is window-specific") is exactly the
  Phase 3F manual finding rediscovered by the tool from raw inputs -
  good sanity check that the comparator surfaces real signal.

2026-05-19 - LESSON: UTF-8 BOM is a Windows-specific JSON encoding gotcha that bites cross-platform fail-closed pipelines hard. PowerShell Set-Content -Encoding UTF8 writes BOM by default; Python stdlib json.loads is strict and rejects BOM with JSONDecodeError. The fix is one of two trivial flags - operator side use UTF8NoBOM, or driver side use utf-8-sig - but it is invisible to anyone who has not been bitten by it before. Lesson: in a Windows-PowerShell environment specifically, the deny-by-default load gate should probably accept BOM by default (RFC 8259 allows parsers to ignore BOM); switching the driver's read_text encoding from utf-8 to utf-8-sig is a one-line robustness improvement that costs nothing. Doing so does require its own authorization since it changes the driver sha; the operator-side fix is smaller and SHOULD be tried first. Lesson: the fail-closed progression across 4 runs (structure -> missing-required -> missing-timestamp -> BOM-encoding) is a useful learning artifact for the operator - each round, the system pointed out exactly the next layer of incompleteness with deterministic reasons and no invented content. This is what the deny-by-default discipline buys: a clear teaching arc instead of a single ambiguous failure.

- 2026-05-20 (Regime Intelligence Phase 3H multi-symbol fetcher build):
  Adding a peer tool with a slightly broader allowlist instead of
  modifying the existing strict-BTC-only tool is the right surgical move
  when "safety profile" is part of the value proposition. Both tools
  now exist; the narrower one (BTCUSDT-only) remains the audit-friendly
  default; the broader one (BTC/ETH/SOL) is the multi-asset workhorse.
  Operators pick which surface they want; reviewers can point at the
  narrow tool as proof that "broader scope was never silently enabled".
  Parametrizing tests with pytest.mark.parametrize over symbols
  (BTCUSDT/ETHUSDT/SOLUSDT) catches off-by-one bugs in filename
  construction and CLI output formatting more efficiently than three
  separate test functions - and keeps the test file shorter.
  Re-running the SAME safety scans (forbidden imports, forbidden call
  identifiers, credential strings, environ access, real-network ban)
  against the new tool's source caught zero issues on first run; this
  confirms the Phase 3B template was clean enough to clone safely.
  Keeping ALLOWED_SYMBOLS as a frozenset (not a list) is a tiny but
  meaningful signal: this set is immutable at runtime and any addition
  requires an explicit code change and review, not a config tweak.

2026-05-19 - LESSON: a fail-closed pipeline with multiple distinct gates (structure -> required-fields -> timestamp -> BOM -> grading) walks the operator through incompleteness ONE LAYER AT A TIME. Each round, the operator gets a deterministic reason for the specific issue blocking THIS run, fixes only that, and resubmits. After 5 rounds the operator had a clean intake all the way through M4R1 grading - WITHOUT Claude inventing content or modifying the operator file. Lesson: when a candidate reaches the grader and gets graded INSUFFICIENT_EVIDENCE, that is a USEFUL outcome - it tells the operator the specific content gap (data_availability not declared) rather than a vague "missing things". The CALENDAR_COMPLEXITY_COST warning labels on every record were similarly informative: the operator hedged "exact handling unknown" on calendar_requirements; tightening that to "cash equity RTH; NYSE official holiday cal" would drop the warning. Lesson: the M4R1 hold_unless_explicit_gate's treatment of explicit-"unknown" as "not-explicit" is correct discipline - "unknown" is honest about a gap, not a substitute for an actual rule. The operator can use this as the ladder out of HOLD: every "unknown" they replace with a concrete rule from the pasted text is one step toward HELD_BUT_PROMISING or FINAL_REVIEW_CANDIDATE.

- 2026-05-20 (Regime Intelligence Phase 3I ETH two-window sweep + ETH vs
  BTC cross-asset observations - 4 windows now compared): The Phase 3D/3E
  sweep tool + Phase 3G comparator work cleanly across a different asset
  with zero code changes - that's evidence the tools are properly
  parameterized rather than BTC-specific. Cross-ASSET findings differ
  from cross-WINDOW findings in important ways: BTC's two windows
  produced IDENTICAL consensus signature (same dominant/confidence/all
  three flags); ETH's two windows produced PARTIALLY identical signature
  (same dominant/confidence but DIFFERENT defensive flag because ETH
  2023-2025 has non-zero bull votes). This is the first time any
  bull_votes != 0 has shown up in our work, and it correctly flips the
  defensive_bias_flag to False (the flag rule requires bull_votes == 0).
  Good empirical confirmation that the consensus flags do react to
  reality rather than reporting a constant. Stickiness as a qualitative
  property now survives cross-asset (2 BTC windows + 2 ETH windows = 4
  windows, every regime stays medium-or-high in every setting); that's
  the strongest finding so far. Conversely, the "all-three-regimes-high
  stickiness in N of 12 settings" count is wildly variable across
  assets (ETH 2020-2022: 2/12 vs BTC 2020-2022: 7/12) - that specific
  count is window+asset specific, not a portable summary statistic.
  ETH endpoints lean more directly bearish than BTC endpoints in BOTH
  windows compared - this could be a feature of the period (both
  windows end mid-bear/early-recovery for crypto) rather than an asset
  property, and we should resist reading it as ETH-specific until we
  have at least 4 ETH windows. The "direct bull<->bear flips are
  absent" claim is now falsified in 4/4 windows we've tested at short
  lookbacks - safe to retire as a universal claim and re-scope to
  long-lookback-only.

- 2026-05-20 (Regime Intelligence Phase 3J SOL two-window sweep + 6-window
  cross-asset findings - BTC + ETH + SOL across 2 windows each): SOL
  2020-2022 produced the first UNANIMOUS consensus in our work
  (12/12 settings = bear, strong confidence, uncertainty=False) -
  empirical evidence that the consensus tool's "strong" tier and
  uncertainty=False output do fire correctly when warranted, not just
  defaulting to "mixed/True". The window contained the SOL-specific
  FTX-driven late-2022 collapse (~-69% rolling return at lookback=60),
  which is exactly the kind of one-directional collapse that should
  produce strong consensus. Conversely, SOL 2023-2025 gave an EXACT
  6/6 tie between sideways and bear that exercised the comparator's
  canonical-tie-break order (bull->sideways->bear, picking sideways)
  for the first time - reassuring that the tie-break is deterministic
  and visible. The cross-asset stickiness comparison surfaces a real
  asymmetry: BTC has 6-7/12 "all-three-high" settings, ETH has 2-8/12,
  SOL has 0-1/12. SOL's regimes are individually persistent (still
  medium-or-high band) but the three regimes are rarely all
  simultaneously high - SOL's high-volatility period produces shorter
  regime clusters that don't all reach the >=0.70 self-transition
  threshold. So "all-three-high stickiness" is NOT a universal cross-
  asset property; it varies by underlying volatility. The 6-window
  finding most worth carrying forward: "daily regimes have at least
  medium stickiness in every regime in every setting" survives all 6
  windows; that's the strongest cross-asset empirical claim we have.
  Lesson on consensus signature: "consensus signature replicates
  across windows" fires for BTC's two windows but not ETH's, not
  SOL's - so it's a single-asset/specific-window observation, not a
  portable property of crypto majors. Adjust future claims accordingly.

2026-05-19 - LESSON: when a candidate lands at HELD_FOR_OPERATOR_REVIEW, the value of a sealed planning document is that it converts a single ambiguous "fix things" instruction into a precise, ordered, copy/paste-able checklist. The S3A plan distinguishes (a) fields settable on context priors alone (no code-read), (b) fields requiring a one-time browser read by the operator, and (c) fields that can honestly remain absent. The plan also predicts the exact next-run outcome (HBP vs FRC vs still-HELD) per fill-scenario, so the operator can pick how much effort to invest based on how strong a survivor they want. Lesson: surfacing the H4 + M4R1 + hold-gate logic in plain English ("explicit-unknown counts as not-explicit"; "data_availability is the primary blocker") is more useful than re-citing the grade name - the operator can target the actual control variables. Lesson: synthesizing stop_rule from already-declared risk_rule + crossover convention is a fair move; it converts "honest unknown" into "honest concrete" without inventing content the operator did not provide. Lesson: respect the boundary - even when the operator could plausibly want Claude to fetch the README to extract exit_rule etc., the no-fetch authorization means Claude documents what to look for instead, and the operator does the read.

- 2026-05-20 (Regime Intelligence Phase 3K crypto regime master overview
  + correction): Building a STRICTER per-row stickiness check (band must
  be in {medium, high}, low counts as not-persistent) for the overview
  surfaced an honest correction: my earlier brain memory entries (Phase
  3F/3I/3J) claimed daily regime persistence holds across all windows,
  but that was using the WEAKER comparator-level check
  (stickiness_high_in_all_three_count >= 1 per window). The stricter
  per-row check finds 3 of 6 windows (ETH 2020-2022, SOL 2020-2022,
  SOL 2023-2025) have at least one setting with at least one regime at
  the "low" band. The strong claim that "every regime stays in
  medium-or-high band in every setting in every window" is NOT
  supported by the full 6-window dataset. This is a useful reminder
  that summary-level counts and per-row band scans answer different
  questions, and the strictest-supported claim is the right thing to
  report cross-asset. Designing the overview tool to inclusion-test
  each candidate finding against ALL inputs (universal AND) before
  asserting it kept Phase 3K from accidentally over-claiming. The
  test where one synthetic window has bullish_bias_flag=True and the
  tool correctly OMITS the false-in-all-windows claim is the single
  most valuable test in the file - it directly proves the inclusion
  logic distinguishes "all" from "most". Asset-specific and retire
  sections are where most of the action lives when you have 3+ assets;
  the robust-cross-asset section is rightly hard to populate because
  cross-asset properties are rare. The "strategy research notes"
  section structured around "what this dataset DOES support" /
  "what it DOES NOT support" / "what kinds of models would
  misrepresent the data" stays clearly observational and never reads
  as a buy/sell recommendation - good template to reuse.

2026-05-19 - LESSON: when an operator authorizes a re-run framed around a specific edit ("enriched single-candidate intake re-run") but the file is byte-identical to the prior run, the honest move is to run the driver faithfully AND surface the unchanged-file finding with a byte-identical-output determinism proof. Do not silently pretend the edits were made; do not refuse to run the authorized work. Both halves of the response have value: the run confirms the schema's deterministic property (same input -> byte-identical intake_memory_jsonl), and the honest finding tells the operator their edits did not persist. Lesson: when reporting determinism proofs, comparing the intake_memory.jsonl sha across runs is the cleanest signal - it strips out the report_date_utc noise from preflight seals and gives the operator a clean "did anything actually change?" check. Lesson: per-candidate "vs rerun4: BYTE_IDENTICAL" tags in the report make the no-change finding visible at a glance instead of buried in narrative.

- 2026-05-20 (Regime Intelligence Phase 4A attribution design): When
  considering a research bridge that joins TWO independently-built data
  systems, the cheapest first-cost activity is a read-only inspection
  + a written design doc - cheaper than a half-built tool because the
  inspection surfaces architectural gaps that change the design.
  Inspection here surfaced one such gap: the Phase 1/2 per-run reports
  don't persist per-day regime labels. That changes the build plan from
  "consume an existing labels stream" to "recompute via the pure-
  deterministic classifier on the same frozen CSV", which is a smaller,
  safer build that requires zero modifications to existing core logic.
  classify_series being pure-deterministic is now the load-bearing
  property of the Phase 4B design - which means it should NEVER be
  changed without re-validating Phase 4B. Worth noting in core
  contracts.
  Inspection also surfaced a vocabulary mismatch (Phase 1's
  {bull,sideways,bear} vs Strategy Lab's existing {TREND/RANGE/
  COMPRESSION/EXPANSION/HIGH_VOL/LOW_VOL}) that I almost glossed over.
  The honest design path is "ONE vocabulary at a time, no auto-mapping,
  no silent crosswalk" - any vocabulary translation needs an operator
  decision, not a tool decision. Same lesson for the BTCUSD<->BTCUSDT
  symbol mismatch in the backtest JSONs: warn the operator and let
  them confirm; don't silently coerce. The wrong shape of failure here
  would have been to publish an attribution report against
  half-aligned data the operator didn't realize was half-aligned.
  Final lesson: paper_arena.json is aggregate-only and looks tempting
  to ingest, but per-trade dates are missing. Better to skip cleanly
  with a documented "insufficient resolution" than try to fake daily
  attribution from aggregate snapshots.

2026-05-19 - LESSON: a planning document is only as good as the ground truth it was based on. The S3A plan instructed the operator to fill the S2 schema field names (exit_rule/calendar_requirements/cost_slippage_requirements per S2D §1) and assumed those would satisfy the H4+M4R1 graders. The operator followed the plan perfectly, the file passed every load and S2 gate cleanly, the driver ran clean - and the candidate still stayed HELD because the graders look for different field names (exit_or_invalidation/calendar_semantics/cost_awareness/trigger_frequency_estimate). The S2C synthetic fixtures that previously succeeded had ALL of these vocabularies declared simultaneously, which masked the issue at fixture-time. Lesson: when writing an operator-facing enrichment plan that runs through a multi-stage grader, the plan SHOULD inspect the graders'' actual required field names (not just the schema-spec field names) and either (a) tell the operator to declare both vocabularies, or (b) recommend a driver patch to alias them. Going forward, this becomes a real S2D / S3A drafting principle: the operator must not need to learn two field-name vocabularies; if they do, the plan is incomplete. The cleanest answer is a driver-side alias map in _prepare_for_grader, with a single source of truth that the operator-facing spec can stay simple. Lesson: a sealed honest report of the field-name mismatch is more valuable than another operator edit round, because it identifies a real architectural gap that affects every future S3-like enrichment, not just this candidate.

2026-05-20 - LESSON: the full S3 -> S3D operator-iteration arc is a teaching artifact for deny-by-default. Six rounds, six distinct gates fired: (1) structure-invalid (bare list); (2) S2 missing required-present fields; (3) S2 missing created_at_utc; (4) INPUT_LOAD_FAILED_UTF8_BOM; (5) HELD with schema-vs-grader field-name mismatch; (6) survivor. Each round produced a deterministic reason, no invented content, no Claude file modification, all production artifacts byte-unchanged across every run. The operator did NOT need to be perfect on round 1 - the system surfaced the next gap precisely each round. Lesson: when the system tells the operator "missing X", the operator can fix X and resubmit; lesson: when the system says "explicit-unknown counts as not-explicit", the operator stops writing "unknown" and writes honest hedged-text instead; lesson: when the schema says exit_rule but the grader looks at exit_or_invalidation, you eventually surface that mismatch with a diagnostic. Lesson: the FRC grade triggered partly on substring presence ("oos" + "walk-forward") in the operator's honest text "... evidence unknown from pasted summary" - this is a real H4 heuristic limitation worth surfacing in the report. The survivor label remains "ready for next separately-authorized step", not "verified" - the substring-leniency is by design and gets caught (or not) at the deep-extraction stage. Lesson: produce sealed reports for ALL runs including the unchanged-file determinism runs - they confirm the system's stability and give the operator a paper trail. The 6-round arc would have been hard to navigate without each round leaving a sealed artifact.

- 2026-05-20 (Regime Intelligence Phase 4B v1 build + first real run):
  The Phase 4A design's "recompute daily labels via deterministic
  classify_series, don't persist them" architectural choice paid off
  immediately - zero changes to sparta_regime_intelligence/ were
  required, the joiner stays fully decoupled, and the existing
  per-window summaries don't need a schema bump. Worth carrying
  forward: when joining two data systems, prefer recomputing the
  derived stream from the same deterministic source over adding new
  fields to either system's persistence schema. Sha-256 verification
  on the strategy bar_returns CSV against the value already recorded
  in the backtest JSON is essentially free and rejected silent file
  swaps - good cheap provenance gate. The first real attribution
  matched the textbook expectation almost too cleanly (breakout
  strategy net-contributed in bull-classified bars, net-subtracted
  in sideways) - which is a mild warning sign that the regime
  classifier and the strategy may be picking up the same underlying
  directional signal at this lookback. The "regime classification is
  computed from the same price series the strategy traded against;
  co-movement is mechanical, not predictive" limitation is doing
  load-bearing work; an operator who skipped that line could
  over-interpret the regime-conditional cumulative returns as edge
  evidence. The conflict overlay verdict_metrics counts mechanically
  match the regime overlay because at the chosen single-setting
  threshold the bull regime is ALWAYS verdict=aligned and sideways
  is ALWAYS verdict=conflict for a breakout style - the conflict
  overlay adds no new information in that case. That's not a bug;
  it's a feature of the rule encoding meeting the data. Worth noting
  in the report's text rather than treating "conflict aggregates
  loss" as independent confirmation. Final lesson: for the first
  real attribution we passed zero skipped/missing, which is the
  happy case but also the rarest case in general - the
  skipped_dates_sample[] and missing_regime_sample[] paths got tested
  on synthetic data and were ready for cases where the join is
  partial; that defensive plumbing will be more valuable than the
  metrics themselves when an operator runs this against a backtest
  whose window extends outside the staged regime CSV.

2026-05-20 - LESSON: writing a deep-extraction application plan BEFORE the first gated-live network call is the right discipline. It surfaces (a) exactly what content the extractor will read and what it will ignore, (b) the candidate-dict shape the operator must supply since the extractor does not discover the repo file tree, (c) the verdict-overlay fields the operator/follow-up must compute from extracted text, (d) the downgrade-only decision rules and the absolute invariants (extraction never promotes to Tier-1). The plan also acts as an audit point: if H3e is later run and produces outputs that do not match the predicted verdict-overlay schema, that is itself a signal that something drifted. Lesson: when planning the first read-only network access in a deny-by-default pipeline, sequence it as four separate phases (PLAN -> STAGE -> EXECUTE -> VERIFY), each with its own authorization. This matches the M4R2 dispatch-injected pattern: the extractor module is built fixture-only; the transport is injected at EXECUTE time; the verdict computation happens AFTER extraction. The boundary between extractor + transport + verdict is the same boundary that lets us reason about which step "owns" the network exposure. Lesson: keep the H4-substring-leniency caveat visible at the top of every downstream document - it is the precise reason deep extraction exists for this candidate, and forgetting it would risk treating FRC as verified rather than "ready to verify".

- 2026-05-20 (Regime Intelligence Phase 4C batch attribution + key
  cross-strategy finding): Running attribution across 5 representative
  strategy families immediately surfaced the answer to the Phase 4B
  question ("is the bull-positive/sideways-negative pattern strategy-
  specific or universal?") - it is FAMILY-specific, not universal.
  Directional families (momentum_breakout, regime_filter_overlay,
  volatility_targeting) all share the pattern: best=bull, sideways
  hurts, uncertainty hurts. Mean-reversion families
  (rsi_mean_reversion, atr_compression_expansion) cleanly INVERT it:
  rsi has best=BEAR / worst=BULL and uncertainty HELPED. This is the
  textbook expectation that mean reversion benefits from choppy
  conditions, but seeing it surface cleanly from real backtests
  joined to deterministic regime labels is evidence the regime
  classifier is picking up something real about the underlying
  series, not just labeling noise. Lesson: the Phase 4B brain memory
  entry warned that the bull-positive pattern might be over-
  interpretable due to mechanical co-movement; this cross-strategy
  run validates that warning - the same regime overlay produces
  inverse patterns for inverse strategy families, which is exactly
  what you'd expect if the regime labels are descriptively useful
  but not predictively useful. The uncertainty_effect split (hurt vs
  helped) cleanly tracks strategy family type and could be a useful
  one-bit characterization metric for future strategy classification.
  Architectural lesson: dependency-injecting run_attribution_fn into
  the batch tool made the 27-test synthetic-only test suite trivial
  to write - the same pattern used in Phase 3B's _ban_real_http
  fixture works equally well for "ban real attribution" in a tool
  that wraps another tool. Worth carrying forward for any future
  Phase 4D wrapper.

2026-05-20 - LESSON: an operator-downloaded local ZIP is a clean substitute for gated-live network access when the goal is read-only repository inspection. Stdlib zipfile inspects the central directory without extracting anything, so Claude can produce a complete safety verdict (CRC integrity, file count, total uncompressed size, extension distribution, suspicious-path scan, credential-name scan, archive-in-archive scan, zip-bomb-risk estimate) without touching the filesystem outside reading the ZIP itself. This is the SAFEST way to validate untrusted code packages before deciding whether to extract. Lesson: keep the planned inspection-target list (README/Strategy/Backtester/OrderManager/etc.) tied to the H3a decision rules, not to the language of the project. The H3a application plan assumed Python; the actual repo is C++; the rules apply equally because the rules are about WHAT to verify (entry, exit, sizing, cost, OOS, look-ahead) not WHAT LANGUAGE the verification reads. Lesson: surface content drift between operator-pasted summary and actual repo shape (e.g. "operator said SMA crossover; the repo also has find_pairs.py suggesting pairs trading") but do not downgrade on that alone - drift is information for H3a-verify, not a verdict. Lesson: when shell scripts are present in an inspected ZIP, the safe rule is "extract as text only, never invoke" - on Windows this is enforced by the OS anyway, but stating it in writing in the plan makes the boundary explicit for cross-platform readers.

- 2026-05-20 (Regime Intelligence Phase 4D cross-parameter robustness +
  Phase 4C pattern fully replicated): The Phase 4C single-setting
  finding (3 directional + 1 mean-reversion + 1 mixed) survived all
  12 parameter settings unchanged - replication fraction 1.000. This
  is the strongest result we've seen so far, but the right way to
  read it is "the regime classifier and the strategy returns
  produce a consistent labeling across the chosen grid", NOT "we
  discovered something universal about crypto strategies". The same
  caveat from Phase 4B applies: regime labels and strategy returns
  derive from the same price series; consistent co-movement across
  grid settings means the classifier is internally stable, not that
  it predicts. atr_compression_expansion's "mixed_or_fragile"
