  classification turned out to be a STABLE mixed signal - best=bull
  in 12/12 AND uncertainty_helped in 12/12 - the two signals
  disagree consistently. That's a meaningful empirical observation:
  some strategies are bull-positive AND uncertainty-helped at the
  same time, which the binary 8-of-12 rule won't classify but is
  itself a robust pattern. Consider in Phase 4E (if there ever is
  one) a 4-way classification: directional / mean-reversion /
  bull-positive-uncertainty-helped / fragile. The 1.5-second
  inter-setting sleep worked cleanly - no timestamp collisions
  observed in the 60 per-attribution reports; if anything 1.0s
  would probably suffice. The dependency-injection pattern
  (run_batch_fn for tests, real_run_batch for production) made the
  test file possible to write entirely with synthetic data, and the
  22 tests ran in 0.24s. Without that injection the same coverage
  would have required creating real backtest pairings on disk and
  invoking Phase 4B 60+ times in CI. Lesson: when building a tool
  that wraps another tool, always make the wrapped function a
  dependency-injected parameter.

2026-05-20 - LESSON: per-file zipfile extraction with FOUR independent safety nets gives a much stronger guarantee than ZipFile.extractall: (1) allowlist gate on extension/no-ext-name; (2) path-safety re-check at extraction time even though the central directory was already scanned in the validation phase ("the central directory could lie"); (3) each target.resolve() must be verified to live inside the quarantine root via Path.relative_to() BEFORE write; (4) per-file sha256 recomputed from disk after write must equal sha256 of the bytes zipfile gave us. Each of these catches a different class of attack: (1) blocks binaries/archives/PDFs; (2) blocks central-directory-lying entries; (3) blocks slip-path attacks where a resolved name escapes quarantine via symlinks/absolute prefix; (4) catches write-time tampering or filesystem corruption. None of them costs more than a few lines of stdlib code. Lesson: when extracting a ZIP that contains shell scripts on Windows, you get a free safety layer (Windows does not auto-execute .sh) but stating "extracted as text only, never invoked" in writing in the manifest preserves the boundary for cross-platform reading. Lesson: matching the total quarantine bytes against the ZIP's reported uncompressed total is a cheap end-to-end check that nothing was silently dropped during extraction.

- 2026-05-20 (Regime Intelligence Phase 4E selector simulation - Rule C
  best, Rule D surprisingly hurt drawdown): The strongest single
  result so far - Rule C (regime-aware family switch) produced a
  +1.258 cumulative proxy versus Rule A (always-on equal basket) at
  +0.352. This is a 3.5x cumulative ratio; if I treat this as
  evidence of edge I will be making a mistake. The right read is:
  the regime classifier that Rule C uses to switch families is
  derived from the SAME PRICE SERIES the strategies traded against,
  so any 'correct' regime call is mechanically aligned with the
  underlying price movement. Rule C 'switching to rsi on non-bull
  days' is equivalent to 'using the strategy whose returns
  positively correlate with the next bar's direction' - and the
  regime classifier knows the next bar's direction (sort of) because
  it's looking at the rolling return of the same price the strategy
  is responding to. This is the 'mechanical co-movement' caveat
  Phase 4B/4C/4D have flagged finally producing a visible amplified
  effect, and it should be the loudest warning in the entire 4E
  report. The selector tool's limitations section calls this out
  explicitly but operators reading just the headline number will be
  primed for over-interpretation. UNEXPECTED FINDING: Rule D
  (damage-control on uncertain days) INCREASED drawdown vs Rule A
  (0.134 vs 0.117). The Phase 4D-found 'uncertainty hurts directional
  strategies' did not translate to 'flattening on uncertain days
  improves drawdown' because (a) the equal basket has diversification
  benefit Rule D loses, and (b) the confident-day exposure
  concentrates volatility that the basket would have smoothed. Two
  lessons: (1) drawdown is a path-dependent metric and reducing
  exposure on bad days doesn't automatically reduce drawdown - the
  remaining exposed days can be worse. (2) Per-strategy regime
  affinity findings (Phase 4D) do NOT compose into per-rule
  drawdown improvements (Phase 4E) - need to test, not extrapolate.
  Architectural note: building selector rules as standalone functions
  taking a per-day record dict and returning {return, applied, reason}
  made the test suite extremely clean - each rule could be unit-
  tested in isolation with simple synthetic records, and the
  end-to-end test just verifies the orchestration. Dependency-
  injecting at the per-rule level would have made the tool even
  more flexible but at the cost of additional surface area. Worth
  flagging for any future Phase 4F that wants to test more rules.

2026-05-20 - LESSON: deep extraction's job is to VERIFY OR CONTRADICT the upstream grader's reasons, not to take them at face value. The H3a-local-verify on the first real-link survivor produced exactly the corrective result the discipline was designed to produce: H4 graded FRC because of substring presence of "oos"+"walk-forward" in the operator's qualifier text "OOS and walk-forward evidence unknown from pasted summary" - the operator's qualifier was honest; the evidence is genuinely absent in the actual code. Without deep extraction, the candidate would have advanced toward Tier-1 spec authoring under a false-positive grade. With deep extraction, it correctly lands at INSUFFICIENT_EVIDENCE/HELD with three documented downgrade rules fired. Lesson: every claim in the README must be cross-checked against actual code - this repo claims "realistic risk management" while commission/slippage are explicitly commented out as Unused, and claims "Multi-Asset Backtesting" while each symbol gets a separate OrderManager + $100k. Cosmetic claims do not survive code inspection. Lesson: same-bar close fill is a subtle tradeability failure (no future-bar peek = no lookahead bias in the strict sense) but still gives the backtest an unrealistic edge that real-world execution cannot reproduce. Mark as tradeability_check=FAIL, not as lookahead_bias_check=FAIL. Lesson: distinguish "NOT_FOUND" from "CONTRADICTED" in methodology_evidence_status - the candidate's repo doesn't actively show a flawed OOS scheme (NOT_FOUND); it simply lacks any. NOT_FOUND -> HBP downgrade; CONTRADICTED -> INSUFFICIENT_EVIDENCE downgrade. In this case multiple rules push it to INSUFFICIENT_EVIDENCE anyway, but the distinction matters for grading discipline. Lesson: SMA crossover at 20/50 (not the assumed 50/200) is a reminder that operator's "unknown from pasted summary" qualifier was the right honest stance - the operator did NOT invent SMA periods, and deep extraction filled in the truth. Lesson: a "salvageable" HOLD is more valuable than a REJECT here because the candidate code is well-structured and the remediation path (OOS split + cost/slippage wiring + next-bar-open fill + risk-based sizing + pinned dataset) is operator-tractable rather than fundamental.

- 2026-05-20 (Regime Intelligence Phase 4F placebo - strong resistance,
  caveat unchanged): The 500-trial placebo result is unambiguous on
  one front and stays open on another. Unambiguous: the Phase 4E
  +0.905 Rule C advantage is NOT a random fluke under the chosen
  selector rule. 0 of 500 randomly-labelled placebo trials reached
  +0.905; placebo mean is NEGATIVE (-0.147); the empirical p-value
  is 0.0000 to four decimal places; the real advantage exceeds the
  placebo p99 by ~3x. Open: the placebo test cannot distinguish
  "regime classifier has information edge" from "regime classifier
  is mechanically aligned with same-period prices because it was
  derived from them". Both interpretations produce strong placebo
  resistance, and the Phase 4F report's interpretation block makes
  this distinction explicit so an operator reading the headline
  number doesn't over-interpret it. Lesson: shuffle tests are
  necessary but not sufficient. They rule OUT a specific null
  hypothesis ("the result is a random fluke under the selector rule")
  but cannot rule out adjacent null hypotheses ("the classifier and
  the strategy returns are both derived from the same prices, so
  same-period alignment is mechanical not predictive"). The next
  test that DOES distinguish those hypotheses is cross-asset or
  out-of-sample - until then, "strong placebo resistance" is
  evidence that's compatible with both edge and overfit-by-
  construction. Capturing that distinction in the report's
  interpretation text was the most important design decision in
  Phase 4F. The negative placebo mean (-0.147) is itself
  interesting: under random labels, Rule C's switching mechanism
  produces a WORSE result than the equal basket. This makes sense
  given that the directional basket significantly outperformed the
  rsi family (+0.527 vs +0.073 cum), so randomly switching between
  them throws away the directional basket's edge by spreading
  exposure across both - while real Rule C concentrates directional
  exposure on the "right" days. Whether the "right" days are
  knowable in advance is the question the placebo test cannot
  answer.

2026-05-20 - LESSON BATCH L_H3A_001-005 (recorded as permanent Hunter Brain grading discipline; sealed at aec97958):

L_H3A_001 SUBSTRING FALSE-POSITIVE ON OOS/WALK-FORWARD: H4 detects methodology by substring presence in methodology_evidence; an operator's honest qualifier text containing the substring along with "unknown" / "not specified" / "absent" / "incomplete" / "pending" still triggers FRC. Deep extraction is the gate that catches this. Future SEPARATE H4 heuristic patch should tighten the substring check to reject when surrounding context is a negative qualifier.

L_H3A_002 SAME-BAR-CLOSE-FILL IS A HARD WARNING: Not look-ahead bias in the strict sense (no future-bar peek) but gives the backtest an unrealistic perfect-close edge - close prints are only available AFTER the bar closes; realistic fills happen at next-bar open. tradeability_check=FAIL must always downgrade at least to HOLD; first-class downgrade trigger.

L_H3A_003 ZERO-COST BASELINE BLOCKS PROMOTION: A candidate whose code does not apply commission or slippage produces results that overstate real-world returns. ZERO_COST_CONTROL_BASELINE is a hard quarantine flag; promotion to Tier-1 spec or deep-verification advancement is blocked until operator supplies a cost stress test. The flag must be inherited by Tier-1 authoring gates so even an MR1-MR10-complete spec authorization refuses to promote a flagged candidate.

L_H3A_004 FIXED-SHARE SIZING DOWNGRADES RISK QUALITY: A backtester that buys 100 shares regardless of price, volatility, or equity is not risk-managed - 100 shares of a $5 stock vs 100 shares of a $500 stock at the same equity is a position-sizing pathology. FIXED_SHARE_SIZING_PRIMITIVE flag; operator must supply a risk-adjusted sizing replacement (fixed-% of equity, ATR-scaled, or vol-targeted) before promotion.

L_H3A_005 ROLLING DATA WINDOWS KILL REPRODUCIBILITY: Rolling windows tied to datetime.now() destroy reproducibility - re-running the same code on a different day pulls a different dataset. Without dataset pinning even a single-pass in-sample backtest cannot be reproduced; OOS/walk-forward analysis becomes meaningless because slice boundaries cannot be fixed against actual data. UNPINNED_DATASET flag; operator must pin the data window to a fixed historical range with documented data-vendor + retrieval date before promotion.

Cross-cutting lesson: each of these 5 patterns should propagate as a per-candidate flag that downstream Tier-1 spec authoring authorizations INHERIT and REFUSE TO BYPASS. The flag system is the structural way to keep promotion discipline consistent across separately-authorized phases - lessons recorded only in markdown can be forgotten between sessions; flags carried in the canonical record cannot.

2026-05-20 - LESSON: when a sealed grader has a known leniency that produces a false positive (H4 substring match on OOS/walk-forward), the right architectural move is NOT to patch the sealed grader but to patch the downgrade-only wrapper above it. M4R1 was designed exactly for this kind of post-hoc discipline addition - its assess_v2 already runs after H4.assess and applies downgrade rules. Adding 5 more rules + 5 more warning labels is incremental rather than architectural. H4 stays byte-unchanged across the entire prior phase history (S2C/S2E/M4R2/S3/H3a-local-verify all pinned H4=98eda1fd); touching H4 would cascade re-sealing through dozens of reports. Lesson: when a discipline needs to PROPAGATE between phases (intake-time detection -> deep-extraction-time detection -> future Tier-1-time inheritance), the canonical S2 record is the propagation carrier. Adding 5 advisory fields to S2_M4R1_FIELDS lets the flags travel with the record so future Tier-1 authoring authorizations INHERIT them and refuse to bypass without operator code-remediation attestation. The flag system is the structural way to keep promotion discipline consistent across separately-authorized phases. Lesson: distinguish intake-detectable lessons (L_H3A_001 negative-qualifier proximity scan; L_H3A_004 fixed-share regex; L_H3A_005 unpinned-window regex) from deep-extraction-only lessons (L_H3A_002 same-bar close fill; L_H3A_003 zero-cost baseline) and partial-overlap (L_H3A_003 can be partially detected at intake via cost-text regex but full detection requires H3a-verify). The patch design needs both intake-time prechecks AND schema-fields-for-propagation; neither alone is sufficient. Lesson: explicit non-flag carve-outs matter - "fixed 100 shares" downgrades but "fixed 2% of equity" does not; "rolling 2yr datetime.now()" downgrades but "2010-01-01 to 2023-12-31" does not. Without the carve-outs the patch would over-flag and reject legitimate strategies. Lesson: codifying lessons into actual code-readable flags (per-candidate fields with documented detection rules) is much stronger than markdown lessons that depend on operator memory between sessions.

- 2026-05-20 (Regime Intelligence Phase 4H-a out-of-sample FAILED THE
  TEST - confirmation that Phase 4E/4F was mechanical co-movement):
  The Phase 4H-a OOS result is THE single most important finding in
  the entire Regime Intelligence research arc, and it's a NEGATIVE
  result delivered exactly as the safety apparatus predicted. In
  2024, the placebo distribution had mean -0.147 (random switching
  HURT Rule C), real advantage was +0.905, 0 of 500 placebo trials
  reached it -> looked very strong. In 2022, the placebo distribution
  has mean +0.281 (random switching HELPS Rule C), real advantage is
  only +0.323, and 145 of 500 placebo trials matched or beat the
  real -> weak resistance. The interpretation is honest: the Phase 4E
  selector "edge" was mechanical alignment between (a) the regime
  classifier derived from BTCUSDT 2024 prices and (b) the strategies
  trading those exact prices. In 2024 the directional strategies
  outperformed rsi, so the classifier was "right" to route exposure
  to directional on bullish days. In 2022 the directional strategies
  lost money in the bear market and rsi was the only winner; the
  classifier defaulted to rsi (correctly, mechanically) but any
  random rule that put weight on rsi did similarly well. The
  selector wasn't picking regimes; it was riding the strategy mix.
  Most valuable lessons from this entire arc:
  (1) Placebo tests rule out random-fluke null hypotheses but
  CANNOT rule out mechanical co-movement null hypotheses when the
  signal and the response are both derived from the same underlying
  data. The Phase 4F report correctly stated this; Phase 4H-a
  empirically confirmed it.
  (2) Cross-time-window validation IS the discriminator between
  edge and overfit-by-construction. Phase 4E by itself wasn't
  enough; Phase 4F by itself wasn't enough; only Phase 4H-a's
  separate-window placebo could distinguish.
  (3) The phrase "strong placebo resistance" in Phase 4F should
  ALWAYS have been accompanied by "but does not prove information
  edge" - which it was. Future reports must continue to use that
  exact pattern: strong p-value + load-bearing caveat about same-
  source mechanical alignment. Never drop the caveat to make
  headlines look stronger.
  (4) Architecture lesson: when validation reveals overfitting,
  the right response is to RECORD THE FAILURE prominently and
  preserve all the artifacts, not to delete them or paper over the
  finding. Phase 4H-a's failed_no_placebo_resistance result and
  this brain memory entry are the most valuable outputs of the
  entire arc. The negative result is what makes the previous
  positive results trustworthy.
  (5) "Sign preserved but magnitude shrunk + placebo resistance
  collapsed" is the textbook signature of a partially-mechanical /
  partially-noise effect. The 2024 effect wasn't pure overfit
  (the sign IS preserved in 2022, so there's some persistent
  pattern there), but the bulk of the apparent edge was overfit.
  (6) The selector rule itself isn't refuted - what's refuted is
  the claim that the rule contains useful regime information.
  Rule C in 2024 happened to beat Rule A by a large margin
  partly by luck (correct mechanical alignment) and partly by
  small persistent effect. In 2022 the same rule still beat Rule A
  modestly but indistinguishably from random labelling, which is
  the honest reading.
  (7) Any future trading-bot connection or live deployment
  decisions in this codebase must reference Phase 4H-a explicitly.
  Phase 4E/4F alone would have been misleading; Phase 4H-a is the
  required guard.

- 2026-05-20 (Regime Intelligence Phase 4I market-mode diagnostic):
  Diagnosing WHY a result didn't generalize is more valuable than
  the result itself. Phase 4E/4F looked compelling; Phase 4H-a
  refuted it; Phase 4I explains the mechanism. That sequence - build,
  validate in-sample, falsify out-of-sample, diagnose - is the right
  shape for any future selector research. None of the four steps is
  optional. The diagnostic produced two key insights:
  (1) Rule C's edge in BOTH years was dominated by static family-
  selection, not date-level regime routing. In 2024 directional was
  the winning family and Rule C defaulted to directional on ~27% of
  days; in 2022 rsi was the only winner and Rule C defaulted to rsi
  on 93% of days. Random-label Rule C would have done similarly in
  both cases because the "default" family choice is what actually
  drove returns. The regime classifier was decorative, not load-
  bearing.
  (2) The two windows are nearly mirror-image market modes. 2022 had
  120 bear_confident days vs 2024's 36; 2022 had 25 bull_confident
  days vs 2024's 98. 4 of 5 strategy families flipped sign. The
  "selector" was actually riding the strategy mix - and the strategy
  mix is determined by which family was profitable in that year,
  which itself reflects the market mode.
  The corrective design (two-level: market-mode detector first, then
  mode-conditional family rule) addresses the mechanism. But the
  design only works if the market-mode classifier uses at least one
  signal that is NOT derived from BTCUSDT closes - otherwise we
  reproduce the Phase 4E/4F mechanical co-movement problem at the
  mode level. That requirement (a low-coupling external feature)
  is the most important constraint for any future Phase 4J build,
  and it pushes the project toward needing external data that hasn't
  been staged. That's a real cost the design imposes.
  Lesson on test discipline: I drafted an 8-test acceptance gate
  (sanity, in-sample placebo, OOS placebo on multiple modes, k-fold,
  mode-detector standalone placebo, external-feature ablation, cost
  model, cross-asset). Tests 5 and 6 (mode-detector standalone
  placebo + external-feature ablation) are the new ones beyond
  what Phase 4E-4H-a already covered, and they exist specifically to
  catch the same-source coupling failure that bit Phase 4E/4F. Any
  Phase 4J that skips them returns to that failure mode.
  Lesson on naming: "regime-aware switching" is a misleading framing
  for what Phase 4E/4F actually built. The honest framing is
  "family selection with regime-classifier-derived gating". Calling
  it "regime-aware" implies the regime knowledge does work; the
  Phase 4H-a + 4I diagnostic shows it didn't. Future report
  language should reflect that.

- 2026-05-20 (Regime Intelligence Phase 4H-b 3-window synthesis):
  The 3-window data is now complete and the pattern is clear. 2022
  (bear-dominant) failed placebo. 2023 and 2024 (both bull-dominant)
  passed placebo with strong resistance. The Phase 4I diagnostic
  was right: the selector framework is mode-conditional. It works
  in bull/recovery modes where directional strategies dominate AND
  bear+confident days are scarce (under 10% of year). It fails in
  bear/contraction modes where directional strategies lose money
  AND bear+confident days are dominant (>30% of year).
  This refines the Phase 4H-a "failed_no_placebo_resistance" reading.
  The right interpretation is NOT "the selector is useless" - it's
  "the selector is conditionally useful". A bull-recovery operator
  using Rule C in 2023 or 2024 would have seen +0.99 / +0.91 cumulative
  proxy advantage over the equal basket with strong placebo resistance
  on each window. A bear-contraction operator using the same rule
  in 2022 would have seen +0.32 advantage indistinguishable from
  random.
  But - and this is the load-bearing caveat - "conditionally useful"
  under mechanical co-movement is NOT the same as "predictively
  useful". The 2023+2024 strong placebo resistance is still
  compatible with the regime classifier mechanically tracking same-
  period bull moves because both share the same parent price series.
  The selector picks the right strategies (directional) on the right
  days (bull) - but only because the regime classifier was reading
  those days' prices, not because the classifier carried predictive
  information about what tomorrow's bull days would be. To prove
  predictive utility we'd need the mode-detector + classifier to
  consume some signal that is NOT BTCUSDT closes - the Phase 4I
  Section 6 "low-coupling features".
  Lessons from this arc:
  (1) Three-window evidence is the minimum useful threshold for
  "does this framework generalize". One window is decorative; two
  windows can be coincidence; three windows lets you see whether
  failures cluster by mode or by random sampling. Future selector
  research must always include >=3 windows split across distinct
  market modes.
  (2) The "replicated_strong" classification on 2023 is meaningful
  RELATIVE to the bull-mode subset of windows, not absolutely. If
  Phase 4H-c ever tests a 4th window in another bear-dominant
  period (say 2018 if it existed in this dataset), and it also
  failed placebo like 2022, that would lock in the
  bull-only-conditional finding. A 4th bull-dominant window that
  also passed would not add much beyond what we already know.
  (3) The diagnostic-then-test pattern (Phase 4I predicts mode
  conditionality, Phase 4H-b confirms by showing 2023 mirrors 2024)
  is the strongest empirical story possible in this codebase. It
  means the prediction was made BEFORE the test, not after seeing
  the 2023 numbers.
  (4) The Phase 4I proposed two-level selector (mode-detector +
  mode-conditional family rule) now has additional support. The
  honest version of that architecture: Variant A (bull/recovery)
  fires on detected bull-recovery modes; Variant B (bear/
  contraction) fires on detected bear modes; Variant C/D handle
  edge cases. The mode-detector itself still needs at least one
  low-coupling feature to escape the mechanical co-movement
  critique.
  (5) Naming lesson: "Rule C regime-aware switch" remains a
  misleading name. It IS aware of regimes within the window, but
  its apparent edge is dominated by static family-selection
  (default to rsi when not bull+confident) + mechanical co-movement
  (when bull+confident actually triggers, directional happens to be
  the winner because the classifier was reading the same prices).
  "Mode-conditional family router" would be a more honest name.

2026-05-20 - LESSON: replaying a patched grader on the SAME operator file that exhibited the original false positive is the cheapest possible production validation. The S3E replay used the byte-identical S3D-era operator batch (e8f53a84 unchanged) and produced a different and honest outcome - downgraded krishnaa03 FRC->HBP at intake time and attached the right warning labels. The diff between S3D and S3E reports is the unit-test-grade evidence that the patch works as designed on actual data, not just on synthetic fixtures. Lesson: this kind of "replay the same input through the patched code" is a strong corroboration that test-only confidence (132/132 unit tests passing) translates to real-world behaviour. Lesson: the patch's substring-with-qualifier-proximity-scan correctly catches the operator's qualifier text WITHOUT requiring the operator to change anything - the discipline is built into the grader, not into operator hygiene. Lesson: the cost-baseline regex ALSO catches the operator's HEDGE text mentioning ZERO_COST_CONTROL_BASELINE as a "treat as if absent" statement - that's a soft-false-positive (the operator was hedging, not asserting), but the discipline is downgrade-only so the false-positive just LOWERS the grade; promotion is never falsely raised. In this case the H3a-verify already confirmed the code IS zero-cost, so the flag is also independently justified - the soft-false-positive coincidentally produced the right answer. Lesson: HBP-with-warning-labels is a much more useful signal than FRC-no-warnings. It says: "this candidate is salvageable but you need to address X, Y, Z before promotion." That's exactly what a deep-extraction-and-promotion pipeline needs to keep humans honest.

- 2026-05-20 (Regime Intelligence Phase 4J v1 market mode classifier):
  Built a 4-mode transparent rule-based classifier. It correctly
  assigns 2022->bear_contraction, 2023->bull_recovery,
  2024->bull_recovery, AND the mode-vs-selector-outcome consistency
  call is True for all 3 windows. This is the cleanest empirical
  realization possible of the Phase 4I "mode-conditional selector"
  diagnostic prediction.
  Lessons:
  (1) Threshold priority order matters more than the thresholds
  themselves. The bear/shock conflict in 2022 (DD 67%, vol 64%, annual
  -65% all trigger) had to be resolved deterministically. I chose
  bear > shock because the playbook differs (RSI/defensive vs
  flat/defensive-only), and the 2022 observed data shows RSI was the
  winning family - so the bear playbook is the right operator advice.
  Locking this priority into the tool early (rather than letting the
  caller pick) prevents future reviewers from accidentally inverting
  the priority and getting a "shock playbook" recommendation for a
  bear window.
  (2) Three-window consistency is impressive but not validating.
  HIGH-coupling features by definition cannot escape the mechanical
  co-movement critique. The classifier sees annual_return,
  max_drawdown, vol, etc. - all functions of BTCUSDT closes - and
  predicts modes that align with selector outcomes that were
  themselves computed from the same closes. "Of course it agrees."
  The right reading is: the v1 prototype confirms the threshold rule
  set is INTERNALLY consistent and the priority order makes sense.
  It does NOT confirm the classifier has predictive value.
  (3) Naming the playbooks "descriptive labels only" rather than e.g.
  "go long basket on bull_recovery" was load-bearing. The forbidden-
  phrase test (no buy/sell/short/long/trade signal) caught me before
  the report shipped. The pattern "descriptive label + rationale
  string" is the safe template for any future selector layer that
  needs to communicate operator recommendations - never use trade-
  action verbs in the report text.
  (4) HIGH/LOW coupling distinction is a permanent design axis for
  all future research in this layer. Every new feature added to any
  classifier or selector must be tagged "coupling" before it's added.
  A mix of HIGH and LOW coupling features can be useful; pure HIGH
  coupling is research artifact only.
  (5) When tests caught the "no forbidden source substrings" overly-
  strict pattern (which matched the docstring's own "no broker / no
  telegram / no scheduler" non-goals declarations), the right fix was
  to align with the existing codebase pattern: check forbidden
  substrings in IMPORT NAMES, not in raw source text. Phase 4H-a's
  test had already established this pattern. Lesson: when starting a
  new tool, read the most recent sibling test FIRST and copy the AST-
  scan structure verbatim rather than reinventing.

- 2026-05-20 (Regime Intelligence Phase 4K v1 historical window expansion - the v1 thresholds are over-fit):
  Ran the Phase 4J classifier on 2020/2021/2022/2023/2024 and got
  bear / bear / bear / bull / bull. The 2022/2023/2024 trio matches.
  The 2020 and 2021 classifications are clearly wrong against
  obvious historical context: BTC returned +301% in 2020 and +61%
  in 2021 with 35%+ bull-confident-day shares in both, yet the
  classifier sends both to bear_contraction. The mechanism: both
  years had mid-year drawdowns above the 45% bear-DD trigger
  (March 2020 COVID crash ~54%, May/July 2021 crash ~53%), AND the
  priority order routes bear before bull is even checked. The bear
  rule fires on DD alone with no direction conditioning, so any
  bull-trend-with-deep-drawdown year gets miscategorized.
  Lessons:
  (1) Phase 4K's value was diagnostic, not validating. The
  expansion test caught the over-fit BEFORE any v2 work added
  coupling-reduced features. If we had skipped this step and gone
  straight to v2 with ETHUSDT/SOLUSDT features, the v2 would
  inherit the same broken taxonomy - every "high-DD volatile bull"
  year in ETH/SOL would also get tagged bear_contraction. The
  Phase 4J recommended-order "do (3) first, then (1) only if (3)
  confirms threshold stability" was the correct call.
  (2) Direction conditioning is load-bearing in any drawdown-based
  classifier. A 50% drawdown inside a +300% year is meaningfully
  different from a 50% drawdown inside a -65% year. The current v1
  bear rule conflates them; v2/v3 must condition the DD trigger on
  return direction (e.g. "bear_contraction requires DD>45% AND
  annual<0%" instead of "DD>45% OR annual<-20%").
  (3) The taxonomy itself is incomplete. There is no mode for
  "volatile bullish expansion" (high return + deep DD + high vol +
  bull-dominant regime share) which is what 2020 and 2021 actually
  were. A 5-mode v2 with `volatile_bull_expansion` (or renaming
  `volatility_shock` to subsume both bull-shock and bear-shock
  with direction-conditional playbooks) is the design redirect.
  (4) Over-fitting to 3 windows produced a classifier that LOOKED
  internally consistent (3-for-3 mode_vs_selector_outcome=True in
  Phase 4J) but failed the moment we expanded to 5 windows. This
  is a useful reminder that "internal consistency" with the design
  set is not validation. The 3 windows were necessary but not
  sufficient.
  (5) The 2020/2021 misclassifications also failed quietly: the
  secondary_flags field correctly noted "shock_also/volatility_
  above_threshold" was firing, which is a useful diagnostic
  breadcrumb. Keeping that field in any v2 redesign is worth doing.

## 2026-05-20 - Public-summary candidates cannot pass the H4 hold gate by design

**Lesson**: Even after the H3a patch surfaced 5 new code-quality
advisory labels (METHODOLOGY_NOT_FOUND, ZERO_COST_CONTROL_BASELINE,
SAME_BAR_CLOSE_FILL, FIXED_SHARE_SIZING_PRIMITIVE, UNPINNED_DATASET),
the universal hold gate (entry+exit+stop+sizing must all be POSITIVELY
EXPLICIT) is what actually blocks public-summary batches. The 5
advisory labels matter only after the hold gate is passed; they cannot
*cause* a hold by themselves on a public-summary input because the
gate is already closed upstream.

**How to apply**: When sourcing a new operator batch, do not just fill
the advisory fields (cost_baseline_status, methodology_quality_flag,
etc.) - that is necessary but not sufficient. Each candidate must also
carry POSITIVELY-EXPLICIT entry_rule + exit_rule (or exit_or_invalidation
alias) + stop_rule + sizing_rule. If any of those four is "unknown" or
"requires inspection", the candidate will hold every time, regardless
of how many advisory flags are filled.

- 2026-05-20 (Regime Intelligence Phase 4L v2 threshold redesign):
  The Phase 4K 2020/2021 misclassification is fixed via 3 surgical
  changes: (a) bear rule is now direction-conditional (annual < 0
  required for the DD/bear_conf branches to fire); (b) a new mode
  volatile_bull_expansion captures the high-return + deep-DD + bull-
  confident-share character that 2020 and 2021 actually were; (c)
  priority order routes shock UNDER volatile_bull so a positive-
  direction year with high vol doesn't fall through to the
  "defensive_throttle" playbook. 5/5 windows now match obvious
  historical context.
  Lessons:
  (1) When v1 thresholds over-fit to the design set, the fix is to
  add direction conditioning, not to tune thresholds. The v1 had a
  STRUCTURAL flaw: the bear rule fired on damage proxies (DD,
  bear_confident_share) without checking which direction the year
  actually went. Adding a precondition (annual < 0) was load-bearing;
  any number of threshold tweaks to "DD > X" without direction
  conditioning would have failed similarly.
  (2) Adding a fifth mode was the right call. The 2020/2021
  character is genuinely a distinct market mode - high return AND
  high vol AND high DD AND bull-dominant regime share - and trying
  to squeeze it into either bull_recovery (would have required
  loosening the DD ceiling and losing the distinction from clean
  bull years) or volatility_shock (wrong playbook for a +301%
  return year) would have been a category error. The new mode
  preserves the existing 4 modes' meanings and adds the missing
  one.
  (3) Test renaming was useful documentation. The v1 test
  test_bull_recovery_blocked_by_high_drawdown asserted bear; v2
  renamed it to test_strong_positive_return_with_high_drawdown_is_
  volatile_bull and now asserts volatile_bull. The rename
  documents the behaviour change in the test name itself - a
  future reader sees the old behaviour and the new behaviour
  back-to-back in git blame instead of having to reconstruct what
  changed.
  (4) Phase 4K -> Phase 4L was the textbook test-driven redirect.
  Phase 4K's value was diagnostic: it exposed the over-fit
  cheaply before any v2 build invested in coupling-reduced
  features. Phase 4L surgically fixed the diagnosed problem in the
  same module, same tool, same test file. Cost: ~150 LOC delta,
  +6 tests, no new files. If Phase 4K had been skipped and we'd
  gone straight to a coupling-reduction v2 build with the broken
  taxonomy, the v2 would have inherited the over-fit and would
  have been much more expensive to walk back.
  (5) Preservation of the v1 behaviour on 2022/2023/2024 was the
  acceptance criterion. The v2 had to not just fix 2020/2021 but
  also leave the correctly-classified windows alone. Specifically:
  2022 still has the extreme_negative_branch firing (annual < -20%
  branch survives unchanged) PLUS the new direction-conditional
  branch also fires (annual < 0 AND DD > 45%, annual < 0 AND
  bear_conf > 25%) - so the bear rule is now BROADER for negative
  years and STRICTER for positive years. That asymmetry is the
  whole point.

## 2026-05-20 - "NOT_FOUND_IN_REPO" is safer than hedged language

**Lesson**: When pasting operator evidence about a missing field, the
literal string "NOT_FOUND_IN_REPO" is grader-safe; hedged language
like "OOS planned" or "walk-forward TBD" or "unknown from pasted
summary" is grader-dangerous. The M4R1 v2 POST_H3A_R01 rule scans
within 80 chars of positive methodology substrings ("out-of-sample",
"walk-forward", etc.) for negative-qualifier vocabulary (18 terms
including "unknown", "TBD", "planned", "absent", "not specified").
A hit downgrades FRC -> HBP - which is correct behaviour for the
krishnaa03 false-positive pattern but punishes any honest "we haven't
verified yet" text near the wrong substrings.

**How to apply**: In operator-pasted text where a methodology element
is absent, write the literal string "NOT_FOUND_IN_REPO" without any
positive methodology substring nearby. Do NOT pre-fill
methodology_evidence with positive-near-negative text. The honest
absence is recorded; the candidate lands at HOLD via the hold gate
(correct outcome), not at HBP via a misleading near-FRC base grade.
This is also why batch_003 forbids hedged language - it eliminates the
trap upstream of the grader.

- 2026-05-20 (Regime Intelligence Phase 4M-a feasibility study - 2020/2021 generation blocked):
  Feasibility study found two hard blockers that prevent immediate
  Phase 4M-a generation: (1) the external BTCUSD_daily.csv at the
  generator's required path starts at 2021-01-01, so there is no
  pre-2021 BTC OHLCV data for strategy indicator warmup, and (2)
  Auth-9 covers 2022/2023/2024 only - a new explicit authorization
  is required for any 2020/2021 batch. Both blockers are
  independent; either one alone is sufficient to stop generation.
  Lessons:
  (1) Feasibility studies are cheap, save expensive mistakes.
  Spending ~30 minutes reading the existing runner + checking the
  external CSV's first date + checking the candidates/packs state
  files revealed two structural blockers before any code was
  authored or any generation kicked off. If the operator had said
  "go run Phase 4M-a", we would have either:
  - Tried to run the existing runner with patched WINDOWS and hit
  a CSV bounds error or produced silently-broken warmup-biased
  numbers;
  - Authored a new runner and discovered the data gap halfway
  through testing it;
  - Modified candidates.json + packs.json with entries that would
  have had to be manually rolled back.
  The READ-ONLY default for SPARTA_BRAIN systems pays off here -
  the feasibility study answered the question without touching
  anything that needs unwinding.
  (2) External data dependency is a hidden coupling.
  The v2_batch_003_runner reads CSVs from
  C:\SPARTA_RESEARCH_LAB\regime_detection_exp_v2\data\raw\ which
  is OUTSIDE the SPARTA_BRAIN repo. Locally-staged frozen CSVs
  in data/frozen_regime_inputs/ are NOT the same files (different
  columns, different SHA, different date coverage). Any future
  research that needs to run strategy_lab backtests has to
  respect this external-data dependency. A useful checklist for
  any future feasibility study is: (a) where does the tool read
  data from? (b) does that data cover the required window? (c)
  does the column layout match what the tool's loader expects?
  (d) is the SHA gate going to fail? Phase 4M-a hit all four.
  (3) The IS-OOS asymmetry is its own design constraint.
  Phase 4L's classifier comparison wants 2020/2021 backtests
  produced the SAME WAY as 2022/2023/2024 so the results are
  comparable. The existing runner uses expanding-IS with
  is_start=2021-01-01 for ALL three windows. There is no clean
  IS pattern that fits 2020/2021 without either (a) shorter IS
  windows (methodological change) or (b) shifting the IS start
  back to 2017/2018 (data dependency above). Either way, the
  resulting Phase 4M-a numbers would be METHODOLOGICALLY
  different from the 2022-2024 numbers - which undermines the
  validation premise. The fix would require operator approval
  of an IS-design change PLUS new data; the cheap-validation
  framing of Phase 4M-a doesn't survive this constraint.
  (4) When a feasibility study blocks the original plan, the
  follow-up should be PHASED, not abandoned. Phase 4M-b
  (ETHUSDT/SOLUSDT coupling-reduction) is a different research
  question (does the classifier stay stable across BTC/ETH/SOL?)
  but it's a useful adjacent test that uses already-staged
  resources and addresses the bigger v2 critique (HIGH-coupling
  features only). The branching of plans here - 4M-a blocked,
  4M-b available - is a healthy pattern.

- 2026-05-20 (Regime Intelligence Phase 4M-a second pass - claim correction + 2021 verdict flipped):
  The previous Phase 4M-a feasibility report (20260520T170909Z)
  contained a factual error: it claimed the local frozen
  data/frozen_regime_inputs/btcusdt_1d_2020-01-01_2022-12-31.csv
  has only timestamp+close columns. A direct probe of the file's
  header line shows it actually has timestamp,open,high,low,close,
  volume - full OHLCV. The error came from inferring the file's
  format from how the Phase 4J/4L classifier USES the file
  (close-only) rather than from how the file is actually STORED.
  Lessons:
  (1) Never infer file contents from how a downstream consumer
  uses them. The csv_loader.py module advertises
  _OPTIONAL_OHLCV_COLS = ("open", "high", "low", "volume") which
  means the loader supports OHLCV when present - it doesn't say
  "the file doesn't have OHLCV". A 5-second header probe would
  have caught this. The previous Phase 4M-a report shipped without
  that probe and reached a wrong feasibility verdict for the
  2021 OOS window.
  (2) Always probe canonical files in a feasibility study. The
  cheap-validation framing of a feasibility study is exactly the
  context where "I assume X" should be replaced with
  "I verified X by reading 2 lines of the file." Glob output gave
  filenames but not headers; the actual confirmation required
  Get-Content -TotalCount 2 on each candidate.
  (3) Corrections in subsequent reports are valuable, not
  embarrassing. The second-pass report explicitly calls out the
  prior error in a Correction section near the top. Future
  readers (including future-me) see both the corrected verdict
  AND the prior mistake side-by-side. This is much better than
  silently shipping a corrected report and hoping nobody notices
  the inconsistency with the prior decision log.
  (4) The corrected verdict (2021 OOS feasible locally) does NOT
  unlock immediate generation - the local CSV doesn't match the
  existing runner's header/path/SHA expectations. Three
  remediation paths are documented; Path B (new sibling runner)
  has the smallest blast radius and is the recommended Phase 4M-b
  scope. The corrected feasibility study brings Phase 4M-b within
  reach but still requires operator Auth-10.
  (5) BTCUSD vs BTCUSDT proxy extension matters at this layer.
  Phase 4B-4H operator note approved the proxy at the regime CSV
  level (the regime classifier reads BTCUSDT closes and the
  strategy bar_returns are labeled BTCUSD). Phase 4M-b alpha would
  extend that proxy to the BACKTEST CSV LEVEL (the local frozen
  CSV is BTCUSDT but the strategy backtests would be labeled
  BTCUSD for downstream compatibility). The draft authorization
  prompt explicitly re-acknowledges this proxy extension - the
  operator needs to actively re-bless it; a silent assumption
  carry-over would be wrong.

## 2026-05-20 - HBP advances to deep extraction; FRC vs HBP is about Tier-1 promotability

**Lesson**: A candidate at HELD_BUT_PROMISING (HBP) advances to
READY_FOR_DEEP_EXTRACTION classification just like FINAL_REVIEW_CANDIDATE
(FRC) does. The S2E driver classifier predicate is
`advances_to_hbp_or_frc AND NOT rejected_memory_matched AND
calendar_complexity != BLOCKING_HOLD AND hold_gate_all_explicit`. HBP
satisfies all four. The difference between FRC and HBP shows up at the
NEXT GATE (Tier-1 spec authoring), not at S2E intake. HBP candidates
carry H3a advisory labels that the future Tier-1 gate will use to
refuse promotion without code-remediation attestation.

**How to apply**: Do not treat HBP as "held" in operator workflow.
Treat HBP as "advances to deep extraction WITH open quality questions".
The open questions are the warning_labels - in the S5 case,
ZERO_COST_CONTROL_BASELINE + FIXED_SHARE_SIZING_PRIMITIVE. Deep
extraction must produce code-grounded evidence to either clear or
confirm each label. After deep extraction, a Tier-1 spec authoring
gate (separate authorization, not yet built per
h4_m4r1_post_h3a_lesson_patch_build_report.future_tier1_inheritance_
contract) consumes the labels and refuses to promote candidates
carrying unresolved flags.

- 2026-05-20 (Regime Intelligence Phase 4M-b alpha v2_batch_004_volatile_bull execution):
  Phase 4M-b alpha shipped cleanly: 5 BTCUSD 2021 backtest cells
  generated, G16/G17/G18 batch gates all passed, v2_batch_003_runner
  byte-unchanged pre- and post-run, all 7 strategy module files byte-
  unchanged pre- and post-run. The runner mirrors v2_batch_003's
  structure but reads from the local frozen CSV instead of the
  external SHA-locked path.
  Lessons:
  (1) Authoring a new runner instead of editing the existing one was
  the right call. Path B (new sibling) has the lowest blast radius -
  the existing batch_003 runner stays Auth-9-locked; the new batch_004
  has its own Auth-10 scope; rollback semantics are isolated per-batch.
  Path A (stage converted CSV) would have required touching files
  outside SPARTA_BRAIN (the external SPARTA_RESEARCH_LAB tree) with
  unclear permissions and SHA-management implications. Path C (modify
  existing runner) would have invalidated the Auth-9 lock.
  (2) The pre-run / post-run SHA snapshot pattern caught nothing this
  time, but it remains the right safety net. Specifically:
  test_v2_batch_003_runner_byte_unchanged is a one-line check that
  pins the locked SHA; running it AFTER the real batch confirms no
  accidental modification. The test pattern of "pin SHA in test
  constant; assert hash matches" is reusable for any phase where a
  prior tool must stay frozen.
  (3) The 2021 BTC results have a structural pattern worth noting:
  regime_filter_overlay (SMA200 long-only filter) was strongly
  NEGATIVE (-21%) in the 2021 volatile-bull window. This is a
  property of how the SMA200 crossover gets whipsawed when the May/
  July crash takes price below SMA200 then back above. The two pure
  directional strategies (momentum_breakout +62%, atr_compression_
  expansion +43%) survived. This is exactly the "deep drawdown
  inside a bull market" pattern the volatile_bull_expansion playbook
  needs to capture - directional exposure is rewarded but SMA200-
  regime filtering specifically GETS HURT. The proposed "volatility
  throttle" descriptor in the playbook label looks more honest now -
  bare SMA200 regime filtering is not enough; the throttle would
  need to be something like ATR-bands or realized-vol scaling.
  (4) candidates.json was MISSING at pre-run (deleted earlier in the
  working tree). The new runner correctly handled this via the
  "was_missing" flag in the snapshot dict. If the runner had assumed
  the file always exists (like the existing batch_003 code does),
  pre-snapshot would have crashed on the b64encode(read_bytes())
  call. The general lesson: state-file snapshot mechanisms must
  handle the missing-file case explicitly - assuming pre-existing
  state is brittle.
  (5) The test for forbidden source substrings was too strict in
  v1 of the test file (caught the runner's own docstring's
  legitimate "strategy_lab/strategies/*.py" reference). The fix was
  to scan AST string Constants for actual writeable-file patterns
  (ends with .py / .json / .csv AND contains strategies/) rather
  than raw substring presence. This mirrors the Phase 4L test
  redesign where the forbidden-substring check was narrowed to
  import targets only - documentation text should never trip a
  safety test.

- 2026-05-20 (Regime Intelligence Phase 4N volatile_bull_expansion empirically distinct from bull_recovery):
  The 4-window evidence is now complete. Rule C placebo resistance:
  2022 bear FAILED (p=0.29, weak), 2021 volatile-bull STRONG (p=0.0060),
  2023 clean-bull STRONG (p=0.0000), 2024 clean-bull STRONG (p=0.0000).
  The volatile_bull_expansion mode passes the placebo test - BUT the
  per-strategy composition that drives the result is STRUCTURALLY
  DIFFERENT from clean-bull. This is meaningful evidence that the Phase
  4L taxonomy redesign was right to split volatile_bull out as its own
  mode, AND that the proposed playbook descriptor needs refinement.
  Lessons:
  (1) "Passes placebo" does not mean "same playbook applies".
  2021 and 2023 BOTH passed strong placebo resistance, but the family
  weights that worked are OPPOSITE: in 2023 regime_filter_overlay was
  the best individual family (+0.702), in 2021 it was the WORST
  (-0.214). The Phase 4L volatile_bull_expansion classification was
  more right than the prototype playbook label suggested. The label
  needs updating from "directional_basket_with_volatility_throttle"
  to something like "directional_basket_minus_sma_regime_with_atr_
  throttle" - removing SMA-based regime filtering and replacing the
  "throttle" wording with the actual mechanism (ATR-band).
  (2) Rule B beat Rule C in 2021 by both cum AND drawdown. Rule B
  fires only when bull+confident (36% exposure in 2021), Rule C
  rotates to RSI on non-bull-confident days (100% exposure). In
  2021, the non-bull-confident days were drawdown days, so RSI-
  default-rotation was wrong - the right move was being FLAT. In
  clean-bull (2023/2024) the non-bull-confident days were mostly
  uncertain/sideways days where RSI-default was profitable. This is
  the structural difference between the two bull modes: in volatile-
  bull, the "rotate to defensive" instinct misfires because the
  defensive family (RSI) doesn't fire enough; in clean-bull, the
  defensive family captures small gains during low-conviction days.
  (3) atr_compression_expansion is the most interesting family in
  volatile-bull. It produced +0.435 cum with vol=0.158 and DD=0.095
  in 2021 - the best risk-adjusted result of any family in any
  window we've tested. The ATR-compression-then-expansion signature
  is exactly what catches the post-crash recovery in 2021 without
  getting whipsawed by the deep-DD phase. This family should
  probably be PROMOTED to "directional" in the volatile_bull
  taxonomy (currently classified as HYBRID and excluded from
  directional baskets).
  (4) The 4-window dataset is now the strongest empirical evidence
  this research arc has produced. One window is decorative, two
  windows can be coincidence, three windows shows a pattern, FOUR
  windows shows the pattern HOLDS conditional on mode classification.
  Specifically: every cleanly bull-tagged window (volatile_bull or
  clean-bull) passed Rule C placebo, and the only bear-tagged
  window failed. This is consistent with the Phase 4L mode-
  conditional thesis.
  (5) HIGH-coupling caveat still applies, and now more clearly. The
  pattern "Rule C passes placebo in bull-tagged windows, fails in
  bear-tagged windows" could be entirely explained by mechanical co-
  movement (BTCUSDT classifier mode-tags the same windows where BTC
  strategies happen to be on the right side of the market). The 4
  windows now form a coherent dataset; the next research step is
  no longer "more windows" (which would just give more HIGH-coupling
  data points) but "low-coupling features" (Phase 4M-b beta with
  ETH/SOL coupling-reduction).

## 2026-05-20 - Template-vs-research detection: filename + location + window-length

**Lesson**: Before deep extraction, examine candidate metadata for
TEMPLATE DEMO signals. Strong indicators that a candidate is a demo
skeleton rather than a research strategy:
1. Filename prefix like "BasicTemplate" / "Sample" / "Example" /
   "HelloWorld"
2. Location in a sample/tutorial/example directory (e.g. QC's
   Algorithm.Python/, backtrader's samples/, vectorbt's examples/)
3. Very short backtest window relative to the strategy timeframe
   (e.g. 6-month window for a daily SMA 4/10 produces ~1-3 trades)
4. Fixed-N hardcoded position sizing (e.g. buy 1 contract) that
   reads like a placeholder rather than a sizing model
5. No brokerage model / no fee model / no slippage model in
   Initialize
6. No stop-loss / no risk-management / no walk-forward / no OOS
7. Filename ends in "Algorithm.py" or "_demo.py" / "_example.py"

**How to apply**: When a candidate carries 4+ of these signals, the
H3a application plan should rank `template_demo_held` as the MOST
LIKELY outcome and recommend Option C (shelve + source stronger
batch) ahead of expensive Option B (gated-live fetcher build).
Templates served their purpose as code-grounded pipeline tests but
should not consume Tier-1 spec authoring resources.

This is a sourcing-layer lesson, not a grader-layer lesson - the
batch_003 plan should be amended in future batches to include a
"is_template_demo_or_research_strategy" pre-flight check at the
operator-side sourcing step, so template candidates get rejected
before staging rather than after.

- 2026-05-20 (Regime Intelligence Phase 4O descriptor refinement):
  Phase 4O propagated the Phase 4N empirical finding into the
  classifier's playbook map without re-running any analysis. The
  volatile_bull_expansion label is now
  "atr_throttled_directional_excluding_sma_regime" which states the
  three things that actually mattered in the 2021 evidence: (a) ATR-
  throttle is the right throttle mechanism, (b) the basket is
  directional, (c) SMA-style regime filtering is explicitly
  excluded.
  Lessons:
  (1) Empirical evidence should propagate into the artifact, not stay
  in the brain memory + report layer. Phase 4N produced a clear
  per-strategy finding but Phase 4L's prototype label
  ("directional_basket_with_volatility_throttle") didn't capture
  the structural exclusion of SMA-regime-filtering or the specific
  identity of the throttle. Without Phase 4O, a future operator
  reading the classifier output would see the old label and have
  to cross-reference the Phase 4N report manually. Now the label
  itself encodes the diagnosis.
  (2) Test-the-rationale, not just the label. The new
  test_volatile_bull_playbook_rationale_cites_phase_4n_evidence
  asserts the rationale text contains the specific empirical
  citations (Rule B>Rule C, ATR best risk-adjusted, SMA whipsawed,
  RSI missed, Phase 4N source, descriptive caveat) AND verifies
  the text has no trade-action verbs. This is the safety equivalent
  of a "schema test" for natural-language documentation - if anyone
  silently rewrites the rationale, the test catches the regression.
  (3) The pattern "test asserts presence of specific evidence terms"
  is reusable. Any future phase that updates a rationale to cite
  empirical findings should add an equivalent test. This keeps the
  rationale honest: if the underlying evidence changes (e.g. Phase
  4P finds different family weights in volatile_bull), the test
  asserting "RSI mean reversion missed the move" would still pass
  on the stale rationale - but the operator-facing diff in the
  rationale would catch the inconsistency.
  (4) Phase 4O cost ~10 minutes of work. The Phase 4L initial
  taxonomy build cost ~60 minutes. The Phase 4N selector analysis
  cost ~5 minutes (re-running an existing tool). Surgical-update
  phases like 4O are the highest leverage step in the research arc -
  they convert "diagnosed but not communicated" findings into
  "diagnosed AND visible in the artifact". The cost/value ratio is
  better than running a new analysis.
  (5) The HIGH-coupling caveat remains, and the playbook label
  doesn't claim to escape it. The rationale ends with "Descriptive
  historical evidence only, not a trading recommendation" - the
  same caveat carried by all Phase 4 output. Even with refined
  per-mode labels, this layer is research-only.

## 2026-05-20 - Four template-detection lessons (L_TEMPLATE_001-004)

**Lessons** (verbatim labels for future grader / sourcing references):

- **L_TEMPLATE_001 BASICTEMPLATE_IS_NOT_RESEARCH**: QC BasicTemplate
  examples + equivalent backtrader samples/ + vectorbt examples/ are
  documentation, not research candidates. The filename prefix + repo
  location are deliberate markers; respect them.

- **L_TEMPLATE_002 TEMPLATES_ARE_INFRASTRUCTURE_NOT_STRATEGY**:
  Sample/demo algorithms are useful as INFRASTRUCTURE references
  (snippet-level patterns: continuous futures setup, sizer config,
  slippage models) but never as STRATEGY candidates. Keep them in a
  separate infra-bookmark file. Mixing the two creates category
  error.

- **L_TEMPLATE_003 PREFER_PUBLISHED_ALGORITHM_LAB_OR_RESEARCH_NOTEBOOKS**:
  Future QC sourcing should prefer Algorithm Lab published algorithms
  (backtest history + author attestation), Research/ notebooks
  (Jupyter in Lean/Research/ or Algorithm.Framework/Research/), and
  LEAN strategies that explicitly document performance methodology
  (tearsheets, OOS tables, walk-forward fold reports).

- **L_TEMPLATE_004 REQUIRE_EXPLICIT_STRATEGY_INTENT**: A research
  strategy must declare WHAT IT BELIEVES ABOUT THE MARKET. A template
  demo just declares WHAT INFRASTRUCTURE IT USES. Add a mandatory
  field "explicit_strategy_intent_statement" to the operator paste
  template; operator pastes the exact README/docstring sentence
  articulating the market belief. If no such sentence exists, write
  literal "NO_EXPLICIT_INTENT_STATEMENT_FOUND" and hard-reject at
  intake.

**How to apply** (forward): when batch_004 sourcing plan is
authorized, encode these 4 lessons as sourcing-step rejects (not
grader-step downgrades) - they should keep template demos out of the
intake JSONL entirely, not just downgrade them after S2E.

- 2026-05-20 (Regime Intelligence Phase 4P Rule E mode-specific, NOT universal):
  Rule E (the Phase 4O descriptor turned into actual selector logic)
  beats Rule C in 2021 volatile_bull (cum +1.044 vs +0.883;
  return-per-DD 8.95 vs 3.65) AND in 2024 risk-adjusted by some
  metrics, but UNDERPERFORMS Rule C in 2023/2024 clean-bull on
  cumulative return, and FAILS BADLY in 2022 bear (worst of all 6
  rules at -0.314). This is the empirical confirmation that the
  Phase 4L mode taxonomy is doing real work: different modes call
  for different rules; no single rule wins across all modes.
  Lessons:
  (1) Designed-on-evidence rules ARE in-sample for the design window.
  Rule E was DESIGNED from the Phase 4N 2021 evidence; the 2021 result
  is therefore in-sample by construction. The honest out-of-sample
  tests are 2022/2023/2024. Rule E's clean-bull underperformance vs
  Rule C is the genuine out-of-sample finding: the rule's exclusion
  of regime_filter_overlay (which HELPED in 2023 +0.702) costs
  ground. The rule's 2022 disaster is also out-of-sample - the ATR
  fallback that worked in 2021 (lowest DD individual family at 0.095)
  becomes a liability in 2022 where atr_compression_expansion had
  cum -0.577. This is the correct interpretation: Rule E captures
  what was special about 2021 but doesn't generalize beyond
  volatile_bull-style windows.
  (2) Rule E2's flat fallback creates universal survivability at the
  cost of clean-bull performance. Rule E2 was the BEST cum in 2021
  (+1.134), SURVIVED 2022 (+0.060), and was COMPETITIVE in 2023/2024
  (+0.642 / +0.827). It never wins but it never loses badly. The
  trade-off between "best in the target mode" (Rule E) and "decent
  everywhere" (Rule E2) is a useful design axis. Phase 4Q or later
  could explore mode-conditional rule selection - the classifier
  picks Rule E in volatile_bull, Rule C in clean-bull, Rule E2 in
  bear or chop - but that META-RULE would itself need placebo
  validation.
  (3) "Worst-case rule design" is informative. Rule E's 2022 result
  (-0.314 cum, -0.98 return-per-DD) is the worst of any rule in
  any window we've tested. It happened because the 50% atr
  fallback amplifies atr's bear-year losses (atr was -0.577
  individually in 2022, so 50% * -0.577 * 339 days = lots of
  damage). The fix is the Rule E2 design: replace 50% atr fallback
  with 100% flat. The cost is 2021 cum dropping from +1.044 to
  +1.134 (actually higher because flat days don't lose money in
  2021 either). So Rule E2 dominates Rule E in 2022 AND ties or
  beats it in 2021 - Rule E2 is strictly better unless the
  operator specifically wants atr exposure outside bull+confident
  days. The 2021 evidence doesn't support that preference;
  Rule E's atr-fallback design is over-engineered.
  (4) The component-active-days breakdown verified the rule is
  doing what its name says. Rule E shows regime_filter_overlay=0
  and rsi_mean_reversion=0 in all 4 windows by construction - the
  count is a sanity check that the rule isn't quietly leaking the
  excluded families. The active-day counts also revealed
  atr_compression_expansion is active EVERY DAY in 2021/2022/2024
  (in BOTH branches), which is by design (it's the throttle
  component AND the directional contributor). This concentrated
  exposure is exactly why Rule E fails in 2022 - atr being lossy
  hits the rule on every single day.
  (5) The 6-rule × 4-window 24-cell comparison table is the
  highest-information artifact this research arc has produced. It
  empirically shows that NO single rule wins across modes, which
  is the empirical content of the Phase 4L taxonomy redesign.
  Without the cross-window comparison, "different modes need
  different rules" is a theoretical claim. With this comparison,
  it's measurable.

- 2026-05-20 (Regime Intelligence Phase 4Q meta-rule comparison - cleanest aggregate result of the arc):
  4 meta-rules tested against 5 universal rules across 4 BTC windows.
  ALL 4 meta-rules beat ALL 5 universal rules on compound cumulative.
  M3 has the highest compound (+10.59); M2 has the best risk-adjusted
  (return-per-DD 86.5); M1 has the best worst-year (+0.093 because it
  keeps Rule C in bear). The Phase 4L mode-conditional thesis is
  empirically supported as a descriptive 4-window finding.
  Lessons:
  (1) "Beats universal on aggregate" is impressive but heavily
  in-sample-loaded. Rule E was designed FROM the 2021 evidence.
  Rule C was designed FROM the 2024 evidence. The meta-rules use
  Rule E (or E2, which shares the same design ancestry) in 2021
  and Rule C in 2024. Both 2021 and 2024 are IN-SAMPLE for some
  underlying component. Only 2022 and 2023 are TRULY out-of-sample
  for the meta-rule mapping. In 2022, the meta-rules either match
  Rule C (M1) or pick a lower-DD-but-also-lower-cum alternative
  (M2/M3 -> E2; M4 -> FLAT). In 2023, all meta-rules pick Rule C
  so there's no advantage. The genuine OOS finding of Phase 4Q
  is: "Rule E2 in bear reduces DD from 0.18 to 0.03 at a 0.03 cum
  cost". That's the empirical content; the +10.59 compound headline
  is mostly bookkeeping.
  (2) Compound vs average-annual is the right framing. Sequential
  compounding across 4 years gives compound 10.59, but the average
  annual return is +0.93. The +10.59 is just (1.13)(1.06)(2.27)(2.26)-1
  - the cross-year multiplication. For operator decision-making the
  per-year results matter more than the compound number. The
  per-year wins are honest: 2021 M3 wins by +0.25, 2022 ties or
  loses by a hair, 2023/2024 are identical Rule C. The compound is
  a side-effect, not the substance.
  (3) Return-per-DD ratio is more honest than compound cum for
  comparing the meta-rules to each other. M2 has 86.5, M3 has 79.2,
  M1 has 57.0, M4 has 81.2. The differences here ARE meaningful and
  do NOT depend on the in-sample/out-of-sample structure. M2 is
  the lowest-DD choice (uses E2 in bear instead of C, accepting a
  small cum cost for a large DD reduction). This is the kind of
  trade-off that survives even if the compound number is partly
  bookkeeping.
  (4) M4's FLAT-in-bear policy reveals a worst-year quirk. With
  FLAT 2022 = 0.0 cum, M4's "n_positive" drops to 3/4 because 0.0
  is not strictly positive. M4's worst-year is 0.0, which sounds
  good, but it's a quirk of the cutoff - in reality M4's bear
  performance is "neutral", not "positive". The n_positive metric
  is sensitive to the exact-zero edge case. M2/M3 with their +0.060
  cum E2-in-bear stay above zero and look 4/4 positive. The metric
  framing matters.
  (5) The mode-conditional pattern doesn't escape the HIGH-coupling
  critique. M2's 86.5 return-per-DD is impressive but still derives
  from BTCUSDT-classifier-mode + BTCUSDT-strategy-returns. The
  mechanism could be: the classifier correctly partitions the 4
  windows into modes precisely BECAUSE the strategies behave
  differently across them, which is mechanical co-movement. A
  rule-shuffling placebo (sample 500 random mode->rule mappings
  from the 6^5 = 7776 possible) would be the next-level test:
  does M3's specific mapping outperform random mappings? This is
  the Phase 4R recommended.
  (6) The research arc Phase 4L (5-mode taxonomy) -> 4O (descriptor
  refinement) -> 4P (Rule E implementation) -> 4Q (mode-conditional
  meta-rule + 4-window comparison) forms a coherent chain. Each
  phase builds on the previous and the conclusions stay honest
  about coupling + in-sample concerns. The aggregate dataset
  produced by 4Q (per-window per-rule cum/DD/exposure for 9 rules
  total across 4 windows = 36 data points) is the deepest snapshot
  this layer has produced.

- 2026-05-20 (Regime Intelligence Phase 4R meta-rule mapping placebo PASSED STRONG):
  The 500-trial placebo test of the M2/M3 specific mode-to-rule
  mappings against random mappings from the candidate rule pool
  produced STRONG resistance on every headline metric: M3
  compound p=0.0100 (5/500 trials matched or exceeded), M2
  return-per-DD p=0.0020 (1/498 - at the floor of the effective
  sample space), M3 ret-per-DD p=0.0060, M2 compound p=0.0260.
  This is the strongest empirical evidence the regime intelligence
  layer has produced.
  Lessons:
  (1) Specific mappings dominate random mappings even when both
  share access to the same underlying rules. The placebo pool
  included all 7 candidate rules including Rule E and E2 that
  were designed FROM the 2021 evidence - so the random trials
  that happened to pick E or E2 in volatile_bull also benefit
  from that in-sample advantage. The fact that M2/M3 still beat
  the random distribution at p<=0.01 means the SPECIFIC choice
  of E or E2 in volatile_bull AND C in bull_recovery AND E2/C in
  bear is doing more than just "luck in picking E/E2 for 2021".
  The combination matters.
  (2) The placebo p-value floor is informative. With 7^3 = 343
  distinct outcomes for the 3 fired modes, the minimum p-value
  achievable on 500 trials is 1/498 = 0.002 (one valid trial
  beats the real value). M2's p=0.0020 is AT this floor. This
  means M2 is the unique-or-near-unique top mapping in the
  evaluated space. The placebo doesn't have power to distinguish
  M2 from "an extremely rare random match" at this sample size -
  but neither does it need to: the meaningful question is "is
  M2 a top-5% mapping" and the answer is yes by a wide margin.
  (3) Caching the per-rule per-window returns is THE design
  pattern for this kind of placebo. precompute_per_window_per_rule
  runs each rule on each window ONCE (5 strategies x 4 windows x
  7 candidate rules = 140 rule applications). Then 500 placebo
  trials are O(500 * 4 * lookup) = effectively free. Without
  caching, 500 trials would require 500 * 4 * 7 = 14,000 rule
  applications, each involving file I/O and indicator
  recomputation. The cache made the test ~100x faster while
  staying byte-identical to a non-cached version.
  (4) Cross-check p-values matter. The headline p-values are M3
  compound (0.010) and M2 ret-per-DD (0.002). But we ALSO
  reported M3 ret-per-DD (0.006) and M2 compound (0.026). All
  four are strong. If only one of the four were strong and the
  other three were weak, that would suggest cherry-picking. The
  uniform strength across all four cross-checks is meaningful
  evidence that the meta-rule edge is robust to which metric
  you pick.
  (5) The HIGH-coupling caveat survives this placebo. The
  placebo tests "is this specific mapping better than random
  mappings on this dataset?", NOT "is this mapping picking
  signal that exists out-of-sample?". The strong p-value is
  consistent with the BTCUSDT classifier + BTCUSDT strategy-
  returns dataset being internally coherent in a way that
  rewards specific rule choices. It does NOT prove the
  classification is picking up information that transfers to
  cross-asset (ETH/SOL) or to future BTC windows. The next
  research step (4M-b beta or similar) must address this
  through cross-asset feature inclusion, NOT through more
  same-asset placebos.
  (6) The 4-phase chain Phase 4L (taxonomy) -> 4O (descriptor
  refinement) -> 4P (Rule E implementation) -> 4Q (M1-M4
  mappings) -> 4R (mapping placebo) is now a complete loop. Each
  phase's claim was tested by the next phase. The taxonomy was
  empirically supported. The descriptor was confirmed by per-
  strategy evidence. The new rule was implemented and tested
  against universals. The mapping was tested against random
  mappings. All steps survived their respective empirical
  tests. The research arc closes with a measurable, audit-
  trail-complete result that respects the HIGH-coupling caveat.

- 2026-05-20 (Regime Intelligence Phase 4S cross-asset confirmation - meta-rule edge survives):
  All 4 BTC modes were CONFIRMED by ETH+SOL majority. No mode changes
  from BTC-only to cross-asset. Cross-asset meta-rule aggregate
  results are byte-identical to Phase 4Q (M3 compound +10.59, M2
  ret-per-DD 86.5, etc.). Cross-asset placebo p-values are also
  unchanged (M3 0.0100 STRONG, M2 0.0020 STRONG). The Phase 4Q/4R
  edge SURVIVED cross-asset confirmation - the strongest empirical
  result of the entire research arc.
  Lessons:
  (1) Cross-asset confirmation gave SAME numbers as BTC-only,
  which is itself meaningful. The hypothesis "BTC strategy returns
  + BTC classifier mode = mechanical co-movement" predicted that
  adding ETH+SOL confirmation would either (a) confirm same modes
  (because correlated assets agree) and produce SAME results, OR
  (b) disagree on some modes and trigger mixed_cross_asset
  fallback, REDUCING the meta-rule compound. We saw (a). That's
  consistent with two stories: either BTC modes ARE the right
  mode (and ETH+SOL agree because they're in the same regime) OR
  BTC/ETH/SOL are so correlated that we cannot distinguish
  "agreement reflects reality" from "agreement reflects co-
  movement". The placebo strength is identical to Phase 4R - we
  did not strengthen the signal, but we did establish a NECESSARY
  condition (no cross-asset disagreement) that all 4 windows pass.
  (2) Conservative fallback logic was the right design choice.
  The Mixed_cross_asset case never fired in our 4-window sample,
  but the test_run_cross_asset_pipeline_disagreement_triggers_mixed
  synthetic test confirmed that when BTC disagrees with ETH+SOL
  majority, the meta-rule correctly falls back to E2 (or FLAT for
  M4). The fallback is conservative but doesn't damage the
  observed BTC-only edge because in our actual data BTC never
  disagreed with cross-asset majority.
  (3) Cross-asset agreement DOES reduce but DOES NOT eliminate
  HIGH-coupling risk. BTC/ETH/SOL were all in volatile_bull in
  2021, all bear in 2022, all bull-mode in 2023/2024. This is
  partly because they're correlated assets (BTC dominance, ETH/
  SOL beta to BTC) and partly because they share the same broad
  market cycles. A genuinely independent feature would be
  something with structurally different drivers - e.g. macro
  rates, on-chain network metrics, futures funding rates from a
  non-spot venue. The next research step (Phase 4T or beyond) is
  to add one of these and re-run.
  (4) The 4S placebo result (M2 ret-per-DD 1/499) is at the
  effective sample-space floor again (just like Phase 4R 1/498).
  Adding mixed_cross_asset to the sampled modes increased the
  effective space slightly (7^4 instead of 7^3) but with only
  500 trials we still hit the floor. To increase p-value
  resolution we'd need either (a) more trials at fixed effective
  modes, OR (b) more truly-distinct modes that fire across more
  windows. (a) gains us log-factor at constant compute cost; (b)
  requires more BTC windows in different modes. Neither is
  achievable cheaply.
  (5) Per-strategy independence verification matters. The cross-
  asset classifier reads ETH/SOL CSVs but the strategy backtests
  remain BTC-only. This is the right architectural choice -
  changing the traded substrate would require new strategy
  backtests on ETH/SOL (which we don't have). Keeping ETH/SOL as
  read-only confirmation signals preserves the entire Phase 4P
  backtest layer unchanged.
  (6) The full 7-phase chain Phase 4L (taxonomy) -> 4O (descriptor
  refinement) -> 4P (Rule E implementation) -> 4Q (M1-M4 mappings)
  -> 4R (mapping placebo) -> 4S (cross-asset confirmation +
  survival test) is now empirically closed. Each phase made a
  claim and the next phase tested or strengthened it. The arc
  closes with a result that is: (a) empirically strong on within-
  sample data; (b) survives cross-asset agreement requirement;
  (c) explicitly bounded by the HIGH-coupling caveat; (d) auditable
  end-to-end via the report chain. This is the most complete
  research artifact this project has produced.

- 2026-05-20 (Regime Intelligence Phase 4T-a DXY design-only feasibility study):
  Inspection-only phase produced two key findings: (1) no DXY/macro
  data exists locally; (2) existing tools/stage_frozen_regime_csv.py
  is fully reusable for DXY ingestion - no new staging tool needs
  to be authored.
  Lessons:
  (1) Pre-build inspection is the cheapest unblocking step. If
  Phase 4T-a had been skipped in favor of writing a DXY ingestion
  tool first, the build would have duplicated work (the existing
  staging utility already handles any timestamp+OHLCV CSV). The
  feasibility study took ~10 minutes of read-only search + report
  authoring, and saved the cost of (a) duplicating the staging
  pipeline, (b) re-justifying the path-bounded write boundary
  that the existing tool already enforces, (c) re-running AST
  safety scans for a new tool. The lesson is general: any new
  research feature that needs operator-staged data should first
  check whether the existing staging utility handles the new
  shape. In this case it does, because the utility was authored
  generically over timestamp+OHLCV.
  (2) Architectural separation pays off. The Phase 4T DXY design
  preserves the layer separation that was built across the prior
  arc: Phase 4L = mode taxonomy (within-asset), Phase 4S = cross-
  crypto confirmation, Phase 4T = macro pressure FLAGS only.
  DXY is added without changing the existing cross-asset mode
  determination - it just attaches flags. This means Phase 4T-b
  is additive (doesn't break Phase 4Q/4R/4S existing reports)
  and easier to back out if the macro feature produces no useful
  signal.
  (3) The 3-flag design is deliberately conservative. The flags
  DXY_risk_on_supportive / DXY_risk_off_warning / DXY_macro_
  conflict are descriptive labels, not selectors. The flags do
  not change which rule the meta-rule picks. This conservative
  start means Phase 4T-b cannot make the situation worse than
  Phase 4S - the worst case is "DXY flags add noise that doesn't
  affect p-values". An aggressive design (DXY votes on mode) would
  have a higher chance of breaking the existing edge by introducing
  bad signal. Save aggression for Phase 4T-c if the conservative
  4T-b shows the flags are informative.
  (4) Calendar-alignment is the one genuine open question. FX is
  5-day/week; crypto is 24x7. The Phase 4T-a report documents this
  as an explicit Phase 4T-b decision (forward-fill vs sparse-join)
  rather than silently picking one. This is honest in two ways:
  (a) it acknowledges the design has not been fully specified yet,
  and (b) it makes the operator aware that the choice will affect
  the downstream feature values. Forward-fill is the simpler
  default and probably the right call - it matches how crypto
  trading desks typically handle FX inputs - but documenting the
  choice keeps the audit trail complete.
  (5) Operator-staged-CSV is the right ingestion path. The Phase
  4T-a recommendation explicitly avoids authoring a new network-
  fetch tool. Reasons: (a) the existing fetch tools are Binance-
  specific and don't generalize to FX sources; (b) authoring a
  new network-fetch tool would expand the safety surface for a
  one-time data load; (c) the existing stage_frozen_regime_csv.py
  utility handles operator-provided files perfectly and is already
  test-locked. The cost-vs-risk tradeoff strongly favors manual
  staging for a one-shot research data ingestion like DXY.

## 2026-05-20 - Operator H3a advisory pre-flags vs grader label attachment

**Lesson**: Operator pre-flagging an H3a advisory field (e.g.
methodology_quality_flag=METHODOLOGY_NOT_FOUND, sizing_quality=
PRIMITIVE_FIXED_CONTRACT) does NOT automatically attach the
corresponding warning label. The M4R1 v2 prechecks have their own
internal evidence requirements:

- methodology_qualifier_precheck attaches METHODOLOGY_NOT_FOUND only
  if status == NEGATIVE_QUALIFIED (positive-near-negative substring
  in methodology_evidence text). Honest neutral text like
  'NOT_FOUND_IN_REPO' is NOT negative-qualified, so the label
  correctly does not attach.
- sizing_quality_precheck attaches FIXED_SHARE_SIZING_PRIMITIVE only
  if status == PRIMITIVE_FIXED_SHARE. The operator-friendly variant
  'PRIMITIVE_FIXED_CONTRACT' is NOT recognized as equivalent. Also,
  the pattern match on code_evidence_sizing requires the canonical
  buy(symbol, N) pattern; MarketOrder(symbol, -1) short-syntax does
  not match.

**How to apply**: The operator's pre-flag values communicate intent
but the grader's precheck decides whether the label attaches based
on its own evidence. This is intentional (defense in depth: the
operator's claim must be corroborated by the actual code) but means:
- If operator wants the label to attach, they may need to either
  (a) write methodology_evidence with positive-near-negative wording
  (NOT recommended - that triggers POST_H3A_R01 false-positive trap)
  or (b) ensure code_evidence_sizing literally matches buy(symbol, N).
- A future grader patch could (a) recognize operator pre-flag values
  as direct label-attach signals when evidence_text is neutral, and
  (b) recognize sizing_quality enum aliases like FIXED_CONTRACT.

This is a sourcing-vs-grader handshake issue. Recorded as feedback
for a future M4R1 v3 patch authorization. Until then, operator pre-
flags are advisory metadata - the canonical S2 record carries them
into deep extraction even if the warning_labels list omits them.

- 2026-05-20 (Regime Intelligence Phase 4T-b DXY/FRED macro features - honest negative finding on actionability):
  DXY added cleanly as low-coupling confirmation feature. The flag
  semantically fires in 2022 and 2024 (the two windows where macro
  and crypto disagreed). BUT the naive exploratory M5 (downgrade
  rule on conflict) underperforms M2/M3 by ~3 compound. So the
  DXY signal is REAL but the naive defensive USE of it is NOT.
  Lessons:
  (1) "Signal informative" and "signal actionable as defensive
  trigger" are different questions. The DXY macro_conflict flag
  correctly identifies macro-crypto disagreement. But "disagreement"
  does not mean "downgrade exposure" - in 2024 the crypto market
