  ignored DXY's risk-off warning AND continued to rally. M5's
  downgrade C->E2 in 2024 cost ~+0.43 cum for protection that
  never paid off. The honest reading: macro_conflict is a
  DESCRIPTIVE warning label; turning it into a defensive rule
  requires more evidence than 1 conflict-and-realized-drawdown
  observation.
  (2) DXY did NOT predict M2/M3's worst drawdowns. Both M2 and M3
  worst per-window DD = 2021 (volatile_bull). 2021 had DXY label
  = neutral (DXY was modestly up but not extreme). So the macro
  feature does NOT catch the within-crypto volatile-bull drawdown
  pathology. This is consistent with the Phase 4L volatile_bull
  story: the May/July 2021 crash was a crypto-specific event,
  not a macro-driven one. DXY is not the right tool for catching
  intra-crypto regime-switch drawdowns.
  (3) FRED DTWEXBGS proxy was correctly labeled. The DXY_PROXY_
  FRED_DTWEXBGS label keeps downstream consumers aware that
  this is NOT the exact ICE DXY EUR/JPY/GBP/CAD/CHF/SEK fixed-
  weight basket. The two indices move similarly in major trends
  but differ in detail (DTWEXBGS is trade-weighted and includes
  CNY/MXN/CAD weights; ICE DXY is fixed). For research-only
  descriptive purposes the proxy is fine; for any operational
  use, this would need to be a documented limitation.
  (4) FX trading calendar interacts with crypto in a non-obvious
  way. DXY has ~252 bars/year (5/week, no weekends); crypto has
  365 (24x7). The compute_dxy_features_for_window's "60d return"
  is actually 60 trading days back = ~84 calendar days. The
  3%/5% thresholds were chosen with this in mind - a 60-trading-
  day +3% USD move is substantial. Documented as a limitation
  in the report. A future Phase 4U could test whether the
  thresholds scale to crypto's 365-day calendar (i.e., what
  WOULD have been the equivalent 60-calendar-day threshold for
  FX).
  (5) The architectural separation (Phase 4L within-asset, Phase
  4S cross-crypto, Phase 4T-b macro flags only) paid off here.
  Adding DXY did not require changing any prior tool. The
  result is byte-additive: M2/M3 reference results are identical
  to Phase 4Q/4S because DXY does not vote. This means Phase
  4T-b cannot WORSEN the existing edge - the worst case is just
  "DXY adds no actionable information" which is exactly what M5
  showed. The next research step (Phase 4U) can iterate on the
  macro USE of the signal without re-litigating the within-crypto
  layer.
  (6) The cleanest empirical finding of Phase 4T-b is the 4-year
  DXY-conflict pattern itself: 2021 neutral / 2022 conflict /
  2023 supportive / 2024 conflict. That maps to real macro
  context: 2021 USD was steady, 2022 USD weakened into year-end
  (Fed pause talk), 2023 USD fell (recession fears, BTC rallied),
  2024 USD strengthened (rates higher for longer). The signal
  TRACKS reality even if its naive defensive use doesn't add
  alpha. The proper Phase 4U test would be: does DXY conflict
  PREDICT subsequent crypto drawdowns (out-of-sample), or just
  describe co-incident macro state? With only 4 windows this is
  unanswerable.

- 2026-05-20 (Regime Intelligence Phase 4W master closeout - research arc 4E->4T-b empirically closed):
  17-phase research chain (Phase 4E through Phase 4W) produced a
  research-grade candidate framework for mode-conditional rule
  selection. Strongest result: M3 compound +10.59 with mapping
  placebo p=0.0100; M2 return-per-DD 86.5 with p=0.0020;
  cross-asset (BTC+ETH+SOL) confirms 4/4 windows; DXY context
  integrates byte-additive. NOT proof of future predictive
  utility - NOT execution-ready. Worth preserving as research
  artifact. Closeout report at SPARTA_REGIME_INTELLIGENCE_PHASE4
  _CLOSEOUT_20260520T200954Z.{json,md}.
  Lessons:
  (1) Honest closeouts matter as much as the work they describe.
  The Phase 4W report does NOT claim "we found alpha"; it claims
  "we found strong within-sample placebo resistance for a
  mode-conditional framework in a specific 2021-2024 BTC+ETH+
  SOL+DXY dataset, with explicit limitations including in-sample
  structure and no 2025 OOS data." The careful framing protects
  future operators (including future-me) from misreading the
  research as a deployable system. The closeout's two-line
  "strongest claim" wording was rewritten three times to keep
  it honest.
  (2) The 12-section closeout template is reusable. Executive
  summary -> architecture -> mode map -> playbook map -> evidence
  timeline -> key numbers -> what failed -> strongest finding ->
  limitations -> recommended next -> final verdict -> artifact
  index. This structure forces each section to do one job. The
  "what failed" section in particular forces honesty - it's the
  section most likely to be left out if the report just summarized
  successes.
  (3) Artifact index pays dividends later. Listing every tool,
  every report stem, every strategy backtest cell, every frozen
  CSV, every brain memory entry means future-me can reconstruct
  the full research arc without re-reading every phase. If anyone
  ever asks "what evidence supports the volatile_bull_expansion
  playbook" - the artifact index points at Phase 4N report stem
  + the 5 batch_004 cells + the regime_intelligence/4P comparison
  table.
  (4) "Stop / archive" should be the RECOMMENDED DEFAULT path in
  every closeout. Tempting to spell out exciting next steps and
  bury "ship and stop" as option C. The honest reading: most
  research arcs SHOULD stop when their within-sample evidence
  is exhausted. Resuming is justified only if (a) new data
  arrives, OR (b) the operator explicitly wants to commit
  resources. The Phase 4W report puts "stop/archive" first to
  remove the implicit bias toward continuation.
  (5) Brain memory + report = audit-complete artifact pair. The
  closeout MD/JSON is the single-document landing place; the
  brain memory entries are the chronological log; the actual
  reports under reports/regime_intelligence/ are the evidence
  trail. Together they form a research artifact that is
  reconstructible without any code execution. Future operators
  can read the closeout to understand the conclusion, the brain
  memory to follow the reasoning chain, and the per-phase reports
  to verify the numbers. No element is redundant; each plays a
  distinct role.

- 2026-05-20 (Regime Intelligence Phase 5A shadow harness design-only):
  Design-only phase produced a 12-section spec for a non-executing
  daily harness that observes market state, records theoretical
  playbook selections, and backfills realized forward returns at
  1d/3d/7d horizons via an atomic-update JSONL ledger.
  Lessons:
  (1) Design BEFORE build is the right discipline for any harness
  that touches operational surfaces. Even though this harness is
  strictly non-executing, the boundary between "records that look
  like instructions" and "records that are diagnostic only" is
  language-sensitive. The §7 forbidden-action-language safety gate
  (specific verbs the test scans for) is a substantive design
  decision that benefits from being settled BEFORE the code is
  written. If Phase 5B had been started without this spec, the
  test would likely have been written after the harness and the
  harness language would have leaked into the test scope.
  (2) Append-only-with-atomic-replace is the right ledger semantic
  for shadow validation. The selection record (day-T) is immutable
  AFTER first write; the LEDGER entry (also keyed by day-T) is
  mutable but only ever via atomic replace (write tmp + rename).
  This way no observer ever sees a partial state: either the entry
  has full 7d realized data with realized_after_available=true, or
  the partial entry with null forward fields. The dual-store
  pattern (immutable per-day record + atomic-replace ledger) means
  the original day-T selection is preserved verbatim even after
  realized data is appended, eliminating any way to retro-edit a
  selection in light of its outcome.
  (3) Sample count gates are conservative on purpose. 30/90/180
  samples is small by statistical standards, but the math here is
  "how many INDEPENDENT daily observations does the framework
  produce per year". Crypto-daily harness produces ~365 samples
  per calendar year, so 180+ samples ≈ 6 months. That's the
  shortest window across which a "regime" could fail to transition
  AND the framework could still be tested across at least one
  mode change. Tighter sample requirements would mean waiting
  longer; looser would mean drawing conclusions too early. The
  design picks the middle.
  (4) Operator-staged-data-only is conservative but correct for v1.
  Adding a fetcher would expand the safety surface for a one-time
  data ingestion. Once the harness pattern proves out and the
  operator wants weekly or daily runs, a separate Phase 5C could
  introduce a sha-locked authenticated fetcher under tight
  authorization. v1 keeps the safety boundary tight.
  (5) Design reports should make their own forbidden-language list
  explicit but inert. §7 spells out the exact words/phrases the
  test scans for - and those words appear ONLY in §7. Every other
  section of the design uses neutral language ("theoretical
  selection", "selected family", "forward return", "observation").
  The single section where the forbidden words appear is also the
  section that documents the safety-test specification, which is
  the only legitimate place to enumerate them. This pattern keeps
  the design itself a valid input to its own forbidden-language
  scan (i.e., the design report would pass the same scan it
  prescribes for harness outputs - except for §7 which is the
  meta-spec).

- 2026-05-20 (Regime Intelligence Phase 5B non-executing shadow harness):
  Built per Phase 5A design. 36 tests pass; synthetic 5-date
  dry-run demonstrated the immutable per-day record + atomic
  JSONL ledger + backfill-on-future-data + realized_after_available
  one-shot transition. All 8 safety gates enforced.
  Lessons:
  (1) The "immutable record vs mutable ledger" split is the right
  pattern for forward-validation harnesses. The day-T selection
  record is the historical artifact - it captures what we
  THOUGHT at time T, which can never be retroactively edited
  even when realized outcomes come in. The ledger entry for
  day-T is the EVALUATION artifact - it accumulates realized
  forward returns as time advances. Tests verified both
  invariants: re-running for the same date raises (immutability)
  and re-upserting the same entry is idempotent (atomic semantics).
  (2) Atomic write-tmp-then-rename is non-negotiable for a ledger
  that may be observed mid-update. os.replace() on POSIX and
  Win32 alike provides atomicity guarantees that "open, write,
  close" does not. The pattern - write to NamedTemporaryFile
  next to the target, then os.replace() - is generalizable to
  any append-only-with-occasional-rewrite store.
  (3) Bare "long" and "short" must NOT be in the forbidden-word
  list. They have too many non-trading meanings ("long-term",
  "short-cut", "as long as", "shortfall"). The harness's
  FORBIDDEN_ACTION_PATTERNS catches "go long" / "go short" but
  not bare "long" / "short" - and a test asserts BOTH the
  positive catch (bare "buy"/"sell" caught) AND the negative
  exemption (bare "long"/"short" pass). The negative test
  documents the deliberate design choice.
  (4) The theoretical_return v1 proxy is the right scope for the
  initial harness. Mapping "selected_rule = Rule C" to "active"
  vs "FLAT" gives us a MODE-TIMING test (does the framework
  correctly call active-vs-flat days?). Family-mix within active
  basket would require continuous per-day strategy bar_returns
  which we don't have outside Phase 4 backtest windows. The
  docstring + docs/ both call out this limitation explicitly so
  future operators don't mis-read the metrics as a strategy-mix
  test.
  (5) Default meta-rule = M3 (best Phase 4R compound). The harness
  could default to M2 (best ret-per-DD) instead - either is
  defensible. M3 has slightly higher compound, M2 has slightly
  lower DD. Default M3 reflects the "this is research, max
  compound is the primary signal" framing. Operators can flip
  via --meta-rule.
  (6) The "no-look-ahead" property is an INVARIANT, not a runtime
  check. The harness uses compute_features_from_rows with
  window_lo and window_hi - both supplied by the caller from
  data_as_of_date. Future bars (timestamp > data_as_of_date)
  are NEVER read into the window. A test confirms the API
  contract (a record built for data_as_of=2023-12-01 should be
  unchanged whether the CSV ends 2023-12-01 or 2024-02-01). The
  invariant is enforced by construction.
  (7) Single CLI binary with 9 flags is more maintainable than
  multiple scripts. --backfill-ledger-only is a useful
  separate mode (operator can re-backfill nightly without
  re-classifying), but the same module handles it. --dry-run
  is essential for sanity-checking BEFORE the first real write,
  and a test asserts dry-run writes nothing.


## 2026-05-20 - Phase 5C + 5E lessons

- **Self-conflict in safety scanners**: the Phase 5B forbidden-action
  regex catches the substring "trade signal", so an early Phase 5C
  disclaimer reading "NOT a trade signal" was itself flagged as
  forbidden language. Lesson: when a tool's own outputs are
  scanned for the same forbidden tokens it imports, never use the
  exact forbidden phrase in disclaimers - reword to "informational
  only; NOT execution-ready" or similar. Apply the same care to
  test assertions that read the tool's outputs.

- **AST-tests vs substring-tests for safety scanners**: a naive
  substring test like `assert "review_queue" not in src` will
  false-fail on the safety scanner's OWN forbidden-token list.
  Lesson: strip `FORBIDDEN_* = (...)` blocks before doing
  substring scans, OR prefer AST-level checks that examine
  Import/ImportFrom nodes and call sites only. The Phase 5E ops
  tests use both approaches.

- **Replay isolation pattern**: `replay_<UTC>[_tag]/` subfolders
  under `shadow_validation/` keep replays from ever clobbering the
  live forward-shadow root. Tests assert that the live root's
  pre-existing marker file is byte-unchanged after a replay run.
  This pattern generalizes to any future "what-if" tool that
  shares a root with a live data stream.

- **Dashboard-without-execution discipline**: the Phase 5E template
  uses HTML buttons + a small inline JS fetch() to toggle a
  PAUSED.flag sentinel - and ONLY a sentinel. No button on the
  page can place an order, modify a strategy, mutate the
  review_queue, send a Telegram message, or start a scheduler.
  Tests enforce this both on the rendered page and via AST/
  substring checks on the tool source. Lesson: it's safe to add
  read-only diagnostic surfaces to an active operator dashboard
  as long as every test fence enforces "no execution surface" on
  both the backend and the rendered HTML.


## 2026-05-20 - Phase 5F lesson

- **pytest collection pollutes `sys.modules` across test files.** A
  runtime safety scan (`assert no httpx in sys.modules`) is fragile
  if any sibling test file does a module-level
  `from fastapi.testclient import TestClient` - pytest's collection
  pass imports all test modules before running any test, so by the
  time the safety test runs, httpx is already in `sys.modules`. Fix:
  push test-only HTTP-client imports INSIDE each test function. The
  contract being asserted (the production runtime does not load
  httpx) stays honest; only the test-helper import location moves.
  This generalizes: any "runtime never loads X" scan needs sibling
  tests to lazy-import X to avoid false fails under multi-file
  pytest runs.


## 2026-05-20 - Phase 5G lessons

- **PowerShell scripts need their own "active-code vs comment-prose"
  test pattern.** The header docstrings on the runner/installer/
  uninstaller legitimately enumerate the surfaces they do NOT touch
  ("no broker, no Telegram, ..."). A naive substring scan trips on
  the prose. Fix: strip PowerShell `#` line comments before the
  forbidden-token scan; assert the *active code* avoids the tokens.
  Same pattern we used for Python module docstrings - generalize.

- **Static analysis of scheduled-task installers is genuinely
  enforceable**. Tests can pin: exact task name string, exact
  trigger time, exact runtime cap, exact runner-script filename,
  and that the action targets only one script. This converts what
  used to be a code-review concern ("did the installer accidentally
  also register a second task or point somewhere else?") into a
  pytest assertion that runs every CI step.

- **schtasks /Query is a safe read-only surface for dashboards on
  Windows.** The Phase 5G ops layer queries the scheduled task
  state via subprocess.run([schtasks.exe, /Query, /TN, name, /V])
  with a 10-second timeout, treats missing/failed/return-non-zero
  as installed=false, and exposes the parsed fields to the dashboard.
  No PowerShell scheduling primitives need to be imported into
  Python, and no admin elevation is required for read-only query.

- **Pinning outbound URLs by constant + asserting in tests works.**
  The Phase 5G FRED URL is one literal string. _assert_fred_dxy_url()
  refuses any other URL. test_tool_has_no_other_outbound_urls walks
  the entire tool source and asserts every http(s):// token belongs
  to a small allowed set. This converts URL surface area into a
  bounded, testable claim instead of a code-review hope.


## 2026-05-20 - Phase 5I lesson

- **Two sys.modules entries for one module**. A test file that
  inserts `tools/` onto sys.path and imports `regime_shadow_ops`
  gets a sys.modules key `regime_shadow_ops`. A consumer that
  imports it as `from tools import regime_shadow_ops` gets the key
  `tools.regime_shadow_ops`. These are different module objects.
  monkeypatch on one does NOT propagate to the other. When a test
  needs to patch a constant that an HTTP route reads at request
  time, patch BOTH module entries (or refactor to a single import
  style). General lesson: when test code and production code import
  the same file via different mechanisms, write the test to assert
  the patch took effect on the same object the production path
  reads.

- **Hard-coded argv is the strongest input safety contract for a
  dashboard button**. The Phase 5I launcher accepts no parameter
  that could be interpolated into the subprocess command. The
  launcher's signature is the contract; `inspect.signature` in a
  test asserts the parameter set is the expected closed set. This
  is dramatically stronger than "we don't pass user input to
  subprocess" - it's "the function literally cannot accept user
  input to pass."

- **Stale lock detection prevents permanent jam**. RUNNING.lock with
  a 35-minute staleness threshold (slightly above the 30-minute
  process runtime cap) means a crash that leaves the lock behind
  doesn't permanently block subsequent manual runs. The dashboard
  still surfaces the lock so the operator sees it, but the next
  click after the staleness window succeeds.


## 2026-05-20 - Phase 5K lesson

- **Infrastructure is not evidence**. After ten phases of building
  the shadow validator (harness, replay, dashboard, scheduler,
  manual trigger, merge layer, 204 tests), the underlying signal
  layer's predictive value is still unproven. The risk of an
  unbounded research project is that "the dashboard is nice" silently
  substitutes for "the signal is real." A pre-committed decision
  contract with explicit numeric thresholds at Day 7 / 30 / 60 / 90
  / 180 and a finite verdict enum (including ARCHIVE_RESEARCH and
  REDESIGN_SIGNAL outcomes) is the antidote. Without an exit clause,
  any project tends to grow infrastructure faster than evidence.

- **Verdict enum belongs in the contract, not in the analyst's
  head**. Five named outcomes (CONTINUE, FIX_INFRASTRUCTURE,
  REDESIGN_SIGNAL, ARCHIVE_RESEARCH, READY_FOR_PAPER_SIMULATION_DESIGN)
  with explicit rules per checkpoint mean each future review converts
  to a mechanical application of thresholds to data, not a fresh
  judgement call. The asymmetric override policy (operator may
  override toward MORE caution, never less) closes the obvious loop
  back to "let it run another month."


## 2026-05-25 - s7 D1 cross-asset Donchian ETF-proxy terminal lesson (parked at REJECT_FAST)

- **Hypothesis validated, mechanic did not survive cost-stress**. The
  s7 D1 cross-asset Donchian ETF-proxy chain (Step 02b through Step
  07; 14 sealed commits; final park commit `a5ac092`) parked at
  `REJECT_FAST` because K12 fired through DR2 (S2/S3 cost-stress
  materially degraded vs S1) AND DR3 (S0 positive while at least one
  stressed tier turned non-positive) on the cost-stress matrix. The
  S1 baseline showed `+$589.59` net PnL on `$100,000` with
  `trade_curve_max_drawdown_pct = 69.10%` and only 37 closed trades;
  USO carried the portfolio while SPY/TLT/GLD were net negative. A
  technically-positive baseline that does not survive realistic
  transaction-cost stress is the canonical false-edge signature; the
  spec section 14 K12 fail-fast was designed for exactly this case.

- **The diversification idea worked; the edge did not**.
  `effective_independent_bets = 3.56` and `avg_pairwise_dependence =
  0.041` on the four-symbol daily-return matrix over the in-sample
  window. The load-bearing hypothesis from spec section 1 H1 (cross-
  family diversification with avg pairwise correlation < 0.5 produces
  genuinely independent bets across equity-index / bonds / metals /
  energy proxies) is empirically validated. This is a real positive
  finding from the s2-s7 research arc and is inheritable by future
  research tracks even though the strategy that wrapped it failed.

- **Do not inherit the mechanic; do not loosen thresholds**. Per spec
  section 14 threshold-lock invariant, the parked Faith / no-filter
  Donchian-55 entry / Donchian-20 exit / pyramid +0.5N / 4 unit max
  / 2N stop mechanic at locked cost-stress on this SPY/TLT/GLD/USO
  universe CANNOT be revived under a lower bar; tightening requires
  a fresh `_revN_` spec. Future research may carry the cross-asset
  diversification idea forward but must NOT rebadge s7 D1, must NOT
  relax the K-criteria, and must NOT silently re-introduce filters
  removed by the locked `Filter: NONE` constraint. The 14-commit
  chain (`efdc307` ... `a5ac092`) is preserved as the audit trail;
  the park report at `reports/s7_d1_cross_asset_donchian_yfinance_proxy_park_report.json`
  (sha256 `5eb4309096a8377943799b7cc164cbbb13a86f327a813520255d0fa3b3e00263`,
  seal `e7f3fce5239d18f7cff78ddda81dde060b6842c54ddb1fdba95bfdcd584eb326`)
  is the canonical terminal record. Do not rescue this spec; build
  the next research track on top of the validated diversification
  finding with a different edge family or a fresh sealed parameterization.


## 2026-05-25 · Four B006_001 framework lessons formalized (record-only, do not change sealed verdict)

- **LESSON_B006_001_001 — favorable verdict ≠ live-ready.**
  A `REQUEST_FULL_PREREGISTRATION_REVIEW` outcome is the *strongest favorable*
  value in the closed enum, but it is still NOT a `PASS`, NOT live-ready, NOT
  profit-proof, NOT a candidate promotion, NOT an FRC grant, and does NOT
  unlock the 6-gate live block. The "favorable" label denotes only that the
  next legitimate step is a preregistration review — itself a human-judgment
  paperwork process — not an operational status change.

- **LESSON_B006_001_002 — warmup-guard pattern is mandatory.**
  QC engine emitted a `OnWarmupFinished` / order-submit warning during the
  warmup window. The warning was code-quality (auto-resolved before any
  eligible rebalance touched live order flow) but exposes that future runners
  must defensively no-op all sizing/submit logic until `IsWarmingUp` clears.
  Future successor B006_NNN candidates MUST include a runner-level warmup
  guard before any order or sizing path.

- **LESSON_B006_001_003 — latent fail-closed evaluation must remain
  observability-only, never verdict-driving (when off-precedence by design).**
  DR6 latent-fired during B006_001 but is not in B006_001's verdict precedence
  chain (same as the entire B005_NNN family). The framework's invariant —
  latent rules are informational, not verdict-driving when explicitly off
  precedence — held. Successor candidates MUST continue to publish the latent
  evaluation table without letting it short-circuit verdict logic.

- **LESSON_B006_001_004 — sealed-spec preconditions MUST be runner-enforced.**
  Sealed-spec §13 listed conditions C3 and C4 (leverage-cap-bound-rate
  preconditions) but the sealed runner did not enforce them — it only emitted
  the rate as a metric. The leverage-cap-bound rate exceeded the C4 textual
  precondition, but because the runner did not enforce, no fail-closed rule
  fired and the verdict logic still produced a favorable outcome. This is a
  load-bearing successor lesson: every textual precondition in a future
  sealed-spec MUST have a runner-side enforcement and a fail-closed rule that
  fires when violated. Successor B006_002 must close this gap.


## 2026-05-26 - LESSON_S10_D1_001 - Metadata-surface failures do not generalize to availability verdicts

- **Lesson:** A `BentoClientError` (or any provider-specific error class) returned by the **metadata/symbology** surface MUST NOT be treated as a "symbol unavailable" verdict. The right surface for the availability question is the **timeseries** surface (`get_range` per-day probe with record-counting).
- **Why:** Different Databento API surfaces fail-closed differently. The metadata surface can fail on auth, rate, schema-detection, or symbology-not-resolved-yet errors that do not imply the underlying timeseries is empty or absent. The S10-D1 probe demonstrated this: all 18 timeseries probes returned HTTP `OK`, even for cells where the metadata surface previously erred.
- **How to apply:** Before declaring a symbol unavailable in a candidate spec, run a small-grid timeseries availability probe (3-6 dates) with record-counting. Zero counts paired with an unresolved-symbol warning are strong negative evidence; non-zero counts on any date are strong positive evidence. Mixed results require further probing at boundary dates.
- **Anti-pattern:** Accepting a single error from the metadata surface as evidence the symbol is "not on the vendor" — this would cause the framework to skip otherwise-valid candidate universes.

## 2026-05-26 - LESSON_S10_D1_002 - The 1380-minute canonical day for CME Globex futures ohlcv-1m

- **Lesson:** For continuous CME Globex futures probed on the `ohlcv-1m` schema, a record count of exactly `1380` represents the canonical full-session day (23 hours of trading × 60 minutes). Counts of 1,296-1,375 are normal partial / shortened-session days. Counts of 244-990 are typically launch-day-adjacent, low-adoption-era, or extended-holiday days. A count of `0` paired with an unresolved-symbol warning is strong evidence the contract did not exist on that date.
- **Why:** CME Globex includes a 60-minute daily settlement maintenance window; the trading session is 23 hours not 24. This makes 1,380 (not 1,440) the natural ceiling for one trading day's ohlcv-1m record count.
- **How to apply:** When interpreting availability-probe output for any CME futures dataset, calibrate against the 1,380 ceiling rather than 1,440. Anything significantly below 1,380 deserves a brief look at whether the day was a known shortened session (year-end, day-after-holiday, etc.) before concluding the symbol was unavailable.

## 2026-05-26 - s9 RSI-2 mean-reversion ETF-proxy terminal lesson (parked at PARKED_SAFE_BUT_NOT_MONEY_PROVEN)

- **Edge was negative even at zero cost; this is a different failure mode
  from s7 D1**. The s9 cross-asset RSI-2 mean-reversion ETF-proxy chain
  (10 sealed commits from `530b545` selection plan to `9cf2f56` park
  report) parked at `PARKED_SAFE_BUT_NOT_MONEY_PROVEN` because K1
  (Sharpe proxy per trade < 0) AND K2 (expectancy per trade <= 0) fired
  at S1 baseline. The cost-stress matrix degraded smoothly across
  S0/S1/S2/S3 with DR2/DR3/DR5 ALL CLEAR; K12 did NOT fire. The
  smoking-gun S0 row showed `-$1,211.03` net PnL over 414 closed
  trades at zero slippage and zero commission. The edge itself is
  negative; costs only make a negative edge more negative. This is
  STRUCTURALLY DISTINCT from s7 D1 ETF-proxy's `REJECT_FAST` via K12
  (cost-stress with a positive S0 edge that costs destroyed). The
  s9 simulator solved every other failure mode of s7 D1: trade
  density (414 vs 37 trades; clears K9 by 4x), drawdown (1.64% vs
  cap-binding catastrophe; clears K4 by 30x), cost-stress robustness
  (DRs all clear), safety attestations (C1-C8 all True), and
  provenance (K8 zero drift across 11 pinned upstream artifacts).
  Per-trade win rate 53.14% is above absolute breakeven but below
  the P/L-implied breakeven of 62.44%, leaving a -9.30 percentage-
  point WR gap (A5 fails); the strategy reverts often enough to win
  the majority of trades but the few losing trades are large enough
  to erase the cumulative edge. All four markets show the same shape,
  so the failure is structural across the universe, not market-
  specific.

- **The diversification finding is now validated by two structurally
  orthogonal mechanics; it is a universe property, not a mechanic
  artifact**. The s9 aggregator independently measured
  `effective_independent_bets = 3.56` and `avg_pairwise_dependence =
  0.041` on the same four-symbol daily-return matrix over the same
  in-sample window, matching the s7 D1 measurement to within
  rounding. This convergence across one trend-following mechanic
  (s7 D1 Donchian) and one mean-reversion mechanic (s9 RSI-2) is
  unusually strong evidence that the diversification structure on
  SPY/TLT/GLD/USO 2014-2022 is a property of the universe, not an
  artifact of either mechanic. It is the one finding that survives
  both parks and that any future research on this universe can
  legitimately rely on. K10 and A7 clear comfortably under both
  mechanics. The diversification idea is permanently inheritable;
  the strategies that wrapped it are permanently parked.

- **Do not continue simple canonical mechanics on this exact
  universe without a fresh first-principles reason**. Two
  structurally orthogonal mechanics empirically falsified on the
  same ETF universe at canonical parameters with realistic ETF-proxy
  cost assumptions over 2014-2022 is a strong universe-level
  finding. The two failure modes point at different things: s7
  trend-following had a positive S0 edge that cost-stress destroyed
  (motivates lower-cost-regime research); s9 mean-reversion had a
  negative S0 edge that no cost regime could rescue (motivates a
  different mechanic family or different universe). Future research
  should NOT continue rebadging simple canonical mechanics on this
  exact universe under a slightly different parameterization; that
  is parameter-shopping and would invite K7 silent-introduction
  risk. Future research MAY: (a) carry the diversification finding
  forward to a different mechanic family (rotation, carry,
  vol-of-vol) on the same universe; (b) carry the same mechanics to
  a different universe (international ETFs, sector ETFs, single
  names); (c) revisit the cost-structure assumption (futures, prop,
  options) with a fresh `_revN_` spec and first-principles
  justification; (d) accept the universe-level finding and pivot
  entirely. Any rebadged s9 or s7 variant on this exact universe
  requires a fresh sealed Tier-N spec with explicit first-principles
  reasoning, not threshold relaxation. The 10-commit s9 chain
  (`530b545` ... `9cf2f56`) is preserved as the audit trail; the
  park report at `reports/s9_cross_asset_mean_reversion_rsi2_yfinance_proxy_park_report.json`
  (sha256 `cefa80e7b4c2e73f66d5ff4aad37bcb329247e7f16691f92b6d3b748666542c3`,
  seal `026595ed2b1d81589d5a946bd0fd897e182736b75c15ce8a0c3e9f0d585b94c7`)
  is the canonical terminal record. The s9 IS decision memo at
  `reports/s9_cross_asset_mean_reversion_rsi2_is_decision_memo.json`
  (sha256 `30da17f4d9f04a07a36e5300df38f75ae111ba2c9dc15efa5f73ea7c660d8e71`,
  seal `0d7b3561c16cf7cb4892f0233c7445342036c566da52fc54462f4915a0744729`)
  is the corroborating evidence memo. Trading remains PAUSED; live
  remains BLOCKED_AT_6_GATES; FRC never granted; advisory label
  permanent `DIAGNOSTIC_ONLY_NOT_LIVE_GRADE`.


## 2026-05-26 - LESSON_B006_002_001 - Runner-enforced spec preconditions actually fire when calibrated correctly

- **Lesson:** A sealed-spec textual precondition is only as strong as its runner-side enforcement. B006_002 added DR11 specifically to enforce the C4 leverage-cap-bound-rate precondition that B006_001's archival memo §6 Observation 3 identified as un-enforced. The B006_002 QC backtest produced `leverage_cap_bound_rate = 15.625% > 10% threshold` and DR11 fired REJECT_FAST as designed.
- **Why:** The B006_001 run on the same strategy produced the same leverage-cap-bound rate (~15.6%) but received `REQUEST_FULL_PREREGISTRATION_REVIEW` because no rule fired. B006_002 demonstrates that wiring textual preconditions into actual fail-closed rules at the right precedence position (here, position 3) structurally pre-empts favorable verdicts when the precondition is violated.
- **How to apply:** Every future sealed-spec precondition MUST have (a) a named DR rule, (b) a threshold constant, (c) a severity label, (d) a precedence-chain position, and (e) an emitted compact-summary field. Metric-only emission (B006_001's pattern) is not enforcement.

## 2026-05-26 - LESSON_B006_002_002 - Favorable economic numbers do not change a fail-closed verdict by design

- **Lesson:** The B006_002 backtest produced IS Sharpe +0.9467, OOS Sharpe +0.7197, OOS annualized return +8.43%, OOS max drawdown -25.14%, with all four cost-stress OOS Sharpes >0.5 (would have satisfied C5+ in §15). The verdict was still REJECT_FAST because DR11 fired upstream at precedence position 3.
- **Why:** Numbers and risk-profile are orthogonal. A strategy with attractive returns AND a violated risk-profile precondition is still rejected because the strategy as sealed does NOT match the strategy actually exhibited. Treating it any other way re-opens the LESSON_B006_001_004 gap that B006_002 was built to close.
- **How to apply:** Never treat favorable Sharpe / return / drawdown numbers as overriding a fail-closed rule fire. The framework's discipline depends on rules pre-empting verdict-favorable outcomes when their preconditions are violated - if you weaken this, the framework's risk-profile guarantees evaporate.

## 2026-05-28 - LESSON_S14_D1_001 - Cross-sector diversification can improve A7/K10 without creating edge

- **Lesson:** The s14-d1-cross-sector AAPL/JPM/XOM basket achieved its diversification target at P6 IS - A7 effective-independent-bets = 2.09 and K10 avg pairwise correlation = 0.4529 (AAPL-JPM 0.45, AAPL-XOM 0.32, JPM-XOM 0.59), both inside the SEAL's expected bands (A7 ~2.3-2.8, K10 0.30-0.50), with no single-symbol K6 concentration - yet the candidate still FAILED P6 IS with FAIL_SAFETY (net -$13,754.96 on $100k).
- **Why:** Basket construction and signal edge are orthogonal failure axes. Spreading capital across low-correlation sectors reduces variance concentration but cannot manufacture positive expectancy where the underlying mechanic has none. A7/K10 in-band confirmed the basket worked as designed; it did not and cannot rescue a negative-edge entry/exit rule.
- **How to apply:** Treat A7/K10/K6 as necessary-but-not-sufficient diagnostics. Never read "diversification thesis held" as evidence a candidate is viable, and never count a clean A7/K10 as a partial pass. Evaluate per-trade edge (K1 sharpe_proxy, K2 expectancy) independently of basket-quality metrics.

## 2026-05-28 - LESSON_S14_D1_002 - RSI(3) with 2N ATR stop produced >50% win rate but negative expectancy

- **Lesson:** s14-d1-cross-sector RSI(3) bi-directional mean-reversion (thresholds 15/55/85/45) with a 2N Wilder-ATR(14) hard stop produced a 54.31% win rate over 348 IS trades yet net-NEGATIVE expectancy (-$39.53/trade; sharpe_proxy/trade -0.1119), failing K1 and K2 at S1 baseline. The loss was predominantly gross (~$1.4k of the ~$13.7k loss was costs), so it was a real edge failure, not cost erosion.
- **Why:** A hard 2N stop is structurally adversarial to the mean-reversion premise (price reverts): winners exit early when RSI crosses the 55/45 mid-band (small gains) while losers run to the full 2N stop distance (larger losses). A win rate >50% with profit/loss ratio <1 yields negative expectancy. High hit-rate masked a money-losing payoff geometry.
- **How to apply:** For mean-reversion entries, a win rate >50% is NOT evidence of edge - always inspect expectancy and profit/loss ratio together. If the stop can be hit before the reversion completes, a high-hit-rate signal becomes a net loser.

## 2026-05-28 - LESSON_S14_D1_003 - Mean-reversion candidates need exit/stop design tested from first principles, not just the entry signal

- **Lesson:** The s14-d1-cross-sector SEAL locked the entry (RSI(3) thresholds) and the exit/stop (2N ATR + RSI mid-band) together; only at P6 IS did it become clear the exit/stop - not the entry - was the binding failure. Because parameters are locked post-SEAL (no in-candidate iteration), the candidate was terminal at FAIL_SAFETY with no recourse, after the full PLAN->SEAL->BUILD->P4->P6 cost.
- **Why:** Entry signals get the design attention, but for mean-reversion the exit/stop geometry dominates expectancy. Locking an untested stop structure alongside the entry means a stop/entry mismatch can only be discovered after expensive downstream phases, with no permitted fix within the sealed candidate.
- **How to apply:** When SEALing a future mean-reversion candidate, justify the exit/stop design from first principles BEFORE locking - does the stop distance respect the expected reversion horizon? - ideally with a cheap pre-SEAL feasibility check. A Path B follow-on candidate should vary the exit/stop structure (time-based or volatility-scaled exit, wider stop), not just re-tune entry thresholds.
